Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
10 min
Iqrar vs. Hibah and Wasiyyah: Beneficiary Becomes Heir
Explains validity of iqrar, invalidity of hibah and wasiyyah when beneficiary becomes heir after marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an iqrar (acknowledgment of debt) made during marad al-mawt remains valid even if the recipient later becomes an heir, while a hibah or wasiyyah to the same person becomes invalid.

Core Idea
Iqrar is binding at its time; hibah and wasiyyah are judged at death.

A dying man makes an iqrar (debt acknowledgment), hibah (gift), and wasiyyah (bequest) to a foreign woman, then marries her, making her an heir. What happens to each act? This lesson dissects the Hanafi ruling and its rationale, focusing on the critical distinction between acts that are 'mudaf ila al-mawt' (added to death) and those that are not. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying inheritance and transaction laws in death illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts and their initial validity
At the time of making, all three acts (iqrar, hibah, wasiyyah) are valid because the woman is a foreigner (ajnabiyyah) and there is no legal impediment.
Iqrar is an acknowledgment of debt; hibah is an immediate gift; wasiyyah is a bequest contingent on death.
2
Note the change: marriage makes her an heir
After the man marries the woman, she becomes an heir at his death. This changes the ruling for hibah and wasiyyah but not for iqrar.
Heirship is determined at the moment of death, not at the time of the act.
3
Apply the rule: for iqrar, look at time of making; for hibah and wasiyyah, look at death
Iqrar is 'ghayr mudaf ila al-mawt' – not added to death – so its validity is judged at the time it was made. Since she was ajnabiyyah then, iqrar remains valid from the entire estate. Hibah and wasiyyah are considered 'mudaf ila al-mawt' in ruling during marad al-mawt, so their validity depends on the beneficiary's status at death. Since she is now an heir, they become invalid.
The author calls iqrar 'mulzim bi nafsihi' (binding in itself).
4
Understand the proof: hibah in marad al-mawt is like wasiyyah
The passage provides a rational proof: hibah during death illness is treated like wasiyyah because its effect is determined at death – it is invalidated by overwhelming debt and limited to one-third of the estate. Therefore, the same rule applies: no hibah or wasiyyah to an heir.
Arabic text: 'والهبة وان كانت منجزة صورة فهى كالمضاف الى ما بعد الموت حكما'

تشریح اور مذکورہ عورت کے لئے مریض کا یہ بھی باطل ہے اگر چہ ہبہ کے اندر صورۃ تجھیز ہے موت کی جانب ہبہ کی اضافت نہیں ہے لیکن مریض کے مرض الموت کے ہبہ کو وصیت کا درجہ دیا گیا ہے لہذا یوں سمجھیں گے کہ بہبہ کا حکم استحکام و تقر رموت کے وقت ہوگا کیونکہ موت سے پہلے ہبہ میں استحکام نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر موت سے پہلے میت پر اتنا قرض نکل آیا جو اس کے تر کہ کومحیط و مستغرق ہے تو ہبہ باطل ہو جائے گا لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ حکما وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے اور اگر ہبہ کرنے والے پر قرض نہ ہو تو اس کا بہیہ ایک تہائی مال سے معتبر ہوگا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مرض الموت کا ہبہ وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے۔
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 19. A woman is a stranger at the time of making the iqrar. For this reason, the iqrar will be valid from the entire wealth, and due to debt the iqrar will not become invalid, whether the iqrar is in a state of health or in a state of illness, but indeed the latter will be postponed from the former, contrary to wasiyyah, because wasiyyah is an offer at the time of death and the woman is an heir at the time of death, and a bequest to an heir is not valid. Explanation: Zaid made an iqrar of debt for a foreign woman, or bequeathed something to her, or gifted something to her, and Zaid is afflicted with death illness. So all three things were permissible because there is no impediment. But if Zaid then married this foreign woman, then the wasiyyah and hibah become invalid, and the iqrar is valid. Why? Because iqrar is not added to death; the author called it 'mulzim bi nafsihi'. So when it is not added to death, then the state at death is not considered, rather the state at the time of iqrar is considered, and at the time of iqrar she is a foreign woman. Therefore this iqrar will be valid and will be considered from the entire wealth. Then if Zaid has other debts, even then this iqrar will not become invalid, whether the iqrar is in a state of health or in a state of illness; in both cases the iqrar is valid. However, there is this difference: the debt from the state of health will be given precedence over the debt from the state of illness. In any case, the iqrar for this woman is valid. As for wasiyyah and hibah, they are not valid, because wasiyyah involves a transfer of ownership that is added to after death, whereas at the time of Zaid's death this woman is Zaid's heir, and a bequest to an heir is not valid. Reason for invalidity of the hibah of the sick person: And the hibah, even if it is immediate in form, is like that which is added to after death in ruling, because its ruling is determined at the time of death. Do you not see that it becomes invalid due to overwhelming debt, and when there is no debt it is considered from the third? Translation: And hibah, even if it is immediate in form, is like that which is added to after death in ruling, because the ruling of hibah is determined at the time of death. Do you not see that hibah becomes invalid due to overwhelming debt, and when there is no debt it is considered from the third. Explanation: And for the mentioned woman, the hibah of the sick is also invalid, even though in hibah there is immediate transfer in form, there is no addition to death in hibah, but the hibah of one in death illness is given the status of wasiyyah. Therefore it will be understood that the ruling of hibah becomes firm and established at the time of death, because before death there is no stability in hibah, because if before death a debt appears on the deceased that encompasses and overwhelms his estate, then the hibah becomes invalid. Hence it is known that it is in the status of wasiyyah in ruling. And if the one making hibah has no debt, then his hibah will be considered from one-third of the wealth. From this too it is known that the hibah of death illness is in the status of wasiyyah.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah commentary, clarifying the distinction between iqrar (confession/acknowledgment of debt) on one hand, and hibah (gift) and wasiyyah (bequest) on the other, when the beneficiary later becomes an heir. The core principle is that iqrar is a binding legal act (mulzim bi nafsihi) that is not contingent upon death; its validity is judged at the time it is made. Therefore, if at the time of iqrar the recipient is a non-heir (ajnabiyyah), the iqrar is valid and effective from the entire estate, even if she later becomes an heir through marriage. In contrast, hibah and wasiyyah made during marad al-mawt (death illness) are treated as contingent upon death: hibah is considered like wasiyyah because its effect is determined at death. Since the woman becomes an heir at death, the hibah and wasiyyah to her become invalid. The proof for treating hibah like wasiyyah is that it is annulled by overwhelming debt and is limited to one-third of the estate, both characteristics of wasiyyah. This ruling adheres to the Hanafi position that acts added to death (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt) are subject to the laws of inheritance, while acts that are not so added are judged at their time of execution.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): A binding acknowledgment of debt or obligation, not added to death (ghayr mudaf ila al-mawt). It is valid at the time it is made, regardless of later changes in the status of the beneficiary.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator, which is mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt (appended to after death). It is invalid if made to an heir unless other heirs consent.
ہبہ (hibah): A gift that is normally immediate (munajjaz) but during marad al-mawt is treated like wasiyyah in ruling, i.e., limited to one-third and subject to debts.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A life-threatening illness from which the person is expected to die; acts performed during such illness are subject to special rules resembling wasiyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the iqrar of a man in marad al-mawt to a woman who later becomes his wife remain valid, while his hibah and wasiyyah to her become invalid?
A) Because iqrar is not added to death; its validity is judged at the time it was made when she was ajnabiyyah.
B) Because iqrar is limited to one-third of the estate, so it is always valid.
C) Because the woman consented to the iqrar after marriage.
D) Because iqrar is a form of wasiyyah and thus follows the same rule.

Key Takeaway
The validity of iqrar is judged at its making; hibah and wasiyyah are judged at death.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Invalidity of Gifts and Acknowledgment to a Christian Son When He Converts Before Death
Explains invalidity of iqrar, hibah, wasiyyah when a Christian son converts before testator's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hibah, wasiyyah, and iqrar made during marad al-mawt to a Christian son who converts before death, and explain the reasoning for each.

Core Idea
When the cause of inheritance exists at the time of the act, suspicion of favoritism invalidates the act, even if the beneficiary is not yet an heir.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from Al-Hidayah: a Muslim father in terminal illness makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) of debt, a gift (hibah), or a bequest (wasiyyah) to his Christian son. If the son converts to Islam before the father's death, all three acts become invalid. The reasoning hinges on the principle of tuhmat al-ithar (suspicion of preferential treatment) and the nature of hibah and wasiyyah as contingent on death. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to identify when legal acts are overturned due to potential fraud on inheritance rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and scenario
What are the three acts performed by the father? Who is the beneficiary? What change occurs before death?
The acts: iqrar of debt, hibah, wasiyyah. Beneficiary: Christian son. Change: son converts to Islam before father's death.
2
State the ruling for each act
What is the hukm for iqrar, hibah, and wasiyyah after the son converts? Are they valid or invalid?
All three become invalid (batil).
3
Analyze hibah and wasiyyah
Why are hibah and wasiyyah invalid? Consider that they are treated as offers contingent on death, and at death the son is an heir.
In marad al-mawt, hibah is mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt; at death the son is an heir due to conversion, so bequests to an heir are invalid.
4
Analyze iqrar
Why is iqrar invalid despite being generally binding? Focus on the presence of the cause of inheritance (sonship) at the time of iqrar, which creates suspicion of favoritism.
The key: bunuwwah existed at the time of iqrar, leading to tuhmat al-ithar. Compare with the woman's case where marriage was not present.
5
Compare with the woman's case
How does this case differ from the earlier case of iqrar for a woman who later marries the testator? What principle explains the difference?
In the woman's case, the cause of inheritance (marriage) arose after iqrar, so no suspicion. Here, sonship existed from birth.

Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 16. Ruling regarding iqrar of debt, hibah, and wasiyyah by a sick person for his Christian son. The Book of Bequests. He (Muhammad) said: And when a sick person makes an iqrar of debt for his son while his son is a Christian, or makes a hibah to him, or makes a wasiyyah for him, then the son becomes Muslim before his (the father's) death, all of that becomes invalid. As for hibah and wasiyyah, because we said that he is an heir at death, and these two are offers at the time of death or after it. Translation: Muhammad said: And when a sick person made an iqrar of debt for his son while his son is a Christian, or made a hibah to him, or made a wasiyyah for him, then the son became Muslim before the death of his father, so all of this is invalid. In any case, hibah and wasiyyah are because of the reason we have stated that the son will be an heir (due to his Islam) at the time of death, and these two are offers at the time of death or after death. Explanation: A sick man has a Christian son. Now this sick Muslim man makes an iqrar of debt for this son, or makes a wasiyyah of something for him, or makes a hibah of something to him, and before the father's death, the son becomes Muslim. So now he becomes an heir, whereas in the first scenario he was not an heir. Therefore, the iqrar that was made in his favor also becomes invalid, and the wasiyyah and hibah also become invalid. In the previous case of the woman, the iqrar was valid, but here the iqrar is also invalid. The reason for the invalidity of wasiyyah and hibah is apparent: in these, the state of the contract is not considered, rather the time of death is considered, and at the time of death he is his heir, because what prevented inheritance was disbelief, and now he has become Muslim. And wasiyyah and hibah are both in one category: they involve an offer in which transfer of ownership occurs at death or after death. 'At the time' (indahu) is said from the perspective of transfer appended to the removal of legal capacity, and 'after' (ba'dahu) is said from the perspective of the estate remaining in the ownership of the deceased after death. Reason for invalidity of iqrar: And the iqrar, even though it is binding in itself, but the cause of inheritance, i.e., sonship (bunuwwah), is present at the time of iqrar, so it is considered in creating suspicion of preference. Contrary to what preceded, because the cause of inheritance, i.e., marriage, is incidental (not present at the time). So much so that if the marriage tie existed at the time of iqrar while the woman was a Christian, then she became Muslim before his death, the iqrar would not be valid because the cause existed at the time of its occurrence. Translation: And the iqrar, even though it is binding in itself, but the cause of inheritance, i.e., sonship, is established at the time of iqrar, so the cause of inheritance will be considered in creating suspicion of superiority. Contrary to the previous issue, because the cause of inheritance is marriage and it is incidental (not present at the time). So much so that if the marriage tie existed at the time of iqrar while the woman was a Christian, then she becomes Muslim before his death, the iqrar would not be valid due to the existence of the cause at the time of its occurrence. Explanation: Here the iqrar is also not valid, whereas in the woman's case the iqrar was valid. The answer is being given: Although iqrar is binding in itself, the inheritance that this son receives is not due to becoming Muslim, but its cause is sonship, and sonship existed at the time of iqrar as well. Hence a suspicion arises that the man is trying to give preference to some children over others. As for the woman's case, the iqrar there...
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Hidayah (by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) with commentary. It deals with the case of a Muslim father in marad al-mawt who makes an iqrar, hibah, or wasiyyah in favor of his Christian son. If the son converts to Islam before the father's death, all three acts become invalid. The reasoning differs for each: (1) Hibah and wasiyyah are invalid because they are considered as offers contingent upon death; at the time of death, the son is an heir (since Islam removes the impediment of disbelief), and bequests or gifts to an heir are not valid. (2) Iqrar, though generally binding, is also invalid here due to the suspicion of favoritism. The key distinction from the previous case (woman who later marries) is that in the son's case, the cause of inheritance (bunuwwah/sonship) was already present at the time of the iqrar. Since sonship existed, the father may be seen as trying to prefer this son over other children by acknowledging a debt, even if the son was a non-Muslim at the time. The suspicion (tuhmah) of preferential treatment invalidates the iqrar. In contrast, in the woman's case, the cause of inheritance (marriage) did not exist at the time of iqrar; it arose later, so no such suspicion exists, and the iqrar remains valid. The text further notes that even if a Christian wife existed at the time of iqrar and later converts, the iqrar would also be invalid if the marriage existed at the time of iqrar. This reinforces the principle: if the cause of inheritance exists at the time of the act, the act is invalid due to suspicion.

Key Terms
بنوت (bunuwwah): Sonship; the legal relationship of a son to a father, which is a cause of inheritance (sabab al-irth) in the Hanafi school.
تہمت الایثار (tuhmat al-ithar): Suspicion of preferential treatment; the idea that a person in marad al-mawt might favor some heirs over others through iqrar or gifts, invalidating the act.
سبب الارث (sabab al-irth): The cause or basis of inheritance, such as marriage (zawjiyyah), sonship (bunuwwah), etc. In this context, its existence at the time of an act creates suspicion.
مضاف الی ما بعد الموت (mudaf ila ma ba'd al-mawt): Appended to after death; a legal act whose effect is contingent upon death, like wasiyyah and, in marad al-mawt, hibah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the iqrar of a father in marad al-mawt for his Christian son invalid when the son converts to Islam before the father's death, whereas the iqrar for a woman who later becomes his wife was valid?
A) Because in the son's case, the cause of inheritance (sonship) existed at the time of iqrar, creating suspicion of favoritism; in the woman's case, marriage did not exist at that time.
B) Because the son is a closer relative than the wife.
C) Because iqrar for a non-Muslim is always invalid.
D) Because the father died before the son converted.

Key Takeaway
If the cause of inheritance exists at the time of an iqrar, hibah, or wasiyyah in marad al-mawt, and the beneficiary later becomes an heir before death, the act is invalid due to suspicion of favoritism or because the act is contingent on death.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Ruling for a Slave or Mukatab Son: Iqrar, Hiba, and Wasiyyah
Extension with a debt-based exception for iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqrar, hiba, and wasiyya for a slave or mukatab son who is freed before the father's death, and apply the condition regarding the slave's debt to determine the validity of iqrar.

Core Idea
Iqrar for a slave son is valid if he has no debt; otherwise invalid. Hiba and wasiyya are always invalid.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if a free son is freed before the father's death, any iqrar, hiba, or wasiyya made for him becomes invalid because he becomes an automatic heir. The text now extends this ruling to a son who is a slave or mukatab (a slave under contract for freedom). However, a crucial condition from Kitab al-Iqrar modifies the rule for iqrar: it depends on whether the slave has personal debt. This lesson will unpack that condition and clarify the status of hiba and wasiyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the general ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses a father making an iqrar, hiba, or wasiyya for a son who is a slave or mukatab, and the son is freed before the father's death. The initial ruling from Al-Jami' al-Saghir treats all three as invalid.
This mirrors the earlier ruling for a free son.
2
Apply the condition from Kitab al-Iqrar
Note that an exception is introduced: if the slave son has no personal debt, the iqrar is valid. If he has debt, it is invalid.
The key is whose benefit the iqrar actually serves.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the condition
If the slave has no debt, the iqrar is considered to be for the master (the father's iqrar effectively acknowledges the master's right), and the master is a stranger (ajnabi) to the father, making iqrar valid. If the slave has debt, the iqrar is for the son himself, making it invalid because the son is an heir.
The presence of debt attaches the iqrar to the son's own liability.
4
Analyze the rulings for hiba and wasiyya
Hiba and wasiyya are always invalid in this scenario. Wasiyya is invalid because it depends on the time of death, at which point the son is an heir. Hiba is generally considered like a bequest in terminal illness (marad al-mawt) and thus invalid; a minority narration that considers it valid because it is immediate is not relied upon.
The default position for hiba is that it is invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is: iqrar is valid only if the slave has no debt; otherwise invalid. Hiba and wasiyya are invalid in all cases.
This is the view presented in Al-Hidayah, citing the condition from Mabsut.

And if there is debt on him, then the iqrar is not valid, because this acknowledgment is for him, while he is his son. Commentary: The author of Al-Hidayah states that from the wording of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, it seems that the ruling for iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba in this case is the same. But in Mabsut's Kitab al-Iqrar, it is mentioned that if the slave has no debt, then the iqrar is valid, because this iqrar is not for the slave but for his master, and the master is a stranger. And if he has debt, then the iqrar is not valid, because this iqrar is for the master? No, it is for the slave, and the slave is his son, and iqrar for a son is not valid. Reason for invalidity of wasiyya and hiba for slave/mukatab: And the wasiyya is invalid due to what we mentioned, that the consideration in it is the time of death. As for hiba, it is narrated that it is valid because it is an immediate transfer while he (the son) is still a slave. But in most narrations, it is like a bequest in terminal illness, so it is not valid. Translation: And wasiyya is invalid due to the reason we already mentioned, that the consideration in wasiyya is the time of death. As for hiba, it is narrated that it is valid because it is an immediate transfer and he is a slave. And in the general narrations, it (hiba) is like a bequest in terminal illness, so it is not valid.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to a son who is a slave or mukatab (slave under contract to earn his freedom). If the father makes an iqrar, hiba, or wasiyya for such a son, and the son is freed before the father's death, then all three are invalid for the same reason: the son becomes an heir at death. However, a condition from Kitab al-Iqrar (in Mabsut) is introduced: if the slave son has no debt, then the iqrar is valid because it is actually for the master (who is a stranger), not for the son. If the slave has debt, then the iqrar is for the son (since the debt would be paid from the slave's earnings/assets), and it is invalid. The passage also notes that for a slave/mukatab, wasiyya is invalid because it depends on the time of death. For hiba, there is a narration that it is valid because it is an immediate transfer (while the son is still a slave), but the general and relied-upon narrations treat it like a bequest in terminal illness, thus invalid.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): Slave, a person owned by another, incapable of ownership.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract with his master to earn his freedom by paying a sum.
مولی (mawla): Master, the owner of the slave.
دین (dayn): Debt owed by the slave to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid, because the son becomes an heir.
B) Valid, because the iqrar is considered for the master Zaid, who is a stranger.
C) Invalid, because the son is a slave.
D) Valid, because iqrar is never invalid.

Key Takeaway
The validity of iqrar for a slave son depends on his debt status; hiba and wasiyya are always invalid due to the time-of-death consideration.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Iqrar, Wasiyya, and Hiba for a Slave or Mukatab Son
Explains validity of father's iqrar/wasiyya/hiba for slave/mukatab son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the rulings on a father's iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba for his slave or mukatab son, state the condition that validates iqrar, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on hiba in death sickness.

Core Idea
Iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba for a slave son are invalid if he becomes an heir; but iqrar is valid if no debt, and hiba is disputed.

When a father makes a legal disposition (iqrar, wasiyya, hiba) for his son who is a slave or mukatab, the validity depends on when the disposition takes effect and whether the son later becomes an heir. The Hanafi school refines this with a special condition for iqrar from al-Mabsut, and holds an internal debate about hiba in death sickness. This lesson unpacks these rules and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text states that if a father's iqrar, wasiyya, or hiba is made for a slave/mukatab son who later becomes free before the father's death, the disposition is invalid because at the time of death the son is an heir.
2
Examine the exception for iqrar
According to al-Mabsut, the iqrar is valid if the slave son has no debt at the time; if he has debt, it is invalid. Understand the reasoning: the iqrar benefits the master (stranger) when no debt, but benefits the son (heir) when there is debt.
3
Analyze wasiyya
Wasiyya is always invalid because its validity is assessed at the moment of death, and at death the son is an heir.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on hiba
One narration says hiba is valid because it is an immediate transfer (tamlik fi al-hal) and at that moment the son is a slave (non-heir). The majority (عامۃ الروایات) say hiba in death sickness is like a will, hence invalid. The relied-upon position is the majority view.
5
Compare the three dispositions
Note the key difference: iqrar has a debt-contingent exception; wasiyya is always invalid; hiba has a valid narration but the majority rule is invalidity in death sickness.

Chapter of Wills. ... (Urdu commentary) For (the iqrar) became valid because it occurred (before the change). If at the time of iqrar there is marriage and he makes iqrar, the iqrar is invalid. For example, a Christian woman is married to a Muslim; due to not being Muslim, she does not inherit from the Muslim, but if she becomes Muslim she will inherit, and the cause of inheritance is this marital tie. So if the husband made an iqrar of debt for this Christian wife and then she became Muslim, this iqrar is invalid because at the time of iqrar the cause of inheritance (marriage) existed. Ruling of iqrar, hiba, wasiyya for a slave or mukatab son. And similarly if the son was a slave or mukatab and then was freed, due to what we mentioned. Translation: And similarly if a son is a slave or mukatab and then was freed, for the same reason we have mentioned. Commentary: Similarly, if someone's son is a slave or mukatab of someone and the father made an iqrar, will, or gift for him, and then before the father's death he was freed, here also the iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba are invalid for the reason just mentioned. Condition for validity of iqrar. And it is mentioned in Kitab al-Iqrar that if he (the slave) has no debt, the iqrar is valid because he made the iqrar for his master, and the master is a stranger; but if he has debt, the iqrar is not valid because he made the iqrar for him (the slave) while he is his son. Translation: And in Mabsut's Kitab al-Iqrar it is mentioned that if he has no debt, the iqrar is valid because the one making iqrar did so for his master, and the master is a stranger; but if he has debt, the iqrar is not valid because this iqrar is for him while he is his son. Commentary: Sahib al-Hidayah states that from the text of Jami' al-Saghir it appears that the ruling for the mentioned case is the same for iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba. But in Mabsut's Kitab al-Iqrar it says that if the slave has no debt, the iqrar is valid because this iqrar is not for the slave but for his master, and the master is a stranger. And if he has debt, the iqrar is not valid because this iqrar is not for the master but for the slave, and the slave is the son of the person making iqrar, and iqrar for a son is not valid. Reason for invalidity of wasiyya and hiba for a slave and mukatab. And the wasiyya is invalid due to what we mentioned, that the consideration in it is the time of death. As for hiba, it is narrated that it is valid because it is transfer of ownership immediately, and at present he is a slave; but in the majority of narrations, hiba in death sickness is like a wasiyya, so it is not valid. Translation: And the wasiyya is invalid for the reason we mentioned, that the consideration in wasiyya is the time of death. As for hiba, it is narrated that it is valid because hiba is immediate transfer of ownership, and at present he is a slave; but in the majority of narrations, hiba in death sickness is in the position of a will, so hiba is not valid. Commentary: For a slave and mukatab, wasiyya and hiba are also invalid because in wasiyya, the time of death is considered, and at the time of death he is his heir, and a will for an heir is not permissible. Now as for hiba, there are two narrations regarding it: (1) It is valid because hiba is immediate transfer of ownership, and at present he is a slave who will not be an heir. (2) It is not valid because in death sickness it is in the position of a will, so just as the will is not valid, this is also not valid.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on al-Hidayah, deals with the validity of a father's legal dispositions (iqrar, wasiyya, hiba) towards his son who is a slave or mukatab at the time of the disposition but later becomes free. The author first explains that if a disposition was made while the son was a slave and then he becomes free before the father's death, the disposition is invalid because at the time of death (the critical moment for inheritance) the son is an heir, and a disposition for an heir is not valid. The passage then refines this with a condition from al-Mabsut regarding iqrar: if the slave has no debt, the iqrar is valid because it is effectively for the master (a stranger); if the slave has debt, the iqrar is invalid because it benefits the slave himself, who is a potential heir. For wasiyya, it is always invalid because its validity is assessed at death. For hiba, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: one narration holds it valid as immediate transfer, but the majority (عامۃ الروایات) consider hiba in death sickness to be like a will, hence invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the latter, as indicated by the phrase 'عامۃ الروایات'.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male slave owned by another person.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay for his freedom in installments.
اقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt owed to another person.
وصیت (wasiyya): A will or bequest made by a person, effective after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
ہبہ (hiba): A gift, an immediate transfer of ownership without consideration.
مولی (mawla): Master (owner) of a slave; also can mean a freed slave or client.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi narration, what is the ruling on a father's hiba to his slave son during the father's death sickness?
A) Valid, because hiba is immediate transfer.
B) Invalid, because it is treated like a will and the son becomes an heir.
C) Valid, only if the son has no debt.
D) Invalid, only if the son is a mukatab.

Key Takeaway
A father's iqrar, wasiyya, and hiba for a slave or mukatab son are generally invalid if the son becomes an heir, but iqrar has a conditional exception based on the son's debt, and hiba is disputed with the majority ruling it invalid in death sickness.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Marad al-Mawt: Definition and Hiba from Chronically Ill Persons
Defines marad al-mawt and rules on hiba from chronic cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of marad al-mawt and apply it to distinguish when a hiba from a chronically ill person is from all wealth versus limited to one-third.

Core Idea
A chronic illness is not death-sickness unless death is feared; then hiba is from one-third only.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi inheritance law: not every serious illness renders a person legally 'dying.' The author, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, gives examples of chronic conditions that, when prolonged and not feared to cause death, leave the person's full capacity to gift property. Only when the condition becomes acute and death is feared does the one-third limitation apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central definition
Find the sentence that defines marad al-mawt in the commentary. The key phrase is 'predominant fear of death' (ghalebah al-khawf). Write down the definition.
The definition is implicit in the commentary: marad al-mawt is any illness from which there is a predominant fear of death.
2
List the four chronic conditions mentioned
The text lists muq'ad (paraplegic), mafluj (paralyzed), ashal (withered limb), and maslul (consumptive). These are examples of conditions that may become prolonged.
These are not exhaustive; they illustrate the category of chronic, non-feared illnesses.
3
Apply the condition of 'prolonged and not feared'
For each condition, if it has lasted a long time and there is no longer fear of death, the person is treated as healthy. State the ruling: hiba from all wealth.
The criterion is subjective: does the person (or observers) fear death from this condition?
4
Contrast with acute phase: sahib al-firash
If the chronically ill person becomes bedridden (sahib al-firash) and death is feared, this new phase is considered a new illness (marad al-mawt). Then hiba is limited to one-third.
This is an exception: the same person can move between healthy and death-sickness status based on symptoms.

Source Text

مرض الموت کی وضاحت اور مقعد ، مفلوج، اشل مسلول کے ہبہ کا حکم
قال والمقعد والمفلوج والاشل والمسلول اذا تطاول ذلك ولم يخف منه الموت فهبته من جميع المال لانه اذا تقادم العهد صار طبعا من طباعه ولهذ لا يشتغل بالتداوى ولو صار صاحب فراش بعد ذلك فهو كمرض حادث
ترجمہ اور پانج اور فالج زدہ اور اشل (جسکے ہاتھ پاؤں شل ہو گئے ہوں ) اور مسلول (جس کو سل کا مرض ہو جس میں پھیپھڑے خراب ہو جاتے ہیں ) جب کہ یہ مرض لمبا ہو جائے اور اس سے موت کا خوف نہ رہے تو اس کا ہبہ پورے مال سے ہوگا اس لئے کہ جب عہد پرانا ہو گیا تو وہ اس کی طبیعتوں میں سے ایک طبیعت بن گئی اسی وجہ سے وہ دوا کرنے میں مشغول نہیں ہوتا اور اگر وہ اس کے بعد صاحب فراش ہو جائے تو وہ مرض جدید کے مثل ہو گا۔
تشریح جب بار بار مرض الموت کا ذکر آ رہا ہے تو یہاں سے مصنف اس کی وضاحت کرنا چاہتے ہیں، جس کا حاصل یہ کہ جس مرض سے ہلاکت کا خوف غالب ہو وہ مرض الموت ہے ورنہ نہیں چنا نچہ فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص اپاہج ہو یعنی کھڑا ہونے کی قدرت نہیں رکھتا ، اور جس کو فالج ہو گیا ہو یا کوئی عضوشل ہو گیا ہو یا سل کی بیماری ہو ، اور یہ مرض اس کو زمانہ دراز تک رہے جس سے موت کا خوف نہ رہے تو یہ مرض الموت نہ ہوگا اور اگر وہ اس حالت میں ہبہ کرتا ہے تو اس کا ہبہ پورے مال سے ہوگا کیونکہ وہ تندرست ہے۔
اس لئے کہ جب یہ بیماریاں طول اختیار کر جائیں تو وہ اس کی طبعی چیزیں بن جاتی ہیں اسی لئے آدمی ان کا علاج معالجہ بھی نہیں کرتا ۔
اور اگر وہ اس کے بعد صاحب فراش ہو جائے تو اس کو نیا مرض شمار کیا جاتا ہے۔
مرض الموت میں ہبہ کا حکم
وان وهب عند ما اصابه ذلك ومات من ايامه فهو من الثلث اذا صار صاحب فراش لانه يخاف منه الموت ولهذا يتداوى فيكون مرض الموت والله اعلم
Clarification of death sickness and the ruling on hiba from a paraplegic, paralyzed, withered, and consumptive person. He (Imam Muhammad) said: The paraplegic, the paralyzed, the one with withered limbs, and the consumptive - when this (condition) becomes prolonged and death is not feared from it, his hiba is from all of his wealth, because when time becomes old, it becomes a natural disposition of his, and therefore he does not occupy himself with treatment. And if he becomes bedridden after that, it is like a new sickness. Translation: And the paraplegic, the paralyzed, the one with withered limbs (whose hands and feet are paralyzed), and the consumptive (who has tuberculosis in which lungs deteriorate) - when this illness becomes long and there is no fear of death from it, his hiba is from all of his wealth, because when time becomes old, it becomes one of his natural dispositions, therefore he does not engage in treatment. And if he becomes bedridden after that, it is like a new sickness. Commentary: Since the mention of death sickness repeatedly occurs, the author now wishes to clarify it. The gist is that whatever sickness has a predominant fear of death is death sickness; otherwise not. So he says: If a person is paraplegic i.e., unable to stand, or has paralysis, or a limb is withered, or has tuberculosis, and this illness continues for a long time such that there is no fear of death, then it is not death sickness. And if he makes a hiba in this state, his hiba is from all of his wealth because he is healthy. Because when these illnesses become prolonged, they become part of his natural disposition, therefore a person does not even treat them. And if he becomes bedridden after that, it is considered a new sickness. Ruling of hiba in death sickness. And if he gives a hiba when that (sickness) afflicts him and he dies within days, it is from one-third if he becomes bedridden, because death is feared from it, and therefore he seeks treatment, so it is death sickness. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage clarifies the legal definition of marad al-mawt (death sickness) and its application to hiba (gift). The author first establishes the general principle: marad al-mawt is any illness from which there is a predominant fear of death ('khawf al-halakah'). Then he gives examples of chronic conditions (paraplegia, paralysis, withered limbs, tuberculosis) that, if prolonged and no longer feared to cause death, are not considered marad al-mawt. In such cases, the person is treated as healthy, and their hiba is valid from all of their wealth (not limited to one-third). However, if such a person later becomes bedridden and death is feared, that new phase is considered marad al-mawt. The final line adds that if a person is struck by such an illness and dies within days while bedridden, the hiba is from one-third because it is marad al-mawt. The commentary emphasizes that the key factor is the subjective fear of death, not the mere presence of a chronic condition.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A death-sickness: an illness from which there is a predominant fear of death, affecting one's legal capacity to dispose of property beyond one-third.
مقعد (muq'ad): A person who is paraplegic or unable to stand, permanently confined to sitting position.
مفلوج (mafluj): A person afflicted with paralysis (fālij), often half-body paralysis.
اشل (ashall): A person with a withered or shriveled limb (usually hand or foot), having lost its function.
مسلول (maslul): A person suffering from consumption (tuberculosis), a chronic lung disease.
صاحب فراش (sahib al-firash): A person who becomes bedridden, indicating an acute phase of illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a chronically ill person (e.g., with paralysis) considered not in death sickness (marad al-mawt)?
A) If the illness is prolonged and there is no fear of death.
B) If the person is bedridden.
C) If the illness is acute.
D) If the person is undergoing treatment.

Key Takeaway
A chronic illness prolonged without fear of death does not trigger marad al-mawt; hiba from such persons is from all wealth.

Recovery from Death Illness Removes One-Third Restriction
Statement of rule: recovery negates the one-third limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school considers dispositions made during a death illness as valid from full wealth if the testator recovers, and explain the rationale based on the absence of an heir's right.

Core Idea
Recovery from a death illness voids the restriction: the disposition is as if made in full health.

This lesson addresses a key rule in Hanafi inheritance law: the limitation of bequests to one-third of the estate applies only when the testator dies in that illness. If the testator recovers, the illness is legally treated as non-existent, and any bequest made during that time becomes fully valid. The following passage from Al-Hidayah articulates this principle concisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
Recognise that the act in question is a bequest (wasiyyah) made during an illness that may be considered marad al-mawt (death illness).
2
Recall the default restriction
Remember that in Hanafi law, bequests from a death illness are limited to one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent.
This restriction protects the heirs' rights.
3
Apply the exception: recovery
Apply the rule: if the testator recovers from that illness, the illness is retroactively treated as mere sickness, not death illness. The bequest is then valid from the entire estate.
The rationale: recovery shows no right of the heirs had attached to the wealth.
4
Contrast the contrary case
Consider the opposite: if the testator dies in the same illness, the one-third limit applies. This highlights that the critical factor is the outcome, not the state at the time of bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حضرت مصنف آگے ایک قاعدہ اور بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ جس مرض سے مریض شفایاب ہو گیا ہوتو وہ مرض نہیں رہا بلکہ وہ صحت کے مثل ہے، کیونکہ جب مریض اچھا ہو گیا تو اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہو گئی کہ اس کے مال کے ساتھ کسی کا حق وابستہ نہیں ہوا ہے۔
The author further states a principle: that an illness from which the patient recovers is no longer an illness, rather it is like health, because when the patient recovered, it became known that no right of anyone was attached to his wealth.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage states a key principle: the restriction of bequests to one-third of the estate applies only if the testator dies in that illness. If he recovers, the illness is considered as if it never existed, and any disposition made during that illness is deemed to have been made while healthy. Therefore, such dispositions are valid from the entire wealth, not just the one-third. This is because the right of the heirs only attaches upon death from that illness. If the person recovers, the potential right of the heirs is nullified.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): An illness from which a person dies, which restricts bequests to one-third of the estate.
شفاء (shifa'): Recovery from an illness, which removes the legal restrictions of marad al-mawt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They remain limited to one-third of the estate.
B) They are invalid because the illness is over.
C) They are valid from the full wealth as if made in health.
D) They are valid only if the testator reaffirms them after recovery.

Key Takeaway
Recovery from a death illness retroactively removes the one-third restriction, making bequests valid from the full estate.

Priority Between Muḥābāh and Itq in Marad al-Mawt
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority between muḥābāh and itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding priority between muḥābāh and itq in death illness, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In death illness, when one-third is insufficient, precedence between muḥābāh and manumission depends on chronology per Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn always prioritize manumission.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement: when a person in death illness performs both a muḥābāh (sale at undervalue) and a manumission, and the one-third of the estate cannot cover both, which transaction takes priority? The answer reveals a deeper principle about the nature of these acts as bequests and acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the condition
The passage deals with two transactions: muḥābāh (a sale undervalue) and itq (manumission), both occurring in marad al-mawt when the one-third is insufficient to fulfill both.
Note that muḥābāh and itq are among the three excepted bequests that take priority over regular bequests.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that if muḥābāh precedes itq, muḥābāh takes full priority; if itq precedes muḥābāh, they share the one-third equally.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that itq is always given priority over muḥābāh, regardless of the order in which they occurred.
4
Analyze the underlying rationale
The Sahibayn consider itq a pure act of worship with no worldly benefit, making it more deserving. Abu Hanifa focuses on the chronological execution of transactions.
This reflects a difference in prioritizing contractual effectiveness versus religious merit.
5
Determine the practical difference
If muḥābāh was done first, under Abu Hanifa the muḥābāh consumes the one-third; under the Sahibayn, itq consumes it. If itq was done first, Abu Hanifa splits equally; Sahibayn still give itq full priority.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, giving priority to itq in all cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان حابي ثم اعتق وضاق الثلث عنهما فالمحاباة اولى عند ابي حنيفة وان اعتق ثم حابى فهما سواء وقالا العتق اولى في المسألتين
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مریض نے محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا اور ثلث ان دونوں سے تنگ ہو گیا تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک محابات اولی ہے اور اگر اس نے آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی تو وہ دونوں برابر ہیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ دونوں مسئلوں میں عقیق اولی ہے۔ تشریح مرض الموت کی تمام وصایا برابر ہوتی ہیں ایک کو دوسرے پر فضیلت نہیں ہوتی لہذا تمام اصحاب الوصايا ثلث میں برابر کے شریک ہوتے ہیں یعنی اپنے اپنے حصہ کے بقد رثلث میں سب شریک ہوتے ہیں البتہ تین چیزیں ایسی ہیں جو تمام وصیتوں سے مقدم ہوتی ہیں:- 1- مرض الموت کا عشق ۲- مرض الموت کی تدبیر ۳- مرض الموت کی محابات یہ تین چیزیں دیگر وصایا سے مقدم ہوتی ہیں لہذا اگر ان تینوں میں سے کسی کے ساتھ دیگر وصایا جمع ہو جائیں تو ثلث کے اندر سے پہلے ان کو پورا کیا جائے گا اور اگر ان کو ادا کر کے ثلث میں کچھ بچ جائے تو دیگر اصحاب اوصایا کو ملے گا ورنہ کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ لیکن اگر محابات اور معتق جمع ہو جائیں تو اب کون متقدم ہوگا تو اس میں صاحبین اور امام ابوحنیفہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ عشق ہر حال میں محابات سے اولیٰ ہے، اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر پہلے مریض نے محابات کی ہو اور اس کے بعد آزاد کیا ہو تو اس صورت میں تو محابات مشق سے اولی ہے اور اگر اس نے پہلے آزاد کیا ہو اور پھر اس نے محابات کی ہو تو دونوں برابر ہیں، برابر ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثلث میں دونوں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔ اور محابات کے مقدم ہونے کا یہ مطلب یہ ہے کہ ثلث کے اندر پہلے محابات کو جاری کیا جائے گا اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو مابقی میں محق نافذ ہوگا ورنہ نہیں، اور عشق کے مقدم ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ ثلث سے پہلے محقق کو نافذ کریں گے اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو مابقی میں محابات کو جاری کریں گے ورنہ نہیں۔
He said: If he made muḥābāh then freed, and the one-third is insufficient for both, then muḥābāh is preferable according to Abu Hanifa. If he freed then made muḥābāh, then both are equal. They (Sahibayn) said: manumission is preferable in both cases. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if the patient made muḥābāh then freed, and the one-third is insufficient for both, then according to Abu Hanifa muḥābāh is preferable; if he freed then made muḥābāh, then both are equal. The Sahibayn said: manumission is preferable in both cases. Explanation: All bequests in death illness are equal; one is not given preference over another. So all legatees share equally in the one-third. However, three things are excepted which are given priority over all other bequests: (1) manumission in death illness, (2) tadbir in death illness, (3) muḥābāh in death illness. These three are given priority over other bequests. So if any of these are combined with other bequests, they are fulfilled first from the one-third. If something remains after them, it goes to the other legatees; otherwise nothing. But if muḥābāh and manumission both occur, which is given priority? There is a disagreement between the Sahibayn and Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn say: manumission is always preferable to muḥābāh. Imam Abu Hanifa says: if the patient first made muḥābāh and then freed, then muḥābāh is preferable; if he first freed and then made muḥābāh, then both are equal. 'Equal' means they share equally in the one-third. 'Muḥābāh is preferable' means it is executed first from the one-third; if something remains, manumission is executed; otherwise not. 'Manumission is preferable' means it is executed first from the one-third; if something remains, muḥābāh is executed; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the order of priority between muḥābāh (a sale at undervalue or gift in exchange) and itq (manumission) when both occur in death illness and the one-third of the estate is insufficient to cover both. The matn from Al-Quduri states the positions: According to Abu Hanifa, if muḥābāh was performed first and then manumission, muḥābāh takes priority. If manumission was first and then muḥābāh, they share equally in the one-third. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that manumission is always given priority, regardless of order. The commentary explains that generally all bequests are equal, but three types (itq, tadbir, muḥābāh) are exceptions and take priority over regular bequests. However, among these three, there is disagreement when both muḥābāh and itq are present and the one-third is not enough. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, if muḥābāh was done first, it consumes the one-third first; under the Sahibayn, manumission always gets priority.

Key Terms
محابات (muḥābāh): A transaction (usually a sale) in which the seller sells at a price below market value, effectively making a gift of the difference. In death illness, it is treated as a bequest.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave. In death illness, it is considered a bequest from the one-third if the slave's full value exceeds one-third.
صاحبین (al-Ṣāḥibayn): In the Hanafi school, the two disciples: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose views are authoritative alongside Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Itq takes priority.
B) Muḥābāh takes priority.
C) Both share equally.
D) The muḥābāh is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority between muḥābāh and itq is resolved in fatwa by always giving precedence to manumission as an act of worship.

General Rule: Bequests Share Equally in One-Third with Three Exceptions
Statement of general rule with example and three exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that multiple bequests under one-third share proportionally and identify the three exceptions that take priority.

Core Idea
Bequests under one-third share equally in the pool—except for freeing slaves, valid tadbir, and muḥābāh, which jump to the front.

In the previous lesson, we learned that bequests are limited to one-third of the estate. But what happens when multiple bequests are made, each individually within the one-third limit? This passage establishes the Hanafi rule that they all share proportionally in the one-third, with no preference—unless one of the three exceptional acts is present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
When no bequest individually exceeds one-third, all legatees share the one-third proportionally according to their bequest amounts, with no priority among them.
2
Work Through the Numerical Example
Given an estate of 12,000 and one-third of 4,000, with bequests totaling 8,000, each legatee receives half of their bequest because total bequests are double the one-third.
The example shows proportional sharing: 1,000 bequest gets 500, 2,000 gets 1,000, etc.
3
State the Rationale
Equality in the cause of entitlement (all are valid bequests) necessitates equality in entitlement itself.
This is a logical (talil) argument, not a textual proof.
4
List the Three Exceptions
Immediate manumission (itq) in death illness, valid tadbir (manumission suspended on death), and muḥābāh (sale at undervalue) in death illness take full priority from the one-third before other bequests.
Invalid tadbir (e.g., 'free one month after death') does not get priority.
5
Apply the Exception Rule
If any exception is present, it consumes from the one-third first; if something remains, other bequests share proportionally; if nothing remains, they get nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاصل فيه ان الوصايا اذا لم يكن فيها ما جاوز الثلث فكل من اصحابها يضرب بجميع وصيته في الثلث لا يقدم البعض على البعض الا العتق الموقع فى المرض والعتق المعلق بموت الموصى كالتدبير الصحيح والمحاباة البيع اذا وقعت فى المرض لان الوصايا قد تساوت والتساوى فى سبب الاستحقاق يوجب التساوي في نفس الاستحقاق
ترجمہ یہاں سے صاحب ہدایہ اصل مسئلہ سے ہٹ کر اس باب کا ایک قانون کلی پیش کرتے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ جب بہت کی وصیتیں جمع ہو جائیں اور ان میں سے کوئی وصیت انفرادی طریقہ پر ثلث سے متجاوز نہ ہو تو یہ تمام اصحاب الوصایا برابر کے شریک ہوں گے ربعض کو بعض پر فوقیت حاصل نہ ہوگی۔ مثلاً زید کا کل ترکہ بارہ ہزار روپے جس کا ثلث چار ہزار روپے ہے اور زید نے عمرہ کے لئے ایک ہزار کی وصیت کی اور بکر کے لئے دو ہزار کی اور خالد کیلئے تین ہزار کی اور ساجد کے لئے دو ہزار کی ، جن کا مجموعہ آٹھ ہزار ہوتا ہے مگر انفرادی طریقہ پر کوئی وصیت ثلث سے متجاوز نہیں ہے لہذا تمام وصایا درست ہیں اور سب ثلث کے اندر شریک ہوں گے مگر حصہ رسد لہذا ہر ایک کو اس کی وصیت کا نصف دیا جائے گا جس کا مجموعہ چار ہزار ہو گا جو کل ترکہ کا ثلث ہے، لہذا عمرو کو پانچ سو اور بکر کو ایک ہزار اور خالد کو پندرہ سو اور ساجد کو ایک ہزار روپے دئے جائیں گے ، اور ان سب کا مجموعہ چار ہزار ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام یہاں کسی کو کسی پر فوقیت حاصل نہ ہوگی۔ مگر اس قانون کلی سے تین چیزیں مستشفی ہیں اگر ان میں سے کوئی چیز دیگر وصایا کے ساتھ جمع ہو جائیں تو ان کے سامنے وہ وصایا دب جائیں گی ثلث میں پہلے ان تینوں میں سے جو موجود ہے اس کو نافذ کیا جائے گا اگر کچھ بچ جائے تو اس میں دیگر اصحاب وصایا سب حصہ ور سد شریک ہوں گے اور اگر کچھ نہ بچے تو اصحاب الوصایا کے لئے کچھ نہ ہوگا۔ اور وہ تین چیزیں یہ ہیں :- ۱- مرض الموت میں تنجیز آزاد کر دینا۔ ۲- ایسا عتق جو موصی کی موت پر معلق ہو جیسے مدبر بنا دینا، کہ مدبر کی آزادی موصی کی موت پر ہوگی اور تدبیر کو صحیح کی قید سے اس لئے مقدم کیا تا کہ تدبیر فاسد سے احتراز ہو جائے جیسے اگر موصی نے یوں کہا کہ یہ غلام میری موت سے ایک ماہ بعد آزاد ہے تو یہ تدبیر صحیح نہیں ہے لہذا یہ دیگر اصحاب الوصایا سے مقدم نہ ہوگا بلکہ یہ دیگر اصحاب الوصایا کے ساتھ شریک ہوگا اور اگر تد بیر سمیح ہو جیسے موجی یوں کہے کہ یہ غلام میرے مرنے پر آزاد ہے تو یہ عشق دیگر اصحاب الوصایا سے مقدم ہوگا۔ -۳- بیج کے اندر محابات جب کہ محابات مرض الموت کے اندر ہو، بہر حال یہ تین چیزیں مستقلی ہیں ان کے علاوہ باقی تمام وصایا ایسی ہیں جن میں سے کسی پر کوئی فوقیت نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ سب برابر ہیں اور جب استحقاق کے سبب میں برابری اور مساوات ہے تو نفس استحقاق کے اندر بھی برابری ہوگی۔
The principle regarding it is that when there are bequests, none of which exceed the one-third, then each of the legatees takes his entire bequest from the one-third; no one is given preference over another except for manumission executed during illness, manumission suspended on the testator's death like valid tadbir, and muḥābāh in a sale when it occurs during illness, because bequests are equal and equality in the cause of entitlement necessitates equality in the entitlement itself.
Translation: From here, the author of al-Hidayah digresses from the specific issue and presents a general rule of this chapter. He says: When many bequests are combined and none individually exceeds the one-third, then all legatees are equal partners; none has superiority over another. For example, Zaid's total estate is twelve thousand rupees, its one-third is four thousand rupees. Zaid made a bequest of one thousand for Amr, two thousand for Bakr, three thousand for Khalid, and two thousand for Sajid, total eight thousand. But individually none exceeds the one-third. So all bequests are valid, and all share in the one-third proportionally. Thus each gets half of his bequest: Amr gets five hundred, Bakr one thousand, Khalid fifteen hundred, Sajid one thousand, total four thousand. Summary: no one has superiority. However, three things are excepted from this general rule. If any of these are combined with other bequests, those bequests are suppressed; from the one-third, that excepted item is executed first; if something remains, other legatees share proportionally; if nothing remains, they get nothing. The three things are: (1) immediate manumission in death illness, (2) manumission suspended on the testator's death, like making a mudabbar (valid tadbir), because the mudabbar's freedom occurs at the testator's death. The condition 'valid tadbir' is added to exclude invalid tadbir, e.g., if the testator says 'this slave is free one month after my death', that is not valid, so it is not given priority but shares with other bequests. If tadbir is valid, like saying 'this slave is free upon my death', then it takes priority over other bequests. (3) muḥābāh in a sale when it occurs in death illness. In any case, these three are independent; apart from them, all other bequests have no superiority over each other; they are all equal, and when the cause of entitlement is equal, the entitlement itself is equal.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage establishes the general rule for distributing multiple bequests when none individually exceeds one-third of the estate. The rule is that all legatees share proportionally in the one-third according to the amounts bequeathed. No one is given priority. The author provides a clear numerical example: an estate of 12,000 with one-third of 4,000, and bequests totaling 8,000. Since none exceeds the one-third, all bequests are valid and each legatee receives half of his bequest (since total bequests are double the one-third). The reason given is that all bequests are equal in their cause of entitlement (the will), so entitlement itself should be equal. Then the author lists three exceptions that take full priority from the one-third before any other bequest is considered: (1) immediate manumission (itq) executed during death illness, (2) valid tadbir (manumission suspended on death), and (3) muḥābāh (sale at undervalue) in death illness. These are given priority because they are considered more urgent or pious acts. If these excepted items consume the entire one-third, other bequests get nothing; otherwise the remainder is shared among other bequest holders.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a person to be executed after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.
ثلث (thulth): The one-third of the estate that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without heirs' permission.
تدبیر (tadbir): A declaration that a slave will be free upon the master's death. It is a valid form of manumission suspended on death.
عتق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave. In this context, immediate manumission during death illness.
محاباة (muḥābāh): A sale at undervalue; in death illness, it is treated as a bequest for the undervalue amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the general rule for multiple bequests when none exceeds one-third of the estate?
A) They are executed in order of the date they were made.
B) They share proportionally in the one-third, with no priority except for three exceptions.
C) The largest bequest is paid first, then the next, until one-third is exhausted.
D) The testator's executor decides the distribution.

Key Takeaway
Multiple bequests under one-third share proportionally, but itq, valid tadbir, and muḥābāh take full priority from the one-third.

Dividing the Third Among Muhabaat and Itq: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing the third among multiple acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Hanifa's rule for dividing the third among multiple preferential sales (muhabah) and manumissions ('itq) in death illness, and distinguish the Sahibayn's position that manumission always takes precedence.

Core Idea
Order matters: acts of the same type share equally; later manumission competes with preceding muhabah, but Sahibayn give manumission absolute priority.

In death illness, acts of preferential sale (muhabah) and manumission ('itq) are treated as bequests from the one-third of the estate. When multiple such acts occur, the allocation of the third becomes a legal puzzle. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on how to prioritize these acts. This lesson unpacks two scenarios from the Hidayah to help you trace the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their legal nature
Recognize that muhabah (preferential sale) and itq (manumission) during death illness are both subject to the one-third limit. The dispute concerns how to divide the third when multiple such acts occur. Each act competes for a share of the third.
Muhabah occurs in a commutative contract; itq is a pure act of worship.
2
First scenario: muhabah, then itq, then muhabah
Apply Abu Hanifa's principle: divide the third equally between the two muhabaat (since they are equal in type). Then take the share of the second muhabah and split it equally with the manumission that preceded it.
3
Second scenario: itq, then muhabah, then itq
Here, the third is divided between the first manumission and the muhabah. The manumission's share is then divided between the first and second manumissions equally.
4
Contrast with the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn hold that manumission always takes precedence (العق اولى بكل حال). Under their rule, in both scenarios the third would be allocated to the manumission(s) first, reducing the muhabah shares accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا قال ابو حنيفه اذا حابي ثم اعتق ثم حابى قسم الثلث بين المحابتين نصفين لتساويهما ثم ما اصاب المحاباة الاخيرة قسم بينها وبين العتق لان العتق مقدم عليها فيستو يان ولو اعتق ثم حابي ثم اعتق قسم الثلث بين العتق الاول والمحاباة وما اصاب العتق قسم بينه وبين العتق الثانى وعندهما العتق اولى بكل حال.
ترجمہ: اور اس اصول کی بنیاد پر ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا جب کہ مریض نے محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی تو ثلث کو دونوں محابتوں کے در میان آدھا آدھا کیا جائے گا ان دونوں کے مساوی ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر جو مقدار کہ آخری محابات کو پہنچی ہے اس کو محابات اور معتق کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ محقق محابات پر مقدم ہے پس دونوں برابر ہوں گے اور اگر مریض نے آزاد کیا پھر محابات کی پھر آزاد کیا تو ثمث کو عتق اول اور محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور جو مقدار کہ عتق کے حصہ میں پڑے اس کو عتق اول اور عتق ثانی کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہر حال میں عتق اولی ہے۔
تشریح: امام ابو حنیفہ کے بیان فرمودہ اصول کے مطابق ان کے نزدیک اس اصول پر دو متفرع ہونے والی جزئیوں کو پیش فرماتے ہیں - مریض نے مرض الموت میں ایک غلام کو آزاد کیا اور دو شخصوں کے ساتھ بیع میں محابات کی جسکی ترتیب اس طرح ہے اولاً محابات کی تھی اور ثانیاً غلام آزاد کیا اور ثالثاً پھر محابات کی تو یہاں کیا حکم ہوگا؟ تو فرمایا کہ ثلث کو دونوں محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کر لیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہ دونوں محابات برابر ہیں اس لئے کہ دونوں کا وقوع عقد معاوضہ کے ضمن میں ہوا ہے، پھر جو ثلث کا نصف آخری محابات کے حصہ میں پڑا ہے اس نصف کو آخری محابات اور معتق کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ آخری محابات سے پہلے عتق آیا ہے اور جب عتق پہلے آئے اور محابات بعد میں آئے تو مزاحمت کی وجہ سے وہاں عتق اور محابات برابر کے شریک ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا۔
- اور اگر پہلے مریض نے آزاد کیا ہو اور پھر محابات کی ہو اور پھر ثالثا آزاد کیا ہو تو اب کیا حکم ہوگا؟ تو چونکہ یہاں محابات سے عتق مقدم ہے لہذا قاعدہ مذکورہ کے مطابق ثلث کو عتق اول اور محابات کے درمیان تقسیم کیا جائے گا، پھر جو محابات کے حصہ میں آیا اس میں کوئی ردو بدل نہ ہوگا، اور جو عتق کے حصہ میں آیا ہے اس کو عتق اول اور عتق ثانی کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا جس کی وجہ ظاہر ہے۔ اور یہ سب تفصیل امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ہر حال میں عتق ہی کو مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔
And upon this, Abu Hanifa said: When one does muhabah (preferential sale), then manumits, then does muhabah, the third is divided between the two muhabaat in halves due to their equality. Then what reaches the last muhabah is divided between it and the manumission, because manumission takes precedence over it, so they become equal. And if one manumits, then does muhabah, then manumits, the third is divided between the first manumission and the muhabah, and what goes to the manumission is divided between the first and second manumission. And according to the two Sahibayn, manumission is always preferable. Translation and commentary follow.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the division of the one-third limit (thalith) when there are multiple acts of muhabah (preferential sale) and manumission ('itq) in the death illness. The text presents two sub-branches derived from Imam Abu Hanifa's principle. In the first scenario, where a patient first does muhabah, then manumits, then does another muhabah, Abu Hanifa divides the third equally between the two muhabaat because they are equal (both occur within a commutative contract). Then the portion of the second muhabah is split with the manumission because the manumission preceded it, so they compete equally. In the second scenario, where manumission precedes both muhabaat, the third is split between the first manumission and the muhabah, and then the manumission's share is split between the first and second manumission. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that manumission always takes precedence over muhabah, regardless of order.

Key Terms
محابات (muhabah): A sale at a price below market value, i.e., preferential treatment (favoritism) in a commutative contract.
عتق (itq): Manumission (freeing of a slave), considered a pure act of worship.
ثلث (thalith): The one-third of the estate that a testator can dispose of through bequests (wasiyya).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario (muhabah, then itq, then muhabah), how does Abu Hanifa divide the third?
A) Half to the first muhabah, half to the second muhabah, then the second muhabah's half is further split with the manumission.
B) All to the manumission, ignoring the muhabaat.
C) One-third to each act equally.
D) The third is split between the two muhabaat only, no share for manumission.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa divides the third based on type and order: acts of the same type share equally first, then later manumission competes with preceding muhabah; the Sahibayn give manumission absolute priority.

Bequest for Manumission with Partial Loss of Funds: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on executing bequest when specified funds are partially lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the execution of a bequest for manumission when the specified funds are partially lost, and analyze their qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
A bequest for manumission is tied to the specified price; partial loss of funds invalidates it, unlike Hajj which is a pure worship act.

In this passage, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a bequest for manumission. The testator leaves 100 dirhams to free a slave, but some dirhams are lost. Abu Hanifa rules that the bequest fails for the remainder, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that it should be executed to the extent possible. This disagreement hinges on the nature of manumission as either a pure act of worship or a transactional act tied to a specific object. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct ruling in similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the two rulings
The testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to free a slave, but part is lost. Abu Hanifa rules that no slave is freed with the remainder. The Sahibayn rule that a slave should be freed with the remainder, by analogy to a bequest for Hajj.
Focus on the difference in outcome: heirs keep the money vs. freeing a cheaper slave.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn analogize manumission to Hajj: both are acts of piety (qurbah), so the bequest should be fulfilled as far as possible with the remaining funds.
This is a qiyas based on the common illa of being a pious act.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's counter-qiyas
Abu Hanifa distinguishes manumission because it is tied to a specific price (the slave's value). Executing the bequest with a cheaper slave would mean freeing a different slave than intended. Hajj, on the other hand, is a pure right of Allah that can be performed at varying costs. He also compares to a bequest of a specific sum to a person: if some is lost, the remainder goes to that person, but here the 'person' (the slave) is defined by price, so a different price changes the intended recipient.
Understand why the analogy fails in Abu Hanifa's view: the illa is not valid because the object is specified.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, if part of the 100 dirhams is lost, the heirs keep the remainder and no slave is freed. Under the Sahibayn, a slave is bought with the remainder and freed on behalf of the testator.
This affects the distribution of the estate.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but typically Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The Sahibayn's view, though strong in analogy, is overcome by the specificity of the bequest.
In fatwa practice, the stronger view is Abu Hanifa's unless there is a reason to adopt the Sahibayn's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن أوصى بان يعتق عنه بهذه المائة عبد فهلك منها در هم لم يعتق عنه بما بقى عند ابي حنيفة وان كانت وصيته بحجة يحج عنه بما بقى من حيث بلغ وان لم يهلك منها وبقى شى من الحجة يرد على الورثة وقالا يعتق عنه بما بقى لانه وصية بنوع قربة فيجب تنفيذها ما امكن اعتبار بالوصية بالحج.
ترجمہ: محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور جس نے وصیت کی کہ اس کی جانب سے اس سو درہم سے ایک غلام آزاد کر دیا جائے پس ان میں سے ایک درہم ہلاک ہو گیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مابقی کا اس کی جانب سے غلام آزاد نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر اس کی وصیت حج کے بارے میں ہو تو اس کی جانب سے مابقی سے وہاں سے حج کرایا جائے گا جہاں سے پہونچ ہو سکے اور اگر اس میں سے کچھ ہلاک نہ ہوا ہوا اور حج سے کوئی چیز باقی بچ گئی تو مابقی کو ورثا کو واپس کر دیا جائے گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کی جانب سے مابقی سے آزاد کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہ نوع قربت کی وصیت ہے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے حج کی وصیت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔
تشریح: زید نے اپنے وارثوں کے سامنے یہ وصیت کی کہ ان سو درہم سے میری جانب سے حج کرادیا، اور اتفاق سے ان میں سے کچھ دراہم ہلاک ہو گئے تو مابقی دراہم سے زید کی جانب سے حج کرانا واجب ہے، اگر اتنی مقدار باقی ہے کہ دہلی سے اتنی مقدار سے حج کرایا جا سکتا ہے اور زید دہلی کا ہی باشندہ ہے تو دہلی سے حج کرایا جائے گا اور اگر دہلی سے حج نہیں ہو سکتا البتہ بمبئی سے جانے سے حج کے لئے وہ رقم کافی ہے تو دہلی کے بجائے بمبئی سے حج کرایا جائے گا۔ خلاصہ کلام حج کی وصیت کی صورت میں کچھ دراہم کا ہلاک ہو جانا وصیت کو باطل نہیں کریگا اور اس کی جانب سے حج کرایا جائے گا۔
اور اگر زید نے یہ وصیت کی ہو کہ ان سو درہم کا غلام خرید کر آزاد کر دیا تو ورثا پر واجب تھا کہ وہ ان سو درہم کا غلام خرید کر آزاد کریں لیکن اتفاق سے ان میں سے مثلاً ایک درہم ہلاک ہو گیا اور باقی رہ گئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو اس میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اب بھی وہی حکم ہے جو حج کی وصیت کی صورت میں ہے یعنی مابقی کا غلام خرید کر اس کی جانب سے آزاد کیا جائے گا، اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مابقی کا غلام خرید کر اس کی جانب سے آزاد نہیں کیا جائے گا، اگر اس نے حج کرانے کی وصیت کی تھی اور ان میں سے کچھ ہلاک نہیں ہوا اور حج کر دیا گیا لیکن حج سے فراغت کے بعد کچھ دراہم بچ گئے تو جو باقی دراہم بچے ان کو ورثا کو واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اختلافی مسئلہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عتق کی وصیت یہ قربت کی ایک قسم کی وصیت ہے لہذا جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس کی اس وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے انھوں نے اس کو حج کی وصیت پر قیاس ہے۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل: وله انه وصية بالعتق لعبد يشترى بمائة وتنفيذها فيمن يشترى باقل منه تنفيذ لغير الموصى له وذلك لا يجوز بخلاف الوصية بالحج لانها قربة محضة هي حق الله تعالى والمستحق لم يتبدل وصار كما اذا اوصى لرجل بمائة فهلك بعضها يدفع الباقى اليه.
ترجمہ: اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عتق کی وصیت ہے ایسے غلام کے لئے جس کو سو میں خریدا گیا ہو اور وصیت کو نافذ کرنا اس غلام کے لئے جس کو سو سے کم میں خریدا گیا ہو، نافذ کرنا ہے غیر موصی له (جس کے لئے وصیت نہیں کی گئی) کے لئے اور یہ جائز نہیں، بخلاف حج کی وصیت کے کیونکہ وہ خالص قربت ہے جو اللہ کا حق ہے اور مستحق بدلا نہیں، اور یہ ایسے ہی ہے جیسے اگر کسی نے ایک شخص کے لئے سو درہم کی وصیت کی اور کچھ ہلاک ہو گئے تو باقی اسے دے دیا جائے گا۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever bequeaths that a slave be freed on his behalf with these hundred dirhams, and one dirham thereof is lost, then according to Abu Hanifa no slave is freed on his behalf with the remainder. But if his bequest was for Hajj, then Hajj would be performed on his behalf with the remainder as far as it reaches. And if nothing is lost and something remains after the Hajj, it is returned to the heirs. And the two (Sahibayn) said: A slave is freed on his behalf with the remainder, because it is a bequest of a type of piety, so it must be implemented as far as possible, by analogy to the bequest for Hajj. Translation and commentary follow.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage discusses a bequest where the testator specifies a sum of money (100 dirhams) to be used to buy and free a slave. If some dirhams are lost, the ruling differs. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest fails for the remainder because the bequest was for a slave purchased with exactly 100 dirhams; buying a cheaper slave would fulfill the bequest for a different object, which is invalid. In contrast, a bequest for Hajj is a pure act of worship (qurbah mahdah) where the means can be adjusted; if funds are lost, Hajj is performed with what remains, and any surplus is returned to heirs. The Sahibayn analogize manumission to Hajj, arguing that both are acts of piety, so the bequest should be implemented as far as possible. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: manumission is tied to a specific amount (the price of a slave), whereas Hajj is an act that can be performed with varying funds. Additionally, he compares to a bequest of a specific sum to a person: if some is lost, the remainder is given to that person.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest made by a testator for after death, applicable to one-third of the estate.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave, considered an act of worship but also a transaction subject to property law.
قربة (qurbah): An act that brings one closer to Allah, a pious deed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a bequest to free a slave with 100 dirhams not executed with the remainder if some dirhams are lost?
A) Because manumission is not a valid bequest.
B) Because the remainder is too small to be useful.
C) Because the bequest was for a specific slave (purchased with 100 dirhams), and buying a cheaper slave would change the intended object.
D) Because the heirs refuse consent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest for manumission with a specified sum is invalidated by partial loss of the sum, unlike a bequest for Hajj, because manumission is tied to the specific price of a slave.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest for Manumission with Partial Loss: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest for manumission with partial loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi intra-school positions on executing a bequest for manumission when designated funds are partially lost, and apply the underlying legal principle to determine whether the bequest is executed from the remainder.

Core Idea
If bequeathed funds are lost, manumission fails under Abu Hanifa but succeeds under Sahibayn due to the nature of the legatee.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest for manumission (itaq) when part of the designated wealth is lost. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hinges on whether manumission is a pure act of worship (like Hajj) or has an element of the slave's right. Understanding this dispute refines your ability to apply the Hanafi framework for executing bequests when conditions change.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the loss
Identify the scenario: testator bequeaths 100 dirhams to buy and free a slave; 1 dirham is lost, 99 remain. The question is whether the bequest is executed from the remainder.
The loss is partial; the bequest was specific to the full amount.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn say execute from the remainder. Their proof: analogy to a bequest for Hajj, which is executed from remaining funds. Manumission is an act of worship (qurbah) like Hajj, so it should be fulfilled as far as possible.
They use qiyas: Hajj is a pure right of Allah; they analogize manumission to it.
3
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says the bequest is not executed from the remainder. His proof: the bequest is for a specific slave bought with the full amount. Using less changes the legatee (slave), which is impermissible. Unlike Hajj, where the entitled party (Allah) remains the same.
Key distinction: the legatee changes for manumission but not for Hajj.
4
Analyze the distinction: right of Allah vs. right of the slave
The dispute turns on whether manumission is a pure right of Allah or includes a right of the slave. Abu Hanifa sees an element of the slave's right, so the legatee is the specific slave; Sahibayn see it as pure worship, so the right is Allah's and any amount suffices.
This distinction is crucial for understanding Hanafi rulings on manumission.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the heirs keep the remainder; under Sahibayn, they must buy a cheaper slave and free it on the testator's behalf.
The difference affects the heirs' inheritance and the slave's freedom.

Source Text
