كتاب الوصايا
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ ترجمہ محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے اور جس نے وصیت کی کہ اس کی جانب سے اس سو درہم سے ایک غلام آزاد کر دیا جائے پس ان میں سے ایک درہم ہلاک ہو گیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مابقی کا اس کی جانب سے غلام آزاد نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر اس کی وصیت حج کے بارے میں ہو تو اس کی جانب سے مابقی سے وہاں سے حج کرایا جائے گا جہاں سے پہونچ ہو سکے اور اگر اس میں سے کچھ ہلاک نہ ہوا ہوا اور حج سے کوئی چیز باقی بچ گئی تو مابقی کو ورثاء پر واپس کر دیا جائے گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کی جانب سے مابقی سے آزاد کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہ نوع قربت کی وصیت ہے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے حج کی وصیت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔
تشریح زید نے اپنے وارثوں کے سامنے یہ وصیت کی کہ ان سو درہم سے میری جانب سے حج کرادیا، اور اتفاق سے ان میں سے کچھ دراہم ہلاک ہو گئے تو مابقی دراہم سے زید کی جانب سے حج کرانا واجب ہے، اگر اتنی مقدار باقی ہے کہ دہلی سے اتنی مقدار سے حج کرایا جا سکتا ہے اور زید دہلی کا ہی باشندہ ہے تو دہلی سے حج کرایا جائے گا اور اگر دہلی سے حج نہیں ہو سکتا البتہ بمبئی سے جانے سے حج کے لئے وہ رقم کافی ہے تو دہلی کے بجائے بمبئی سے حج کرایا جائے گا۔ خلاصہ کلام حج کی وصیت کی صورت میں کچھ دراہم کا ہلاک ہو جانا وصیت کو باطل نہیں کریگا اور اس کی جانب سے حج کرایا جائے گا۔
اور اگر زید نے یہ وصیت کی ہو کہ ان سو درہم کا غلام خرید کر آزاد کر دیا تو ورثاء پر واجب تھا کہ وہ ان سو درہم کا غلام خرید کر آزاد کریں لیکن اتفاق سے ان میں سے مثلاً ایک درہم ہلاک ہو گیا اور نانوے باقی رہ گئے تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو اس میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔
صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اب بھی وہی حکم ہے جو حج کی وصیت کی صورت میں ہے یعنی مابقی کا غلام خرید کر اس کی جانب سے آزاد کیا جائے گا، اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مابقی کا غلام خرید کر اس کی جانب سے آزاد نہیں کیا جائے گا، اگر اس نے حج کرانے کی وصیت کی تھی اور ان میں سے کچھ ہلاک نہیں ہوا اور حج کر دیا گیا لیکن حج سے فراغت کے بعد کچھ دراہم بچ گئے تو جو باقی دراہم بچے ان کو ورثا کو واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اختلافی مسئلہ میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتقاق کی وصیت یہ قربت کی ایک قسم کی وصیت ہے لہذا جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس کی اس وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے انھوں نے اس کو حج کی وصیت پر قیاس کیا۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله انه وصية بالعتق لعبد يشترى بمائة وتنفيذها فيمن يشترى باقل منه تنفيذ لغير الموصى له وذلك لا يجوز بخلاف الوصية بالحج لانها قربة محضة هي حق الله تعالى والمستحق لم يتبدل وصار كما اذا اوصى لرجل بمائة فهلك بعضها يدفع الباقى اليه ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محقق کی وصیت ہے ایسے غلام کے لئے جس کو سو میں خریدا گیا ہو اور وصیت کو نافذ کرنا اس غلام کے اندر جس کو اس سے کم میں خریدا گیا ہو موصی لہ کے غیر کے لئے وصیت کو نافذ کرنا ہے اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے بخلاف حج کی وصیت کے اس لئے کہ یہ خالص قربت ہے جوکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کاحق ہے اور مستحق نہیں بدلتا اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ اس نے وصیت کی ہو کسی شخص کے لئے سو دراہم کی پس ان میں سے کچھ ہلاک ہو گیا تو باقی کو اسی شخص کو دے دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زید کی وصیت مذکورہ میں موصی لہ وہ غلام ہے جس کو سو میں خریدا جائے اور جب اس سے کم میں خرید کر آزاد کیا جائے گا تو موصی لہ بدلا ہوا ہے اور ورثا کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ وہ موصی لہ میں تبدیلی کر دیں۔ اور رہا مسئلہ حج کی وصیت کا تو وہاں مستحق حج کسی صورت میں نہیں بدلتا اس لئے کہ حق خالص قربت ہے اور وہ اللہ کا حق ہے تو مستحق حج اللہ تعالیٰ ہے جس میں کوئی تبدیلی نہیں ہے۔ اور حج کی وصیت ایسی ہے جیسے زید نے وصیت کی کہ یہ سو درہم خالد کو دے دینا اتفاق سے ان میں سے کچھ دراہم ہلاک ہو گئے تو جو دراہم باقی ہیں وہ خالد ہی کو دئے جائیں گے کیونکہ موصی لہ میں کوئی تبدیلی نہیں ہے اور اعتاق والی صورت میں موصی لہ میں تبدیلی ہے۔
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on al-Hidaya, Volume 16. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever made a bequest that a slave be freed on his behalf from these hundred dirhams, then one of them was lost, then according to Abu Hanifa a slave will not be freed on his behalf from the remainder. And if his bequest was regarding Hajj, then Hajj will be performed on his behalf from the remainder from wherever possible. And if none of it was lost and something remained after Hajj, the remainder will be returned to the heirs. And the Sahibayn said: He will be freed on his behalf from the remainder, because this is a type of bequest of worship, so executing the bequest as much as possible is obligatory, by analogy to the bequest of Hajj. Explanation: Zaid made a bequest before his heirs: 'Perform Hajj on my behalf from these hundred dirhams.' And by chance some dirhams were lost, so performing Hajj on Zaid's behalf from the remaining dirhams is obligatory. If enough remains to perform Hajj from Delhi, and Zaid is a resident of Delhi, then Hajj will be performed from Delhi. If Hajj cannot be done from Delhi but the amount is sufficient for going from Bombay, then Hajj will be performed from Bombay instead of Delhi. In summary: In the case of a bequest of Hajj, the loss of some dirhams will not nullify the bequest, and Hajj will be performed on his behalf. And if Zaid made a bequest: 'Buy a slave with these hundred dirhams and free him,' then it was obligatory on the heirs to buy a slave with these hundred dirhams and free him. But if by chance one dirham was lost and ninety-nine remained, what is the ruling? There is a difference of opinion between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The Sahibayn say: The same ruling as in the case of the bequest of Hajj applies: a slave will be bought with the remainder and freed on his behalf. And Imam Abu Hanifa says: A slave will not be bought with the remainder and freed on his behalf. If he had bequeathed Hajj and none of it was lost, and Hajj was performed, but after completing Hajj some dirhams remained, then those remaining dirhams will be returned to the heirs. The proof of the Sahibayn in this disputed issue is that the bequest of manumission is a type of bequest of worship, so executing his bequest as much as possible is obligatory; they analogized it to the bequest of Hajj. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that it is a bequest of manumission for a slave who is bought for one hundred, and executing it for one who is bought for less is execution for someone other than the legatee, and that is not permissible. Unlike the bequest of Hajj, because it is pure worship which is a right of Allah the Exalted, and the entitled party does not change. And it becomes like when he bequeathed one hundred to a man, then some of it was lost, the remainder is given to that same man. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa, the gist of which is that in Zaid's mentioned bequest, the legatee is the slave who is bought for one hundred. And when a slave bought for less is freed, the legatee has changed, and the heirs do not have the right to change the legatee. As for the issue of bequest of Hajj, there the entitled party for Hajj does not change in any way because the right is pure worship and it is Allah's right, so the entitled party for Hajj is Allah the Exalted, who does not change. And the bequest of Hajj is like when Zaid bequeathed: 'Give these hundred dirhams to Khalid.' If by chance some dirhams were lost, the remaining dirhams will be given to Khalid himself because there is no change in the legatee. Whereas in the case of manumission, there is a change in the legatee.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest for manumission when some of the designated funds are lost. The issue is: Zaid bequeaths one hundred dirhams to buy a slave and free him. If one dirham is lost, what happens? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the bequest should be executed to the extent possible, i.e., buy a slave with the remaining ninety-nine dirhams and free him on Zaid's behalf. They analogize this to a bequest for Hajj, where if funds are insufficient but some remain, Hajj is performed from wherever possible. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that the bequest for manumission is specific to a slave purchased for exactly one hundred dirhams. Using less changes the intended recipient (the slave), which is not permissible because the legatee must be exactly as specified by the testator. In contrast, for Hajj, the entitled party is Allah, who does not change; any amount used for Hajj fulfills the same right. The commentary elaborates with examples: for Hajj, the starting point can be adjusted based on remaining funds; for manumission, the slave must be bought with the exact amount specified. The ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the bequest is nullified for the remainder, and the remaining money returns to the heirs. The Sahibayn's view is that the bequest is partially valid.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made during one's lifetime to take effect after death, involving transfer of ownership or benefit.
عتاق (itaq): Manumission of a slave; legally, the act of freeing a slave, considered an act of worship and a right of Allah (or of the slave, according to dispute).
موصی لہ (mūṣā lahu): The legatee or beneficiary of a bequest; for a bequest of manumission, the slave to be freed is the legatee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over a bequest for manumission when some dirhams are lost, what is the key factor that leads to Abu Hanifa's position?
A) Manumission is not a valid bequest
B) The legatee (slave) would change
C) The heirs must consent
D) The bequest must be from the exact amount

Key Takeaway
A bequest for manumission is specific to the designated slave; if funds are lost, Abu Hanifa voids the remainder, while the Sahibayn allow partial execution by analogy to Hajj.

Underlying Principle: Is Manumission a Right of Allah or the Slave?
Discusses the usul dispute underlying the ruling on bequest for manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqq Allah and haqq al-'abd in the context of manumission, and explain how this classification affects the acceptance of testimony and the change of legatee in a bequest.

Core Idea
Manumission's classification as haqq Allah or haqq al-'abd determines whether the legatee can change and whether testimony requires a claim.

In this lesson, we examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Is manumission (itq) a right of Allah (haqq Allah) or a right of the slave (haqq al-'abd)? This classification has direct consequences for procedural rules and the validity of bequests. By understanding the principle, you will see how specific rulings flow from deeper usul foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold regarding the legal nature of 'itq. Abu Hanifa considers it haqq al-'abd; the Sahibayn consider it haqq Allah.
2
Understand procedural consequence
For haqq Allah, testimony is accepted without a claim from the beneficiary. For haqq al-'abd, a claim is required. This is a key distinction in Hanafi procedural law.
3
Apply to the bequest scenario
In a bequest for manumission where the slave's value is partially lost, under Abu Hanifa the legatee changes (invalidating the bequest) because the right belongs to the specific slave. Under the Sahibayn, the legatee does not change because the right is Allah's, so the bequest can be partially executed.
4
Recognize the author's validation
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah states that this derivation (that the dispute hinges on the nature of 'itq) is more plausible (وهذا اشبه). This indicates a preference for the Sahibayn's framework.

And it is said that this issue is based on another disputed principle, which is that according to them (the Sahibayn), manumission is a right of Allah, so that testimony is accepted regarding it without a claim, and therefore the entitled party does not change. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is a right of the slave, so that testimony without a claim is not accepted, and therefore the entitled party changes. And this (i.e., that the issue is derived from this principle) is more plausible. Explanation: There is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding manumission being a right of Allah or a right of the slave. Imam Sahib considers manumission a right of the slave, and the Sahibayn consider it a right of Allah. In the case of a right of Allah, a claim is not required for acceptance of testimony. In the case of a right of the slave, a claim is required for acceptance of testimony. When this principle is understood, it becomes clear that the issue of manumission is derived from this principle: According to the Sahibayn, manumission, like the bequest of Hajj, is a right of Allah, and there is no question of change in the right of Allah, so in manumission too the legatee does not change. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, manumission is a right of the slave, so the change of legatee is apparent, because the legatee was the slave who would be bought with one hundred, and now the legatee becomes the one bought with ninety-nine. The author (al-Marghinani) said that this is the correct opinion, i.e., to say that the difference between the Sahibayn and Imam Sahib is based on the difference regarding this principle of whether manumission is a right of Allah or a right of the slave is the correct statement.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage refines the earlier dispute by tying it to a deeper usul principle: whether 'itq (manumission) is a right of Allah (haqq Allah) or a right of the slave (haqq al-'abd). The Sahibayn consider 'itq a haqq Allah, so the entitled party (the slave) is not fixed; any slave can be freed, and the bequest can be partially executed. Imam Abu Hanifa considers 'itq a haqq al-'abd, meaning the specific slave designated by the testator is the entitled party; changing the amount of purchase changes the entitled party, which is invalid. The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) states that this explanation (that the dispute hinges on this principle) is more plausible (وهذا اشبه). The commentary clarifies the practical implication: for haqq Allah, testimony is accepted without a claim from the slave; for haqq al-'abd, a claim is required. Thus, the ruling on the bequest flows from this fundamental difference. This lesson demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh connects specific rulings to broader legal maxims and principles, providing a systematic structure to the madhhab.

Key Terms
حق اللہ (haqq Allah): A right belonging to Allah, with no specific human claimant; testimony regarding it does not require a claim.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right belonging to a human being; testimony regarding it requires a claim from the beneficiary.
عتاق (itaq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave, considered in this context as either haqq Allah or haqq al-'abd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the testator did not specify a particular slave
D) Because the heirs can choose any slave

Key Takeaway
The classification of 'itq as haqq Allah or haqq al-'abd is an intra-Hanafi dispute with direct implications for bequest execution and testimony procedure.

Change of Legatee in Conditional Bequest of Slave Emancipation
Explaining the ruling on change of legatee when condition not met

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifah's ruling on change of legatee in a conditional slave emancipation will and explain the rational proof (qiyas) distinguishing it from a will for Hajj.

Core Idea
If a condition for freeing a slave is unmet, the legatee changes, voiding the will.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling in the Hanafi school regarding conditional wills for slave emancipation. Imam Abu Hanifah holds that if a testator says 'My slave is free if you buy him for 100 dirhams' and the slave is bought for less, the will cannot be enforced because the legatee specified by the condition has changed. This ruling is contrasted with wills for Hajj and specific sums of money, providing a clear example of how the nature of the beneficiary affects the validity of a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a conditional bequest of slave emancipation. The ruling (hukm) according to Imam Abu Hanifah is that the will is not valid (batil) because the condition was not fulfilled and the legatee changed.
The condition is the purchase price of 100 dirhams; if purchased for less, the legatee is a different slave.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof (dalil) is a rational analogy (qiyas) comparing the case to a will for Hajj and a bequest of dirhams.
The passage states 'This is unlike a will for Hajj...' and provides the analogy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key distinction is whether the beneficiary is a specific entity that can change. In Hajj, the beneficiary is Allah, who is unchanging. In a dirham bequest to a person, the person is fixed. In emancipation, the specific slave (bought for 100 dirhams) is the legatee; if a different slave is bought, the legatee changes.
The legal link: the right in Hajj is a pure act of devotion (haqq Allah), so the beneficiary does not change. Emancipation involves a specific slave, so the legatee is tied to the condition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that 'itq is a right of Allah, so the legatee should not change, making the will valid for the purchased slave.
This intra-Hanafi difference is based on the nature of the right: haqq Allah vs. haqq al-‘abd.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The passage presents Abu Hanifah's position as the primary one; no explicit tarjih is given, but the disagreement remains unresolved in this passage.
Later Hanafi works may prefer one view; the mufta bihi is not specified here.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶ اندر جس کو اس سے کم میں خریدا گیا ہو موضی لا کے غیر کے لئے وصیت کو نافذ کرنا ہے اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے بخلاف حج کی وصیت کے اس لئے کہ یہ خالص قریب سے جوکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے اور مستحق نہیں بدلتا اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ اس نے وصیت کی ہو کسی شخص کے لئے سو دراہم کی پس ان میں ہے کچھ ہلاک ہو گیا تو باقی کو اسی شخص کو دے دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ زید کی وصیت مذکورہ میں موضی لا وہ غلام ہے جس کو سو میں خریدا جائے اور

Book of Wills. If someone is bought for less than what was specified in the will, executing the will for someone other than the legatee is not permissible. This is unlike a will for Hajj, because that is pure devotion which is a right of Allah, and the beneficiary does not change. It is like when someone makes a will giving one hundred dirhams to a person, then some are lost; the remainder is given to that same person. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifah. The gist is that in the mentioned will of Zayd, the legatee is the slave who is bought for one hundred. When he is bought for less and then freed, the legatee has changed, and the heirs do not have the right to change the legatee. As for the issue of a will for Hajj, the beneficiary of the Hajj does not change in any case because it is a pure act of devotion and a right of Allah, so the beneficiary is Allah, who does not change. The will for Hajj is like if Zayd wills to give one hundred dirhams to Khalid, and by chance some are lost; the remaining dirhams are given to Khalid because the legatee has not changed. In the case of emancipation, the legatee changes.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Abu Hanifah regarding a specific scenario in wills (waṣāyā). If a testator declares in his deathbed: 'My slave is free if you buy him for one hundred dirhams,' and the slave is subsequently bought for a lesser amount (e.g., ninety dirhams), the will cannot be executed for the slave actually purchased. The reason is that the legatee (muṣā lah) in the testator's statement was the slave that would be bought for one hundred dirhams. Since the condition was not met, the slave who is actually bought is a different entity. The heirs do not have the right to alter the legatee. This is contrasted with a will to perform Hajj, where the beneficiary is Allah Himself, who is unchanging. Similarly, if a testator bequeaths a specific sum of money to a person and part of that sum is lost, the remainder is given to the same legatee because the legatee does not change. The passage is a direct ruling (ḥukm) supported by a rational proof (dalīl 'aqlī) that distinguishes between acts of devotion (like Hajj) and other rights. The commentary (tašrīḥ) elaborates on the proof. This is from the Hanafi school, specifically the position of Imam Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The legatee or beneficiary of a will, the person or entity to whom the bequest is given.
عتق (‘itq): Emancipation of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifah rules that a conditional will for slave emancipation is void if the condition is not met, because the legatee changes, unlike wills for Hajj where the beneficiary is Allah.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is Emancipation a Right of Allah or the Slave?
Analyzing the intra-madhhab dispute on the legal nature of emancipation and its practical effect on conditional wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of 'itq, state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to the case of a conditional will for emancipation.

Core Idea
Whether emancipation is a right of Allah or the slave determines if a conditional will changes its beneficiary.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute about the fundamental nature of emancipation ('itq). Imam Abu Hanifah considers it a right of the slave (ḥaqq al-'abd), while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Ṣāḥibayn), consider it a right of Allah (ḥaqq Allāh). This seemingly theoretical difference has a direct practical consequence: in a case where a testator makes a conditional will for emancipation, the ruling on the will's validity differs based on which view is adopted. By understanding the underlying principle, you will grasp how a foundational usul distinction shapes a specific fiqh ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational principle
Recognize that the dispute is about the nature of 'itq: is it a right of Allah (ḥaqq Allāh) or a right of the slave (ḥaqq al-'abd)? Understand that this is a usul al-fiqh question about classification of rights.
This principle affects other rulings like acceptance of testimony.
2
Understand the procedural consequence
For rights of Allah, testimony (shahādah) is accepted without a claim (da'wā) from the beneficiary. For rights of the slave, a claim is required. This reveals the underlying rationale.
3
Link to the earlier case of conditional will
Recall the case: a testator says 'my slave is free if bought for 100 dirhams' but the slave is bought for 90. According to the Sahibayn, the will is valid; according to Abu Hanifah, it is void. Connect the change in price to the change in beneficiary.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the validity of the will.
4
State the positions clearly
Imam Abu Hanifah: 'itq is ḥaqq al-'abd, so the specific slave is the beneficiary; when the price changes, the legatee changes, making the will void (batil). Sahibayn: 'itq is ḥaqq Allāh, so the beneficiary (Allah) does not change; the will remains valid (sahih).
Both views are within the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the author's comment
The author states that attributing this dispute to the foundational principle is 'more appropriate' (ashbah). This indicates the strength of the reasoning but does not definitively prefer one view.
The mufta bihi is not specified in this passage.

Source Text

عناق کے حق اللہ اور حق العبد ہونے میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف
وقيل هذه المسالة بناء على اصل اخر مختلف فيه وهوان العتق حق الله تعالى عندهما حتى تقبل الشهادة عليه من غير دعوى فلم يتبدل المستحق وعنده حق العبد حتى لا تقبل البينة عليه من غير دعوى فاختلف المستحق
وهذا اشبه
ترجمہ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مسئلہ بنی ہے ایک دوسری اصل پر جس میں اختلاف کیا گیا ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک عشق اللہ تعالی کا حق ہے یہاں تک کہ اس پر بغیر غلام کے دعوے کے شہادت قبول کر لی جائے گی تو مستحق نہیں بدلا اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک محقق بندہ کا حق ہے یہاں تک کہ اس پر بغیر غلام کے دعوے کے بینہ قبول نہ ہوگا تو مستحق بدل گیا اور یہ (یعنی اس مسئلہ کا اس اصول پر متفرع ہونا ) درستی کے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ تشریح عتاق کے حق اللہ اور حق العبد ہونے میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے، امام صاحب عتاق کو حق العبد قرار دیتے ہیں اور صاحبین حق اللہ قرار دیتے ہیں، حق اللہ کے اندر بالاتفاق شہادت کی قبولیت کے لئے دعوئی شرط نہیں ہے اور حق العبد کے اندر شہادت کی قبولیت کے لئے دعوئی شرط ہے۔ جب یہ اصول معلوم ہو گیا تو یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ اعتماق والا مسئله ای اصول پر متفرع ہے، صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق مثل حج کی وصیت کے حق اللہ ہے اور حق اللہ سحق کے اندر تبدیلی کا سوال نہیں تو اعتناق کے اندر بھی موصی اہ نہیں بدلا ۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ نے اعتاق کوحق العبد قرا دیا ہے تو موضی لڑ کی تبدیلی ظاہر ہے کیونکہ موضی لۂ وہ غلام تھا جس کو سو میں خریدا جائے اور اب موصی لہ وہ ہو گیا جس کو نانوے میں خریدا گیا ہے ، مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ شبہ ہے۔ یعنی یہ کہنا کہ صاحبین اور امام صاحب کا یہ اختلاف اس اصول کے اختلاف پر مبنی ہے کہ عتاق حق اللہ ہے یا حق العبد تو یہ قول صواب
کے زیادہ قریب ہے۔
The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding whether emancipation is a right of Allah or a right of the slave. It was said that this issue is built upon another foundational principle in which there is a difference: according to them (Sahibayn), emancipation is a right of Allah Almighty, such that testimony about it is accepted without a claim, so the beneficiary does not change. According to him (Abu Hanifah), it is a right of the slave, such that evidence about it is not accepted without a claim, so the beneficiary changes. And this attribution is more appropriate. Translation and explanation: There is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding whether emancipation is a right of Allah or a right of the slave. Imam Abu Hanifah considers emancipation a right of the slave, while the Sahibayn consider it a right of Allah. In rights of Allah, a claim is not required for accepting testimony; in rights of the slave, a claim is required. When this principle is understood, it becomes clear that the issue of emancipation is derived from this principle. According to the Sahibayn, emancipation is like a will for Hajj, a right of Allah, and the right of Allah does not change, so the legatee does not change in emancipation. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, emancipation is a right of the slave, so the legatee changes, because the legatee was the slave bought for one hundred and now became the slave bought for ninety. The author said that this attribution is more correct.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage delves deeper into the previous ruling by exploring its underlying legal principle. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the fundamental nature of emancipation ('itq). Imam Abu Hanifah holds that when a master frees a slave, it is primarily a right of the slave (ḥaqq al-‘abd) because it benefits the slave directly. In contrast, the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Ṣāḥibayn), view emancipation as a right of Allah (ḥaqq Allāh) because it is an act of devotion and obedience to God. This difference has practical consequences. For example, in matters of testimony (shahādah/ bayyinah), if 'itq is a right of Allah, testimony is accepted even without a claim from the slave. If it is a right of the slave, a claim is necessary. Returning to the earlier case of the conditional will, the Ṣāḥibayn would argue that since 'itq is a right of Allah, the legatee (Allah) does not change, so the will can be executed for the slave bought at the lower price. Imam Abu Hanifah, considering 'itq a right of the specific slave, says the legatee changed, so the will is invalid. The author comments that the view linking this dispute to the foundational principle of the nature of 'itq is more appropriate (ashbah).

Key Terms
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): A right that belongs to Allah, such as acts of worship and prescribed punishments. In this context, it means that emancipation is primarily for the sake of Allah.
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-‘abd): A right that belongs to the individual servant/slave, such as the benefit of emancipation.
صاحبین (Ṣāḥibayn): The two main disciples of Imam Abu Hanifah: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a testator says 'my slave is free if bought for 100 dirhams' and the slave is bought for 90 dirhams, what is the ruling?
A) The will is void because the legatee changed.
B) The will is valid because emancipation is a right of Allah, so the beneficiary does not change.
C) The will is valid only if the heirs agree.
D) The slave is not freed but must pay the difference.

Key Takeaway
The nature of 'itq (ḥaqq Allāh or ḥaqq al-'abd) is a foundational Hanafi dispute that directly impacts the ruling on conditional wills for emancipation.

Heirs' Permission for Will Exceeding One-Third
Ruling on execution of will beyond one-third when heirs consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a will exceeding one-third and explain how heirs' permission affects its validity.

Core Idea
A will beyond one-third is void only due to heirs' rights; their consent makes it fully valid.

This lesson examines a key ruling in the Hanafi school regarding wills (wasiyyah). The general principle is that a testator may dispose of up to one-third of his estate through a will. However, if he bequeaths more, the excess is not automatically void; it becomes effective if the heirs consent after his death. The following passage from the Hidayah illustrates this principle with the example of a slave freed in death illness, where heirs' permission eliminates the need for the slave to work off the excess value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Emancipation of a slave in death illness is treated as a will (wasiyyah). The passage gives a ruling on its validity.
2
Identify the one-third limit
Calculate the total estate: 100 dirhams + slave worth 100 dirhams = 200 dirhams. One-third is 66.66 dirhams. The will (emancipation) exceeds this limit by 33.34 dirhams.
Normally, the will would only be effective up to one-third, requiring the slave to work off the excess (sa'y).
3
Recognize the condition for exceeding one-third
The heirs (two sons) grant permission after the testator's death. This permission makes the entire will valid.
The prohibition on exceeding one-third exists to protect the heirs' shares; by consenting, they waive this right.
4
Apply to the scenario
With full consent, the slave is completely free without any obligation to work (sa'y). The will is executed in its entirety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن ترك ابنين ومائة درهم وعبد اقيمته مائة وقد كان اعتقه في مرضه فاجازا لوارثان ذلك لم يسع في شئى لان العتق فى مرض الموت وان كان فى حكم الوصية وقد وقعت باكثر من الثلث الا انها تجوز با جازة الورثة لان الامتناع لحقهم وقد اسقطوه
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے دو بیٹے اور سودراہم ( ترکہ ) میں چھوڑے اور ایک غلام جس کی قیمت سو درہم ہے اور اس نے اس کو اپنے مرض الموت میں آزاد کیا تھا پس دونوں وارثوں نے اس کی اجازت دیدی تو غلام کچھ کمائی نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ مرض الموت میں عشق اگر چہ وصیت کے حکم میں ہے اور وصیت ثلث سے زیادہ میں واقع ہوئی ہے مگر وہ ( ثلث سے زیادہ کی وصیت ) ورثا کی اجازت سے جائز ہے اس لئے کہ امتناع انھیں کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا اور انھوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا ہے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں یہ بات بار بار گزر چکی ہے کہ وصیت کے نفاذ کا محل ثلث مال ہے البتہ اگر نٹ سے زیادہ وصیت کی گئی ہو اور ورثا نے اس کی اجازت دیدی ہو تو ثلث سے زیادہ کی وصیت بھی نافذ ہو جائے گی اسی اصول مذکورہ کی ایک جزئی یہاں پیش کی
جا رہی ہے کہ، زید کا انتقال ہوا اور اس نے دو بیٹے وارث چھوڑے اور ترکہ میں سو دراہم اور ایک غلام چھوڑا جس کی قیمت سو درہم ہے اور زید نے اس غلام کو اپنے مرض الموت میں آزاد کر دیا تھا تو قاعدہ میں اس کی آزادی ثلث مال میں جاری ہوگی یعنی ۴ ۶۶ در اہم لیکن اگر دونوں لڑکوں نے پوری وصیت کے نفاذ کی اجازت دیدی تو وصیت نافذ ہو جائے گی اور غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور غلام پر کچھ کمائی کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہ حق مرض الموت میں ہونے کی وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے اور وصیت ثلث سے زیادہ میں نافذ نہیں ہوا کرتی لیکن اگر ورثاء اجازت دیدیں تو نافذ ہوتی ہے کیونکہ وصیت کا عدم نفاذ ورثا کے حق کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور یہاں ورثا نے اجازت دیدی تو انھوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا ہے۔
He (Muhammad) said: Whoever leaves two sons and one hundred dirhams and a slave valued at one hundred dirhams, and he had freed him in his death illness, and the two heirs permit that, the slave does not work (to earn his freedom) because emancipation in death illness is considered a will, and it occurred beyond one-third, but it is valid with the permission of the heirs because the prohibition was for their right, and they have dropped it. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever leaves two sons and one hundred dirhams in inheritance, and a slave whose value is one hundred dirhams, and he freed him in his death illness, then both heirs grant permission, so the slave will not have to work (for compensation) because emancipation in death illness is in the category of a will, and the will occurred beyond one-third, but it (the will beyond one-third) is valid with the permission of the heirs because the prohibition was due to their right, and they have dropped their right. Explanation: It has been repeatedly mentioned that the domain of execution of a will is one-third of the estate. However, if a will is made for more than one-third and the heirs give permission, then the will beyond one-third also becomes effective. A specific application of this principle is presented here: Zayd dies, leaving two sons as heirs, and the estate consists of one hundred dirhams and a slave worth one hundred dirhams. Zayd freed the slave in his death illness. As a rule, the emancipation would be effective only up to one-third of the estate (66.66 dirhams). But if both sons grant permission for full execution, the will is enforced, the slave becomes free, and no work (for compensation) is required from him because this is in the category of a death illness will, and wills beyond one-third are not normally effective, but if the heirs permit, it becomes effective because the non-execution was due to the heirs' right, and they have dropped it.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah provides a clear example of a fundamental rule in Islamic inheritance of wills: a will (waṣiyyah) can only be executed from up to one-third (thulth) of the testator's estate. If the testator bequeaths more than one-third, the excess is void unless the heirs (warathah) give their consent after the testator's death. Here, a man dies leaving 100 dirhams and a slave worth 100 dirhams (total estate 200 dirhams). He had freed the slave in his death illness, which counts as a will. Since the slave's value (100) exceeds one-third of the estate (66.66), normally the emancipation would only be effective to the extent of 66.66 dirhams, requiring the slave to work off the remaining value (i.e., earn his freedom by paying the balance). However, the two sons (heirs) give permission for the full emancipation. Once they consent, the full will is executed, the slave is completely free, and no service (sa'y) is required. The reason is that the restriction on giving more than one-third exists to protect the heirs' share. When the heirs voluntarily waive their right, the will becomes effective. This is a classic illustration of the rule 'al-ḥaqqu idhā usqaṭa usqaṭa' (when a right is dropped, it is dropped).

Key Terms
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum amount a testator may dispose of through a will without heirs' permission.
اجازة الورثة (ijāzatu al-warathah): Permission granted by the heirs after the testator's death for a will exceeding one-third to be executed.
سعى (sa'y): Effort or work required from a slave to earn part of his value when emancipation is incomplete due to the one-third limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator in death illness frees a slave worth 100 dirhams, and his estate is 200 dirhams with two sons as heirs who give permission, what is the ruling?
A) The slave is freed but must work to pay 33.34 dirhams.
B) The slave is not freed because it exceeds one-third.
C) The slave is fully freed without any work required.
D) The heirs can decide to free the slave only if they receive compensation.

Key Takeaway
A will exceeding one-third is valid upon heirs' consent; the one-third limit protects heirs' rights, which they may waive.

Effect of Slave's Crime on Will for Emancipation
Ruling on will for emancipation when slave commits crime after testator's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a will for emancipation when the slave commits a crime after the testator's death, and distinguish between the effect of handover (daf‘) vs ransom (fidā).

Core Idea
The victim's right supersedes the testator's; handover voids the will, ransom saves it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a conflict of rights: the testator's will to free his slave versus the crime victim's claim against the slave. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explains that the outcome depends on whether the slave is handed over to the victim or the heirs pay ransom. Understanding this distinction reveals a key principle in Hanafi law—priority of rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
After the testator's death, the slave commits a crime. Two possible actions: either the slave is handed over (daf‘) to the victim's guardian, or the heirs pay ransom (fidā). These lead to different rulings on the will.
The slave may or may not already be handed over before ransom.
2
Analyze the effect of handover
When the slave is handed over, he leaves the testator's ownership. Since the will requires the slave to be owned at execution, the will becomes void. The victim's right takes precedence over the testator's right.
Handover is analogous to a sale by the testator or heir.
3
Analyze the effect of ransom by heirs
If the heirs pay ransom from their own wealth, the slave is purified from the crime as if it never occurred. The slave remains in the testator's estate, and the will becomes valid and executable.
The ransom is a separate transaction that reverses the handover's effect.
4
Understand the analogy to sale
The ruling equates handover to a sale: just as selling the slave by the testator (or heir after death) voids the will, so does handover. This is a clear analogy (qiyās jaliyy) based on the common illa: loss of ownership through a superior right.
The illa is 'leaving the testator's ownership due to a prior/stronger right.'
5
Apply the principle of priority of rights
The victim's right to the slave (or its value) is stronger than the testator's right to free him, because the crime creates an immediate liability. The testator's right is only contingent upon execution. Thus, the stronger right prevails.
This principle applies in other areas of fiqh, e.g., debts vs. bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موصی نے غلام کو آزاد کرنے کی وصیت کی پھر مر گیا اس کے بعد غلام نے کوئی ایسی جنایت کی جس کے عوض لوگوں نے اس غلام کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا پھر ورثا ء خود ہی اس غلام کا فدیہ ادا کر دیں تو کیا حکم ہے
قال و من اوصى بعتق عبده ثم مات فجنى جناية ودفع بها بطلت الوصية لان الدفع قد صح لما ان حق ولى الجناية مقدم على حق الموصى فكذلك على حق الموصى له لانه يتلقى الملك من جهته الا ان ملكه فيه باق وانما يزول بالدفع فاذا خرج به عن ملكه بطلت الوصية كما اذا باعه الموصى او وارثه بعد موته فان فداه الورثة كان الفداء فى ما لهم لا نهم هم الذين التزموه وجازت الوصية لان العبد طهر عن الجناية بالفداء كانه لم يجن فتنفذ الوصية
A testator made a will to free his slave, then he died. After that, the slave committed a crime for which the people handed him over to the guardian of the crime. Then the heirs themselves paid the ransom for the slave. What is the ruling? He (Muhammad) said: Whoever makes a will to free his slave, then dies, then the slave commits a crime and is handed over for it, the will is void because the handover is valid since the right of the guardian of the crime takes precedence over the right of the testator, and similarly over the right of the legatee, because the legatee receives ownership from him (the testator). However, the testator's ownership of the slave remains and is only removed by handover. When [the slave] leaves his (the testator's) ownership by handover, the will is void, just as if the testator or his heir sold him after his death. If the heirs pay ransom, the payment is from their own wealth because they are the ones who undertook it, and the will becomes valid because the slave is purified from the crime by the ransom, as if he did not commit it, so the will is executed.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses a scenario where a will to free a slave is made, but before the will is executed, the slave commits a crime (jināyah) that leads to him being handed over (daf‘) to the victim's guardian (walī al-jināyah). The ruling is that the handover voids the will because the guardian's right to the slave takes precedence over the testator's right (and the legatee's right, since the legatee derives ownership from the testator). Even though the testator has passed away, his ownership of the slave continues until the handover, and once the slave leaves his ownership through the handover, the will has no effect. This is analogous to the testator selling the slave before death, or an heir selling after death. However, if the heirs choose to pay the ransom (fidyah) from their own wealth to free the slave from liability, then the will becomes valid because the ransom wipes out the crime, and the slave can be freed per the will. The key principle is that the right of the crime victim (or guardian) takes priority over the rights of the testator and legatee. The analogy with sale (bay‘) is used: just as a sale by the testator would void the will, so does a judicial handover for a crime.

Key Terms
دفع (daf‘): Handing over the slave to the victim or his guardian as a result of the crime committed by the slave.
فدى (fadā): Ransom paid by the heirs to free the slave from liability for the crime.
ولي الجناية (walī al-jināyah): The guardian of the crime victim, who has the right to claim compensation or demand the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator makes a will to free his slave, then dies, and the slave commits a crime and is handed over to the guardian, what happens to the will?
A) The will remains valid because it was made before the crime.
B) The will is void because the slave left the testator's ownership.
C) The will is still valid but the slave must serve the guardian first.
D) The will becomes valid only if the heirs pay a fine.

Key Takeaway
A will for emancipation is void if the slave is handed over for a crime, but revived if the heirs pay ransom.

Heirs' Permission Validates Bequest Exceeding One-Third
Ruling on bequest exceeding one-third validated by heirs' permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a bequest exceeding one-third becomes fully valid when heirs permit it, and state the consequence for the freed slave.

Core Idea
Heirs' permission removes their own right, making a bequest exceeding one-third fully valid without compensation.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case where a dying man frees a slave worth the entire estate. The emancipation exceeds the one-third limit, but the two sons who inherit both give permission. We will see how Hanafi law resolves this, focusing on the legal reasoning: the prohibition is for heirs' benefit, so their consent lifts it entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act in question? (Emancipation in terminal illness). Does it exceed one-third? What is the initial ruling? (Exceeded, so normally invalid beyond one-third).
The slave's value equals the entire estate, so the bequest is 200 dirhams, one-third is 66.66, thus exceeds.
2
Understand the legal impediment
Why is a bequest exceeding one-third normally invalid? The text says 'because the prevention is due to their right' – the heirs have a right to their shares.
The prohibition is not absolute; it is for the protection of heirs.
3
Analyze the effect of heirs' permission
What do the heirs do? They permit (اجازة). What is the legal effect? The bequest becomes valid (تجوز). How? The heirs have waived their right (أسقطوه).
The permission is given after death, and it is effective in Hanafi law.
4
Recognize the consequence (no istis'a)
What happens to the slave? He does not have to work (لم يسع في شيء). Why? Because the impediment is removed completely.
Istis'a (earning to compensate) is not required; the slave is fully free.
5
Compare with Shafi'i position
How does the Shafi'i school differ? They hold that permission after death is invalid because the bequest was void ab initio. The Hanafi view is that the bequest is suspended (mawquf).
This difference leads to a practical difference: Hanafi allows the bequest fully if heirs consent; Shafi'i does not.

قال ومن ترك ابنين ومائة درهم وعبد اقيمته مائة وقد كان اعتقه في مرضه فاجازا لوارثان ذلك لم يسع في شئى لان العتق فى مرض الموت وان كان فى حكم الوصية وقد وقعت باكثر من الثلث الا انها تجوز با جازة الورثة لان الامتناع لحقهم وقد اسقطوه
He (Muhammad) said: And whoever leaves two sons and one hundred dirhams and a slave whose value is one hundred, and he had freed him in his illness, and both heirs permit that, the slave does not strive for anything, because emancipation during terminal illness is in the ruling of a bequest, and it occurred exceeding one-third, but it is valid by the permission of the heirs, because the prevention is due to their right and they have dropped it.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad on the interaction between bequest (wasiyya) and inheritance rights. The case involves a man who, in his terminal illness, frees a slave worth one hundred dirhams while his estate totals only one hundred dirhams plus the slave (total 200 dirhams). The emancipation, treated as a bequest, exceeds the legal one-third limit (66.66 dirhams). Normally such a bequest would be invalid beyond one-third unless heirs consent. Here both sons (the only heirs) permit the emancipation. The ruling is that the slave is free without needing to work (istis'a) to compensate the estate, because the heirs' voluntary permission removes their right to object. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is: prohibition of bequest beyond one-third exists solely to protect heirs' shares; when heirs themselves waive this right, the bequest becomes fully effective. This is a standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
إجازة الورثة (ijazat al-warathah): Heirs' voluntary permission given after the testator's death to allow a bequest exceeding one-third.
عتق في مرض الموت (itq fi marad al-mawt): Emancipation of a slave during terminal illness, treated as a bequest (wasiyya) for the purpose of the one-third limit.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion available for bequests without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the freed slave not have to work (istis'a) after the heirs permit the emancipation exceeding one-third?
A) Because the slave is too valuable to work.
B) Because heirs' permission removes the legal impediment, so the bequest is fully valid from the start.
C) Because the testator's debt prevented istis'a.
D) Because the emancipation was in health, not illness.

Key Takeaway
Heirs' permission (ijazah) after death makes a bequest exceeding one-third fully valid, and the beneficiary (freed slave) does not need to compensate.

Slave's Crime After Bequest of Freedom: Handover Voids, Ransom Restores
Ruling on bequest to free a slave who commits a crime after testator's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave subject to a bequest of freedom commits a crime after the testator's death, and distinguish between the effects of handover (voiding bequest) and ransom (preserving bequest).

Core Idea
Handover voids the bequest; ransom from heirs' wealth restores it.

A bequest to free a slave after death can be complicated if the slave commits a crime before freedom is executed. The victim's right to compensation takes precedence. This lesson explains how the heirs' actions—handing over the slave or paying ransom—determine whether the bequest remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator dies, leaving a bequest to free a specific slave. After death, the slave commits a crime (jinayah) against a third party.
The crime creates a claim for the victim or guardian (wali al-jinayah).
2
Understand the effect of handover
If the heirs hand over the slave to the guardian as compensation, the bequest becomes void. Reason: handover transfers ownership out of the estate, analogous to a sale.
The guardian's right takes precedence over the beneficiary's right.
3
Understand the effect of ransom
If the heirs ransom the slave from the guardian using their own wealth, the bequest is valid. The ransom purifies the slave of liability, as if no crime occurred.
Ransom is from heirs' personal funds, not the estate.
4
Note the legal analogy
Handover is equated to a sale by the testator or heir after death—both remove ownership and nullify the bequest. Ransom is akin to clearing a debt, preserving the bequest.
This analogy (qiyas) underpins the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و من اوصى بعتق عبده ثم مات فجنى جناية ودفع بها بطلت الوصية لان الدفع قد صح لما ان حق ولى الجناية مقدم على حق الموصى فكذلك على حق الموصى له لانه يتلقى الملك من جهته الا ان ملكه فيه باق وانما يزول بالدفع فاذا خرج به عن ملكه بطلت الوصية كما اذا باعه الموصى او وارثه بعد موته فان فداه الورثة كان الفداء فى ما لهم لا نهم هم الذين التزموه وجازت الوصية لان العبد طهر عن الجناية بالفداء كانه لم يجن فتنفذ الوصية
He said: And whoever makes a bequest to free his slave, then dies, then the slave commits a crime and is handed over for it, the bequest becomes void, because the handover is valid since the right of the crime guardian takes precedence over the right of the testator, and likewise over the right of the beneficiary, because he receives ownership from him, except that his ownership in him remains and is only removed by handover. So when he leaves his ownership by it, the bequest becomes void, just as if the testator or his heir after his death sold him. And if the heirs ransom him, the ransom is from their wealth because they undertook it, and the bequest is valid because the slave is purified from the crime by the ransom, as if he did not commit a crime, so the bequest is executed.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex scenario in bequest law. A testator (musi) directs in his will that his slave be freed after his death. After the testator's death, the slave commits a jinaya (crime or tort) against a third party. The victim's guardian (wali al-jinaya) has the right to take the slave as compensation (or to demand ransom). If the heirs hand over the slave to the guardian, the bequest of freedom becomes void. Reason: the guardian's right is superior to both the testator's right and the beneficiary's right. The slave was still owned by the testator's estate at death; handing him over transfers ownership out of the estate, thus nullifying the bequest (analogous to selling the slave). However, if the heirs voluntarily pay ransom (fida) to the guardian to free the slave from liability, that ransom is at their own expense (not from the estate), and the bequest is valid because the slave is cleared of the crime. The slave is then freed per the bequest. This ruling highlights the precedence of creditors' and tort victims' rights over bequests.

Key Terms
جنایت (jinayah): A crime or tort committed by the slave that imposes liability on his owner (the estate) for compensation.
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave to the victim's guardian as compensation for the crime.
فداء (fida'): Ransom paid by the heirs to the victim's guardian to free the slave from liability.
ولي الجناية (wali al-jinayah): The victim or guardian entitled to compensation for the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the bequest become void when the slave is handed over to the crime guardian, but not when the heirs ransom him?
A) Handover transfers ownership out of the estate; ransom is a payment that does not remove ownership until paid.
B) The heirs' ransom is voluntary and shows they have waived their objection.
C) Handover is equivalent to sale; ransom is equivalent to forgiveness.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
Handover voids the bequest because it transfers ownership; ransom from heirs' wealth restores it.

Effect of Slave's Crime on Will for Manumission
Ruling on will for manumission when slave commits crime, with qiyas and Q&A expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a will for manumission when the slave is surrendered for a crime, and apply the qiyas jali to determine the outcome when the heirs pay ransom.

Core Idea
A will to free a slave is void if the slave is surrendered for a crime, but valid if the heirs voluntarily ransom him.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in wills: when a testator bequeaths freedom to a slave, but after the testator's death the slave commits a crime. The Hanafi school distinguishes between compulsory surrender and voluntary ransom. We will follow Imam Muhammad's reasoning, which uses qiyas to the case of sale, and understand the precise moment when the will becomes void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
State the ruling: if the slave is surrendered to the crime victim's guardian, the will for manumission becomes void. If the heirs voluntarily pay the ransom, the will remains valid.
The ruling is conditional on whether the slave is handed over or ransomed.
2
Understand the Rationale
The right of the crime victim (or his guardian) takes precedence over the testator's right and the legatee's right. When the slave is surrendered, ownership passes from the testator's estate, voiding the will.
The testator's ownership must persist until the will is executed.
3
Examine the Qiyas
The surrender is analogous to a sale after death: both transfer ownership away from the testator. The illa (effective cause) is removal of the testator's ownership.
Qiyas jali: clear analogy because the ruling in the asl (sale) is established.
4
Consider the Exception
If heirs voluntarily pay ransom, they do so from their own wealth as charity. The slave is treated as if no crime occurred, so the will is executed from the one-third.
The ransom is not obligatory; it is a voluntary act that removes the liability.

ہوتی ہے وہ موصی کی جہت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ سوال یہ آپ نے کہاں سے فرمادیا کہ جب غلام ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا گیا تو وصیت باطل ہوگئی مناسب یہ تھا کہ آپ یوں فرماتے کہ غلام کو ولی جنایت کے سپرد کرنے سے Book of Wills. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever makes a will for the manumission of his slave, then the testator dies, then the slave commits a crime and the compensation for the crime is given, then the will becomes void because giving (the slave) is correct, because the guardian of the crime's right takes precedence over the testator's right, and similarly over the legatee's right because the legatee acquires ownership from the testator's side, but the testator's ownership remains in the slave, and ownership is removed by giving (the slave). So when ownership is removed by giving, the will becomes void, just as if the testator or his heir sold him after the testator's death. Then if the heirs pay the ransom for the slave, the ransom will be from the heirs' wealth because they have undertaken it, and the will is valid because the slave becomes free of the crime due to paying the ransom, as if he did not commit the crime, so the will is executed. Explanation: Zaid made a will during his terminal illness that this slave of mine be freed, and Zaid died, and this slave is within one-third of the wealth, but the slave committed a crime whereby the slave had to be handed over to the guardian of the crime. Then the mentioned will becomes void because here it is valid for the heirs to hand over the slave to the guardian of the crime because the guardian's right takes precedence over the testator's right, and a fortiori over the legatee's right because the ownership the legatee obtains is established from the testator's side. Question: Where did you say that when the slave is handed over to the guardian of the crime, the will becomes void? It would be appropriate for you to say that the will becomes void before handing over the slave to the guardian of the crime? Answer: As long as the slave is not handed over to the guardian of the crime, the testator's ownership remains in him, and when he is handed over to the guardian of the crime, then the testator's ownership is removed and the will becomes void. Just as if the testator himself sold this slave, the will would become void because by the testator's selling, his ownership is removed. And after the testator's death, if due to debt on the deceased, the testator's heir paid the ransom for this slave, then this will also become void. The heir has the right to hand over the slave for the crime debt, but if later he pays the ransom for this slave, then this ransom will be on the wealth of the heirs, and this ransom will be considered a charitable payment because paying this ransom was not obligatory upon them; they gave it voluntarily. Therefore, the testator's will is valid, because by paying the ransom the slave becomes pure and free from the crime, as if he did not commit any crime. Hence, there remains no obstacle to executing the will, so the will will be executed.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by an explanatory expansion (sharh). The author, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, states the ruling: If a person makes a will to free a slave, and after the testator's death the slave commits a crime for which he is surrendered to the legal guardian (wali al-jinayah) as compensation, then the will becomes void. The reasoning is that the right of the crime victim takes precedence over both the testator's right and the legatee's right. The analogy is drawn to the case where the testator or his heirs sell the slave after death—ownership is transferred and the will is voided. However, if the heirs voluntarily pay the ransom (fidyah) to redeem the slave from the crime, then the will remains valid because the slave is treated as if no crime occurred, and the ransom is considered the heirs' own charity, not an obligation. The commentary then engages in a question-answer format: clarifying that the will is not void until actual surrender occurs, because the testator's ownership persists until then. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a will is contingent on the testator's continuing ownership of the bequeathed property at the time of death and until execution. The text also notes that if the heirs pay the ransom after surrender, they do so voluntarily, and the will is then executed.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will, valid up to one-third of the estate.
جنایت (jinayah): A crime committed by the slave, making him liable for compensation (damages).
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom paid to redeem the slave from liability for the crime.
ولی جنایت (wali al-jinayah): The legal guardian or claimant of the crime victim (or his heirs) entitled to compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The will becomes void because the ransom is a debt on the estate.
B) The will remains valid and the slave is freed from the bequest.
C) The will is suspended until the crime is fully adjudicated.
D) The will becomes void because the heirs interfered.

Key Takeaway
A will for manumission is void if the slave is surrendered for a crime, but valid if the heirs voluntarily ransom the slave, as the ransom removes the liability without affecting the testator's ownership.

Dispute on Timing of Manumission: Heir's Statement Accepted Unless Evidence
Ruling on conflicting claims of legatee and heir about when slave was freed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of evidence (bayyinah on claimant) to resolve disputes between legatee and heir regarding the timing of manumission in a will.

Core Idea
When legatee and heir disagree on whether a slave was freed in health or illness, the heir's claim is accepted unless the legatee proves otherwise.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi ruling on a conflict over the timing of a slave's manumission by a testator. The legatee claims the freeing occurred in health (making it effective from the entire estate, which would reduce the estate for the will), while the heir claims it was in terminal illness (making it a will from the one-third). The ruling hinges on the fundamental procedural principle that the claimant must provide evidence, and the denier's statement with an oath is accepted. By studying this case, you will learn how the Hanafi school applies the maxim 'al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
There are two parties: the legatee (musa lahu) and the heir. The legatee claims the slave was freed in health, so the manumission is not a will and reduces the entire estate. The heir claims the freeing was in illness, making it a will from the one-third, thus taking priority over the legatee's bequest.
The legatee's claim aims to increase his share; the heir's claim aims to limit it.
2
Determine who is the claimant (mudda'i) and who is the denier (munkir)
The legatee is the claimant because he asserts a right (entitlement to one-third of what remains after freeing from the entire estate) that the heir denies. The heir is the denier because his claim (freeing in illness) contradicts the legatee's assertion.
In Hanafi fiqh, the burden of proof is on the claimant.
3
Apply the evidence rule
The established rule is: 'Al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara' (Evidence is upon the claimant, and the oath is upon the denier). Therefore, the legatee must provide proof (bayyinah) of freeing in health. If he fails, the heir's statement is accepted upon taking an oath.
The ruling does not require the heir to prove his claim; denial with an oath suffices.
4
Conclude the default ruling and exception
The default ruling is that the heir's statement is accepted. The legatee gets nothing from the one-third unless (a) something remains after the freeing in illness is executed from the one-third, or (b) the legatee produces evidence that the freeing was in health.
If the legatee brings evidence, his claim prevails and the freeing is from the entire estate.

Source Text

ومن اوصى بثلث ماله لاخر فاقر الموصى له والوراث ان الميت اعتق هذا العبد فقال الموصى له اعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث اعتقه فى المرض فالقول قول الوارث ولا شي للموصى له الا ان يفضل من الثلث شي او تقوم له البينة ان العتق في الصحة ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے ثلث مال کی کسی دوسرے شخص کے لئے وصیت کی پس موضی لہ اور وارث نے اقرار کیا کہ میت نے اس غلام کو آزاد کیا ہے پس موصی لڑ نے کہا کہ اس کو صحبت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور وارث نے کہا کہ اس کو مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے تو وارث کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور موصی لیڈ کے لئے کچھ نہ ہو گا مگر یہ کہ ثلث سے کچھ ٹی بچ جائے یا موضی لا کے لئے مبینہ قائم ہو جائے کہ عتق حالت صحت میں ہوا ہے۔ تشریح زید مرحوم نے خالد کے لئے اپنے ثلث مال کی وصیت کی اور زید کا ایک غلام ہے خالد اور زید کا وارث اس بات کا اقرار کرتے ہیں کہ زید نے اس کو آزاد کیا ہے، البتہ ان دونوں کا اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ کب آزاد کیا ہے۔ خالد تو کہتا ہے کہ حالت صحت میں آزاد کیا ہے اور وارث کہتا ہے کہ حالت مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے، خالد کے کہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ غلام صحت کی حالت میں آزاد کیا گیا ہے تو یہ وصیت کے درجہ میں نہیں ہے لہذا پورے مال سے اس کا عشق نافذ ہوگا اور جو مال باقی ہے اس کے ثلث کا میں مستحق ہوں ، اور زید کا وارث کہتا ہے کہ زید نے اس کو حالت مرض میں آزاد کیا ہے اور حالت مرض کا اعتاق وصیت سے مقدم ہے اور اس کا نفاذ ثلث مال میں ہوتا ہے اور عتق دیگر وصایا سے مقدم ہوتا ہے لہذا خالد کے حق سے مقدم ہوگا۔ تو ثلث سے اولاً غلام کا عتق نافذ ہوگا اگر غلام کی آزادی کے بعد ثث میں سے کچھ بیچ جائے تو وہ خالد کو ملے گا اور اگر نہ بچے تو نہیں ملے گا تو یہاں کس کا قول معتبر ہو گا ؟ فرمایا کہ اگر خالد اپنے دعوے پر مبینہ قائم کر دے تو خالد کا قول معتبر ہو گا ورنہ وارث کا قول معتبر ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہاں خالد مدعی ہے ساور وارث منکر ہے اور مدعی کا فریضہ ہے کہ وہ گواہ قائم کرے ورنہ مع الیمین منکر کا قول معتبر ہوا کرتا ہے ،لہذا فر ماتے ہیں۔ موصی لہ مدعی اور وارث منکر ہے اور منکر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے لان الموصى له يدعى استحقاق ثلث ما بقى من التركة بعد العتق لان العتق فى الصحة ليس بوصية ولهذا ينفذ من جميع المال والوارث ينكره لان مدعاه العتق فى المرض وهو وصية والعتق فى المرض مقدم على الوصية بثلث المال فكان منكرا والقول قول المنكر مع اليمين
A person made a will of one-third of his wealth for someone. The legatee and the heir both acknowledged that the deceased freed this slave. The legatee said he freed him in health, and the heir said he freed him in illness. Whose statement is accepted? He said: And whoever makes a will of one-third of his wealth for another, then the legatee and the heir acknowledge that the deceased freed this slave. The legatee said, 'He freed him in health,' and the heir said, 'He freed him in illness.' Then the heir's statement is accepted, and there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from the one-third or he provides evidence that the freeing was in health. Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever makes a will of one-third of his wealth for another person, then the legatee and the heir acknowledge that the deceased freed this slave. Then the legatee said that he freed him in health, and the heir said that he freed him in illness. Then the heir's statement is accepted, and there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from the one-third or the legatee establishes evidence that the freeing was in health. Explanation: The deceased Zaid made a will of one-third of his wealth for Khalid. Zaid had a slave. Khalid and Zaid's heir both acknowledge that Zaid freed this slave, but they differ on when he freed him. Khalid says he freed him in health, and the heir says he freed him in illness. Khalid's meaning is that this slave was freed in health, so it is not a will; therefore it is executed from the entire wealth, and I am entitled to one-third of the remaining wealth. Zaid's heir says that Zaid freed him in illness, and freeing in illness takes precedence over a will; it is executed from one-third of the wealth, and freeing takes precedence over other bequests, so it takes precedence over Khalid's right. So from the one-third, the slave's freeing is executed first. If after the freeing something remains from the one-third, it goes to Khalid; if nothing remains, he gets nothing. So whose statement is accepted? He said: If Khalid establishes evidence for his claim, then Khalid's statement is accepted; otherwise the heir's statement is accepted, because here Khalid is the claimant and the heir is the denier. The claimant's duty is to produce witnesses; otherwise with the oath, the denier's statement is accepted. Therefore they said: The legatee is the claimant and the heir is the denier, and the denier's statement with an oath is accepted, because the legatee claims entitlement to one-third of what remains of the estate after the freeing, because freeing in health is not a will and therefore is executed from all the wealth, and the heir denies that because his claim is that the freeing was in illness, which is a will, and freeing in illness takes precedence over the will of one-third of the wealth; so he is a denier, and the statement of the denier with an oath is accepted.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a conflict between a legatee (wasiyyah recipient) and an heir regarding the timing of a slave's manumission by the testator. The legatee claims the slave was freed in health (so the manumission is effective from the entire estate, reducing the estate for the legatee's one-third share), while the heir claims the freeing occurred during the testator's terminal illness (so it is treated as a will, executed from one-third, and takes precedence over other bequests). The ruling states that the heir's statement is taken as true, unless the legatee provides evidence (bayyinah) that the freeing was in health. The reasoning is based on the legal principle that the claimant (mudda'i) must present proof, and the denier (munkir) has his statement accepted with an oath. Here, the legatee is the claimant because he seeks a larger share of the estate (one-third after the freeing), while the heir is the denier since he claims the freeing was a will that consumes part of the one-third. This aligns with the Hanafi maxim: al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara. The commentary elaborates on the implications: if the freeing was in health, it is not a will and is executed from the entire estate; if in illness, it is a will and is limited to one-third, taking priority over the legatee's bequest. The passage thus resolves the dispute by defaulting to the heir's claim unless the legatee can prove otherwise.

Key Terms
موصی لہ (musa lahu): The legatee, the person in whose favor the will is made.
مدعی (mudda'i): The claimant who asserts a right that the other party denies.
منکر (munkir): The denier who refutes the claimant's assertion.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.
عتق (itq): Manumission of a slave; freeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute where the legatee claims the slave was freed in health and the heir claims in illness, what is the default ruling?
A) The legatee's claim is accepted because he is the beneficiary.
B) The heir's claim is accepted unless the legatee produces evidence.
C) The slave is freed from both shares equally.
D) The matter is referred to a judge who decides based on looks.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule that the claimant must bring evidence and the denier's statement with oath is accepted resolves disputes over the timing of manumission: the heir's claim defaults unless the legatee proves the freeing was in health.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
advanced
8 min
Dispute on Slave's Sa'y When Heir Confirms Both Freedom and Debt
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sa'y with heir's confirmation of debt and emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on sa'y when the heir confirms both emancipation and debt, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Debt's priority imposes sa'y per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn say simultaneous confirmation places both in health, so no sa'y.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute from the Book of Wills (Kitab al-Wasaya). The scenario involves a deceased who leaves only a slave, and both the slave and a creditor make claims against the estate. The heir confirms both. The central question is whether the slave must work to pay his value (sa'y). All agree the slave is freed, but the scholars differ on the obligation of sa'y. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi usul principles of priority (asbaq) and strength (aqwa) interact with the irrevocability of emancipation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa holds that sa'y is wajib; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is not wajib.
Remember: the slave is freed in both views; the dispute is only about sa'y.
2
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their reasoning: the heir's single confirmation makes the emancipation and debt appear simultaneously, both attributed to health. The rule that emancipation in health does not impose sa'y applies, even with debt.
They consider both claims as coexisting from the start.
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa's first proof
Debt acknowledgment is stronger (aqwa) because it affects the entire estate, while illness-era emancipation is limited to one-third. The stronger should repel the weaker, but emancipation cannot be annulled, so it is repelled by imposing sa'y.
This uses the qawida: al-aqwa yadfa' al-ad'na.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's second proof
Debt is prior (asbaq) because it can be attributed to health without obstacle. Emancipation cannot be attributed to health because debt prevents gratuitous emancipation in illness. Hence sa'y is wajib.
Priority in attribution leads to practical consequence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: Abu Hanifa's view requires the slave to work; Sahibayn's frees him without obligation. Later authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) prefer the Sahibayn, so the mufta bihi is no sa'y.
Despite being Zahir al-Riwayah, the later tarjih favours the Sahibayn.
