كتاب الوصايا
ہو جائے وہ ایسی ہے جیسے معامیہ ثابت ہوئی ہو۔
سوال امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک تو عشق حق العبد ہے لہذا جب تک غلام کی طرف سے دعوئی نہ ہو تو اقامت بعینہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟ جواب یہاں ہم نے غلام کو مدعی نہیں ٹھہرایا ہے بلکہ مدعی موضی لہ ہے اور موضی لہ ہی وارث کا خصم ہے نہ کہ غلام اور اس کی جانب سے دعوئی موجود ہے اور دعوے کے بعد اقامت بینہ درست ہے کیونکہ جہاں خالد کو ضرورت ہے کہ وہ اپنا حق ثابت کرے تو اقامت بینہ کے سلسلہ میں موضی راہی کو خصم ٹھہرایا جائے گا۔
وارث کا عشق کا دعویٰ کرنے والے غلام اور دین کا دعوی کرنے والے کی تصدیق کا حکم ، اقوال فقہاء قال ومن ترك عبدا فقال للوارث اعتقني ابوك فى الصحة وقال رجل لى علی ابیک الف درهم فقال صدقتما فان العبد يسعى فى قيمة عند ابي حنيفة وقالا يعتق ولا يسعى فى شى لان الدين والعتق في الصحة ظهرا معا بتصديق الوارث فى كلام واحد فصارا كانهما كانا معا والعتق في الصحة لا يوجب السعاية وان كان
على المعتق دين
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے ایک غلام چھوڑا اپس اس غلام نے وارث سے کہا کہ مجھ کو تیرے باپ نے حالت صحت میں آزاد کر دیا تھا اور ایک شخص نے کہا کہ میرا تیرے باپ پر ہزار درہم قرض ہے پس وارث نے کہا کہ تم نے صحیح کہا پس غلام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اپنی قیمت میں کمائی کرے گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ غلام آزاد ہوگا اور کچھ کمائی نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ قرض اور عشق صحت میں دونوں ایک ساتھ ظاہر ہوئے ہیں وارث کے ایک کلام میں تصدیق کرنے کی وجہ سے تو یہ دونوں ایسے ہو گئے گویا کہ یہ دونوں ایک ساتھ تھے اور حالت صحت میں عشق کمائی کو واجب نہیں کرتا اگر چہ معتق پر قرض ہو ۔ تشریح زید کا انتقال ہوا اور ترکہ میں فقط ایک غلام چھوڑا، اس غلام نے وارث سے کہا کہ مجھ کو تیرے باپ نے حالت صحت میں آزاد کر دیا تھا اور کسی اور شخص نے کہا کہ میرا تیرے باپ پر قرض ہے جس کی مقدار ہزار درہم ہے، تو وارث نے ان دونوں کے جواب میں کہا کہ تم دونوں سچ کہتے ہو۔ اب سوال یہ ہے کہ غلام آزاد ہوگا یا نہیں اور غلام پر اپنی قیمت کما کر دینا واجب ہوگا یا نہیں تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا
اختلاف ہے اس بات پر تو سب متفق ہیں کہ غلام آزاد ہو گیا اور اس پر کمائی واجب ہونے اور نہ ہونے میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس پر اپنی قیمت کما کر دینا واجب ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس پر کچھ کمائی کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں عشق کی الصحۃ اور قرض دونوں کا ظہور ایک ساتھ ہوا ہے یعنی جب وارث نے ایک کلام سے ان دونوں کی تصدیق کی تو اس سے ایک ساتھ عتق فی الصحۃ اور قرض کا ظہور ہوا ہے۔
تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ عشق اور دین دونوں ساتھ ساتھ واجب ہوئے ہیں یعنی دونوں کا تعلق حالت صحت سے ہے۔ اور ادھر قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ حالت صحت میں اگر عتق ہوتا ہے وہ علائم کچھ کمائی واجب نہی کرنا خواہ معتق پر قرض بھی ہو، اس لئے صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ غلام پر کمائی واجب نہیں ہے۔

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
وله ان الاقرار بالدين اقوى لانه يعتبر من جميع المال والاقرار بالعتق فى المرض يعتبر من الثلث والاقوى يدفع الادنى فقضيته ان يبطل العتق اصلا الا انه بعد وقوعه لا يحتمل البطلان فيد فع من حيث المعنى بايجاب السعاية ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقرارا قومی ہے اس لئے کہ قرض پورے مال سے معتبر ہوتا ہے اور حالت مرض میں عشق کا اقرار ثلث مال سے معتبر ہوتا ہے اور اقومی ادنی کو دور کر دیتا ہے تو اس دور کرنے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ عتق بالکل باطل ہو جائے مگر عتق اپنے واقع ہونے کے بعد بطلان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تو عشق کو معنی کی حیثیت سے دفع کیا جائے گا کمائی کو واجب کرنے کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے حاصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرض حق سے اقومی ہے، اور قرض کے اقومی ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مریض اگر قرض کا اقرار کرے تو یہ اقرار دین پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مرض میں عشق کا اقرار ہے تو یہ اقرار مال کے ثلث سے معتبر ہوگا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرض عشق سے اقویٰ ہے، اور ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ اقومی ادنی کو دھکا دیدیا کرتا ہے تو اس کا تو تقاضہ یہ تھا کہ عنق بالکل ہی باطل ہوجا تا مگر کیا کیا جائے ، اصول یہ کہ جب عشق واقع ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر بطلان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔
اس لئے عشق کو باطل تو نہیں کر سکتے البتہ معنوی اعتبار سے عشق کو باطل کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
یعنی محقق کو نافذ مان کے غلام پر کمائی کو واجب کر دیا جائے لہذا ہم نے وہی طریقہ اختیار کیا کہ غلام آزاد ہے لیکن اس پر اپنی قیمت کما کر دینا واجب ہے۔
امام صاحب کی دوسری دلیل
ولان الدين اسبق لانه لا مانع له من الاسناد فيستند الى حالة الصحة ولا يمكن اسناد العتق الى تلك الحالة لان الدين يمنع العتق فى حالة المرض مجانا فتجب السعاية
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ قرض مقدم ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے کہ اسناد سے کوئی مانع نہیں ہے پس قرض کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کی جائے گی اور محقق کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قرض مفت حالت مرض میں عشق کو روکتا ہے پس کمائی واجب ہو گی ۔
Imam Muhammad said: Whoever leaves a slave, and the slave says to the heir, 'Your father freed me in health,' and a man says, 'I have a debt of one thousand dirhams against your father,' then the heir says, 'You both speak truthfully.' Then the slave works to earn his value according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The slave is free and does not work to earn anything, because the debt and the emancipation in health appeared together due to the heir's confirmation in one statement, so they become as if they were together, and emancipation in health does not necessitate sa'y, even if the manumitter had a debt. Explanation: Zaid died and left only one slave. The slave said to the heir, 'Your father freed me in health,' and another person said, 'I have a debt against your father of one thousand dirhams.' The heir replied, 'You both speak truthfully.' The question is: is the slave free? And must he work to earn his value? There is disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions. All agree that the slave becomes free, but they differ on whether sa'y is obligatory. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he must work to earn his value; according to the two, he need not. The proof of the two: the emancipation in health and the debt appeared together, i.e., when the heir confirmed both in one statement, both the emancipation in health and the debt emerged simultaneously. So both become effective together, both related to the state of health. And the rule is that emancipation in health does not impose sa'y even if the manumitter had debt. Therefore, the two say sa'y is not obligatory. Abu Hanifa's proof: The acknowledgment of debt is stronger, because it is considered from the entire wealth, while the acknowledgment of emancipation in illness is considered from one-third. The stronger overcomes the weaker, so it would necessitate the nullification of emancipation entirely, but since emancipation after occurrence cannot be nullified, it is repelled in meaning by imposing sa'y. Explanation: This is Abu Hanifa's proof. The summary: debt is stronger than the right (of emancipation). The proof that debt is stronger is that if a sick person acknowledges a debt, it is considered from the entire wealth, but if he acknowledges emancipation in illness, it is considered from one-third. Thus debt is stronger. And the principle is that the stronger repels the weaker. So the requirement would be that emancipation becomes completely invalid. But what can be done? The principle is that once emancipation occurs, it cannot be invalidated. So we cannot invalidate emancipation, but we can invalidate it in a virtual sense. That is, we uphold the emancipation as effective but impose sa'y on the slave. Therefore we adopted this method: the slave is free but must work to earn his value. Imam's second proof: Because the debt is prior, for there is no obstacle to its attribution (to health), so it is attributed to the state of health, and it is not possible to attribute emancipation to that state because the debt prevents gratuitous emancipation in illness, so sa'y is obligatory.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific scenario from the Book of Wills. The case involves a deceased who leaves only a slave as his estate. Two claims arise: the slave claims he was freed by the deceased in health, and a creditor claims a debt of 1000 dirhams. The heir confirms both claims in one statement. The issue is whether the slave must work to pay his value (sa'y) to the estate. All agree the slave becomes free. The disagreement is on sa'y. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the slave must work to earn his value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he does not. The Sahibayn argue that since the heir confirmed both in one statement, both the emancipation in health and the debt become effective simultaneously. Since the emancipation is attributed to health, the general rule applies: emancipation in health does not impose sa'y, even if the manumitter had debt. Abu Hanifa gives two proofs. First, the debt acknowledgment is stronger (aqwa) because it is valid over the entire estate, while emancipation in illness is limited to one-third. The stronger should repel the weaker, ideally nullifying the emancipation, but since emancipation cannot be undone once executed, it is repelled in meaning by imposing sa'y. Second, the debt is prior (asbaq) because it can be attributed to the state of health without obstacle, while the emancipation cannot be attributed to health because doing so would involve passing through the illness period, and the debt prevents gratuitous emancipation in illness. Therefore, sa'y is imposed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is usually that of the Sahibayn, but both views are transmitted.

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'y): The slave's working to earn his own value to pay off a debt or claim on the estate.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; here, claimed to have been done by the deceased in health.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession; here, the heir's confirmation of both claims.
اقوى (aqwa): Stronger; used in the principle that the stronger (debt) repels the weaker (emancipation).
اسبق (asbaq): Prior; used to argue that debt has priority in attribution to health.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute regarding the slave whose heir confirms both emancipation and debt, what is the ruling according to the Sahibayn?
A) The slave is free and must work to earn his value.
B) The slave is free and does not work to earn anything.
C) The slave is not freed.
D) The slave is freed but only after paying the debt.

Key Takeaway
In the disputed scenario, the mufta bihi is that the slave is free without sa'y, but Abu Hanifa's proofs reveal deep usul principles of strength and priority.

Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof: Debt Over Manumission in Marad al-Mawt
Imam Abu Hanifa presents two proofs that debt overrides manumission in terminal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's two proofs that debt overrides manumission in terminal illness and apply the ruling that the freed slave must earn his price (sa'yat).

Core Idea
Debt is stronger than manumission because it affects all wealth, so the freed slave must earn his value.

In this passage, Imam Abu Hanifa presents two independent but complementary proofs establishing that when a terminally ill person acknowledges a debt and also frees a slave, the debt takes precedence. The manumission remains valid, but the slave is required to earn his price to repay the debt. This ruling highlights the Hanafi commitment to protecting creditors' rights while respecting the act of emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conflict
Identify the scenario: a terminally ill person acknowledges a debt and also manumits a slave. The debt is owed from the entire estate, while manumission is a bequest limited to one-third.
Both occur in marad al-mawt.
2
Analyze the first proof (qiyas based on strength)
The creditor's right is stronger because debt is from all wealth, manumission from one-third. The stronger repels the weaker, but manumission cannot be undone, so the effect is applied by imposing sa'yat.
Qiyas with illa of strength.
3
Analyze the second proof (attribution/priority)
Debt can be attributed to the period of health because it existed prior, while manumission only occurs at death. Thus the debt prevents free manumission during illness.
Isnad argument.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they hold the slave is free without earning. The mufta bihi is Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
The dispute is over the applicability of sa'yat.
5
Extract the operative ruling
Slave is free but must earn his price (sa'yat wajib). This reconciles the irreversibility of manumission with the priority of debt.
The earning is a compensation for the debt.

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل

وله ان الاقرار بالدين اقوى لانه يعتبر من جميع المال والاقرار بالعتق فى المرض يعتبر من الثلث والاقوى يدفع الادنى فقضيته ان يبطل العتق اصلا الا انه بعد وقوعه لا يحتمل البطلان فيد فع من حيث المعنى بايجاب السعاية

ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقرارا قومی ہے اس لئے کہ قرض پورے مال سے معتبر ہوتا ہے اور حالت مرض میں عشق کا اقرار ثلث مال سے معتبر ہوتا ہے اور اقومی ادنی کو دور کر دیتا ہے تو اس دور کرنے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ عتق بالکل باطل ہو جائے مگر عتق اپنے واقع ہونے کے بعد بطلان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تو عشق کو معنی کی حیثیت سے دفع کیا جائے گا کمائی کو واجب کرنے کے ساتھ ۔

تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے حاصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرض حق سے اقومی ہے، اور قرض کے اقومی ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مریض اگر قرض کا اقرار کرے تو یہ اقرار دین پورے مال سے معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مرض میں عشق کا اقرار ہے تو یہ اقرار مال کے ثلث سے معتبر ہوگا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرض عشق سے اقویٰ ہے، اور ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ اقومی ادنی کو دھکا دیدیا کرتا ہے تو اس کا تو تقاضہ یہ تھا کہ عنق بالکل ہی باطل ہوجا تا مگر کیا کیا جائے ، اصول یہ کہ جب عشق واقع ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر بطلان کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔

اس لئے عشق کو باطل تو نہیں کر سکتے البتہ معنوی اعتبار سے عشق کو باطل کیا جا سکتا ہے۔

یعنی محقق کو نافذ مان کے غلام پر کمائی کو واجب کر دیا جائے لہذا ہم نے وہی طریقہ اختیار کیا کہ غلام آزاد ہے لیکن اس پر اپنی قیمت کما کر دینا واجب ہے۔

امام صاحب کی دوسری دلیل

ولان الدين اسبق لانه لا مانع له من الاسناد فيستند الى حالة الصحة ولا يمكن اسناد العتق الى تلك الحالة لان الدين يمنع العتق فى حالة المرض مجانا فتجب السعاية

ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ قرض مقدم ہے اس لئے اس کے لئے کہ اسناد سے کوئی مانع نہیں ہے پس قرض کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کی جائے گی اور محقق کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قرض مفت حالت مرض میں عشق کو روکتا ہے پس کمائی واجب ہو گی ۔

تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دوسری دلیل ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ قرض عشق سے مقدم ہے کیونکہ اگر قرض کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کی جائے تو اس سے یہاں کوئی چیز مانع نہیں ہے لہذا قرض کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب کرتے ہوئے کہا جائے گا کہ یہ قرض حالت صحت کا ہے اور عشق مذکور کی اسناد حالت صحت کی جانب ممکن نہیں کیونکہ اس کا ظہور تو اب ہوا ہے جب کہ موصی کا انتقال ہو چکا ہے۔ اور حالت صحت کی جانب اسناد کرنے میں حالت مرض کے اندر کو گزرنا ہوگا اور گزرنا جائز نہیں بلکہ یہ اسناد یہیں دب کر رہ جائے گی۔ کیسے؟

اس لئے کہ پہلے حالات صحت میں قرض موجود ہے اور جب مرض الموت میں مقروض مفت غلام آزاد کرے تو وہ مفت آزاد نہ ہوگا بلکہ غلام تو آزاد ہو جائے گا مگر اس پر کمائی کرنا واجب ہو گا لہذا ہم نے اس پر کمائی کو واجب کر دیا ہے۔
Book of Wasiyyah. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: And his proof is that acknowledgment of debt is stronger because it is considered from all the wealth, and acknowledgment of manumission in illness is considered from one-third, and the stronger repels the weaker, so its consequence is that manumission is invalidated entirely, but after its occurrence it does not admit invalidation, so it is repelled in meaning by imposing earning. Translation: And Abu Hanifa's proof is that acknowledgment is stronger because debt is considered from all wealth, and acknowledgment of manumission in illness is considered from one-third of wealth, and the stronger removes the weaker, so this removal requires that manumission become completely void, but since after occurrence it does not admit invalidation, manumission is repelled in meaning by making earning obligatory. Explanation: This is Imam Abu Hanifa's proof. The summary is that debt is stronger than right, and the proof that debt is stronger is that if a sick person acknowledges a debt, this acknowledgment is considered from all wealth, and if he acknowledges manumission in illness, this acknowledgment is considered from one-third of wealth, from which it is known that debt is stronger than manumission, and it has passed before that the stronger pushes the weaker, so its requirement was that manumission become completely void, but what can be done? The principle is that when manumission occurs, it does not admit invalidation. Therefore, manumission cannot be invalidated, but conceptually it can be invalidated. That is, accepting the manumission as effective, earning is imposed on the slave, so we adopted that method: the slave is free but he must earn his price. Imam's second proof: And because debt is prior, because there is no obstacle to its attribution, so it is attributed to the state of health, and attribution of manumission to that state is not possible because debt prevents free manumission in illness, so earning is obligatory. Translation: And because debt is prior, because it has no obstacle to attribution, so debt is attributed to the state of health, and attribution of manumission to that state is not possible because debt prevents free manumission in the state of illness, so earning becomes obligatory. Explanation: This is Imam Abu Hanifa's second proof. He says that debt is prior to manumission because if debt is attributed to the state of health, nothing prevents it, so debt is said to be from health, and attribution of manumission to the state of health is not possible because its manifestation occurred now when the testator has passed away, and attribution to health would require passing through the state of illness, which is not permissible, so this attribution remains stuck. How? Because first, in health, debt exists, and when in terminal illness a debtor frees a slave for free, he will not be free for free, but the slave becomes free, but earning upon him becomes obligatory, so we made earning obligatory upon him.

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's two proofs for why a debt acknowledged in terminal illness takes precedence over a manumission (itq) also acknowledged in terminal illness, resulting in the freed slave being required to earn (sa'yat) his value. The passage type is ruling_with_proof. Imam's first proof uses a qiyas reasoning: acknowledgment of debt is stronger (aqwa) because it considers all the deceased's wealth, while acknowledgment of manumission only considers one-third. The stronger repels the weaker, so logically manumission should be void, but because manumission once executed cannot be undone, the effect is applied conceptually by imposing earning on the slave. The second proof argues that debt is prior (asbaq) because it can be attributed back to the healthy state before illness, while manumission cannot, as it only occurs at death. Thus the debt prevents free manumission during illness, requiring the slave to earn his price. Both proofs rely on qiyas and istihsan. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Abu Hanifa's view that the slave must earn his price, as opposed to the Sahibayn who hold a different view (not fully detailed here).

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'yat): The slave's obligation to earn money to pay his value to the estate, imposed by Imam Abu Hanifa when manumission conflicts with debt in terminal illness.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right, such as debt or manumission, made by a person in terminal illness.
اسناد (isnad): Attributing a legal event (like debt or manumission) to a particular time (health or illness) for legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because debt is mentioned before manumission in the Quran
B) Because debt is considered from all the estate while manumission is only from one-third
C) Because manumission can be revoked but debt cannot
D) Because the slave prefers debt over freedom

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling reconciles the inviolability of manumission with the priority of debt by requiring the freed slave to earn his value.

Deposit vs Debt Priority in Inheritance: Imam vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on deposit vs debt priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the priority of a deposit over a debt in an insufficient estate, and explain the reasoning based on specific property ('ayn) vs general obligation (dhimmah).

Core Idea
A deposit (specific property) takes precedence over a debt (general obligation) on an insufficient estate.

Imagine a deceased person leaves behind only a thousand dirhams, but two claimants come forward: one says 'he owed me a thousand' and another says 'he was holding my thousand as a deposit.' Who gets the money? This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi debate where Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on the answer. Understanding their reasoning sharpens our grasp of the distinction between specific property rights and personal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man dies leaving 1000 dirhams. Claimant A says it was a debt (dayn), claimant B says it was a deposit (wadi'ah). The estate only has these 1000.
Both claims are for the same amount.
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa says the deposit is stronger (aqwa) and the depositor takes all. Sahibayn say both are equal and they share the 1000 equally.
This is the core disagreement.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Imam argues: a deposit is tied to the specific property ('ayn), while debt is an obligation in the dhimmah (personal liability) with no specific property connection. Therefore, the depositor's claim to the actual property is stronger. Sahibayn argue that both are obligations on the deceased and should be treated equally.
The key distinction is 'ayniyah vs dhimmah.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If the estate is 1000, under Imam the depositor gets all; under Sahibayn each gets 500.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, as recorded in the zahir al-riwayah and favored by later authorities like al-Hidayah.
Deposit takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا مات الرجل وترك الف درهم فقال رجل لى على الميت الف درهم دين وقال الاخر كان لي عنده الف درهم وديعة فعنده الوديعة اقوى وعندهما ترجمہ اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب کہ کوئی شخص مر گیا اور اس نے ہزار درہم چھوڑے پس ایک شخص نے کہا کہ میرامیت پر ہزار درہم قرض ہے اور دوسرے شخص نے کہا کہ میرے اس کے پاس ہزار ہم امانت تھے تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ودیعت اقومی ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ دونوں برابر ہیں۔

تشریح زید کا انتقال ہو گیا اور اس نے ہزار ہم ترکہ میں چھوڑے پس ایک شخص نے کہا کہ زید میر ا مقروض تھا یعنی اس پر میرے ہزار درہم قرض تھے اور دوسرے شخص نے کہا کہ اس کے پاس میرے ہزار درہم امانت تھے۔

تو اب کس کا قول ہو گا ؟

تو حضرات صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ قرض اور دیعت دونوں کا ایک درجہ ہے اور یہ دونوں برابر میں یعنی موجودہ ہزار میں دونوں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک قرض سے ودیعت اقومی ہے لہذا موجودہ ہزار دویم امانت والے کے ہوں گے۔

اب رہی یہ بات کہ ودیعت کیوں اقویٰ ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قرض تو واجب فی الذمہ ہوتا ہے میں سے کس کا تعلق نہیں ہے اور ودیعت کا تعلق مین سے ہے یعنی یہی ہزار درہم ہیں جو میرے اسکے پاس ودیعت تھے اسلئے ودیعت کو اقوی شمار کیا گیا ہے۔
And upon this difference, when a man dies and leaves a thousand dirhams, and one man says, 'The deceased owes me a thousand dirhams as debt,' and another says, 'I had a thousand dirhams as deposit with him,' then according to Abu Hanifa the deposit is stronger, and according to them (Sahibayn) they are equal. Translation: And upon this difference, when a person died and he left a thousand dirhams, then one person said, 'The deceased owes me a thousand dirhams as debt,' and another person said, 'I had a thousand dirhams as trust (amana) with him,' then according to Abu Hanifa the deposit (wadi'ah) is stronger, and according to the Sahibayn both are equal. Explanation: Zaid passed away and left a thousand dirhams in estate. One person said Zaid was my debtor, i.e., he owed me a thousand dirhams, and another person said he had my thousand dirhams as trust (amana). So now whose word will be accepted? The Sahibayn said that debt and deposit are of the same level, and both are equal, meaning they will share equally in the existing thousand. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, deposit is stronger than debt, so the existing thousand will go to the depositor. Now as to why deposit is stronger, the answer is that debt is an obligation in the dhimmah (liability) which has no connection to a specific property, while deposit is connected to specific property, i.e., these very thousand dirhams were deposited with him, so deposit is considered stronger.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the priority of a deposit (wadi'ah) claim versus a debt (dayn) claim when the estate is insufficient to cover both. The passage type is intra_hanafi_dispute. The scenario: a man dies leaving 1,000 dirhams. One claimant says the deceased owed him 1,000 dirhams as debt; another says he had deposited 1,000 dirhams with the deceased. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the deposit is stronger (aqwa) and the entire 1,000 dirhams go to the depositor. The Sahibayn hold that both claims are equal and they share the estate proportionally. Imam's reasoning: debt is a liability in the dhimmah (obligation in person) and not tied to any specific property, whereas a deposit is connected to the very property that exists. Since the deposit is 'ayn (specific property) and the debt is dayn (obligation), the specific property has a stronger claim. This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah, and the mufta bihi position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, as it is based on the principle of specificity ('ayniyah) versus generality (dhimmah).

Key Terms
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A deposit or trust where one person leaves property with another for safekeeping without compensation.
دین (dayn): A debt, an obligation in the dhimmah (personal liability) not tied to specific property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider a deposit (wadi'ah) stronger than a debt (dayn)?
A) Because deposit is mentioned before debt in the Quran
B) Because deposit is connected to specific property while debt is a general obligation in the dhimmah
C) Because the depositor is a Muslim and the creditor may be non-Muslim
D) Because debt can be waived but deposit cannot

Key Takeaway
A deposit (wadi'ah) takes priority over a debt (dayn) on an insufficient estate because it is tied to specific property, not just a personal obligation.

Prioritizing Obligatory Bequests Over Voluntary in Huquq Allah
Ruling on prioritization of obligatory bequests over voluntary in Huquq Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prioritizing bequests for Huquq Allah and apply it to a scenario involving multiple bequests.

Core Idea
In bequests for Huquq Allah, obligatory acts (fard) are always fulfilled before voluntary ones (nafl), regardless of the testator's order.

When a Muslim makes a will that includes bequests for religious duties like Hajj or Zakat, and also includes voluntary charity, which should be carried out first if the estate is limited? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer: the obligatory (fard) takes precedence, even if the testator wrote the voluntary one first. This lesson explains the rule and its reasoning from a classical Hanafi text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and state the main ruling: when a testator makes multiple bequests for Huquq Allah, the obligatory ones (fara'id) are given precedence over voluntary ones (nawafil).
The examples given are Hajj, Zakat, and expiations (kaffarat).
2
Understand the reasoning
The text states: 'because the obligatory is more important than the voluntary, and the apparent meaning is to start with what is more important.' This is the core legal rationale (ta'lil).
The principle is that fard is more significant than nafl in the scale of religious duties.
3
Note the condition of the ruling
The passage also explains that this ruling applies only when a bequest has been made. If no bequest, heirs are not required to fulfill these obligations from the estate; they may do so voluntarily.
This distinction is crucial: without a bequest, the heirs have the option, not the obligation.
4
Apply the rule
Given a scenario where a testator bequeaths one-third of the estate to cover both missed fasts (fard) and a voluntary charity, determine which must be fulfilled first.
Remember: fard always comes before nafl, regardless of the testator's order.

Source Text

فصل ومن اوصى بوصايا من حقوق الله تعالى قدمت الفرائض منها قد مها الموصى او اخرها مثل الحج والزكوة والكفارات لان الفريضة اهم من النافلة والظاهر منه البداية بما هو الاهم

ترجمہ یہ فصل ہے اور جس نے وصیت کی چند وصایا حقوق اللہ میں سے تو ان میں سے فرائض کو مقدم کیا جائے گا موصی نے ان کو مقدم کیا ہو یا موخر کیا ہو جیسے حج اور زکوۃ اور کفارات اس لئے کہ فرض نافلہ سے اہم ہے اور ظاہر موصی سے شروع کرنا ہے اس چیز سے جو کہ اہم ہے۔ تشریح اگر کسی شخص کا انتقال ہو جائے اور اس کے ذمہ کوئی اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہے مثلا نماز یا روز و یاز کو یا حج یا کفارہ یا نذر یا صدقۂ فطر ، تو اب دو صورتیں ہیں مرنے والے نے ان کے بارے میں وصیت کی ہے یا نہیں اگر نہیں کی تو ورثا پر ان کی ادائیگی واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ در خاکو نکالنے اور نہ نکالنے کا اختیار ہے، اور اگر اول صورت ہو یعنی اس نے وصیت کی ہو تو مرحوم کے ثلث مال سے ان کی ادائے گی واجب
Chapter: And whoever makes bequests of the rights of Allah, the obligatory ones among them are given precedence, whether the testator gave them precedence or delayed them, such as Hajj, Zakat, and Kaffarat (expiations), because the obligatory is more important than the voluntary, and the apparent meaning is to start with what is more important. Translation: This is a chapter. And whoever made bequests of several rights of Allah, then among them the obligatory ones (fara'id) will be given precedence, whether the testator gave them precedence or delayed them, such as Hajj, Zakat, and Kaffarat, because the obligatory is more important than the voluntary, and the apparent meaning from the testator is to start with what is more important. Explanation: If a person passes away and there is a right of Allah upon him, such as Salah, Sawm, Hajj, Kaffarah, Nadhr, or Sadaqat al-Fitr, then there are two scenarios: the deceased made a bequest regarding them or not. If not, then it is not obligatory upon the heirs to pay them; rather they have the option to pay or not. If the first scenario (he made a bequest), then payment from one-third of the estate is obligatory.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding multiple bequests involving Huquq Allah (rights of Allah) such as Hajj, Zakat, Kaffarat, etc. The passage type is ruling_statement. The rule: when a testator makes multiple bequests for obligations (fara'id) and supererogatory acts (nawafil), the obligatory must be fulfilled first, even if the testator ordered otherwise. This is because fard (obligatory) is more important than nafl (voluntary). The default intention of the testator is to prioritize what is most essential. If no bequest is made, heirs are not obliged to perform these acts; they may do so voluntarily. However, if a bequest is made, these acts must be executed from the one-third of the estate, starting with obligations. This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. Note: The explanation also includes a note that if no bequest, heirs are not obligated—this is a separate nuance: the ruling only applies when a bequest is made.

Key Terms
حقوق اللہ (huquq Allah): Rights of Allah, i.e., religious obligations such as prayer, fasting, Hajj, Zakat, expiations (kaffarat), and vows (nudhur).
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence (qat'i), such as Hajj, Zakat, Kaffarat.
نافلہ (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary acts of worship, such as extra prayers or charity beyond the obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person bequeaths money for both Hajj (obligatory) and a voluntary charity, but the estate is limited to one-third, which must be fulfilled first?
A) The voluntary charity because the testator mentioned it first
B) Hajj because it is obligatory (fard)
C) They should be split equally
D) Neither, because no bequest is valid for Hajj

Key Takeaway
In bequests for Huquq Allah, obligatory acts (fard) must be fulfilled before voluntary ones (nafl), overriding the testator's order.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Prioritizing Fard Over Nafl in Multiple Bequests
Ruling on fard precedence in multiple bequests of rights of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that fard bequests take precedence over nafl regardless of the testator's order, and explain the two narrations on whether Zakat or Hajj is given priority when both are fard.

Core Idea
Fard bequests always precede nafl; when equal in strength, the testator's order decides.

When a person makes multiple bequests involving rights of Allah, the law must determine which to execute first if the one-third estate is insufficient. This passage from the chapter on wasiyyah establishes a clear hierarchy: obligations (fard) override voluntary acts (nafl) irrespective of the testator's mention. However, when all bequests are of equal strength—e.g., all fard or all wajib—the testator's own order is followed. A notable intra-Hanafi dispute arises between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding Zakat and Hajj, both fard, and whose precedence al-Tahawi records.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the bequests
Identify the three categories: fard (obligatory, e.g. Hajj, Zakat), wajib (necessary, e.g. kaffarat), and tatawwu' (voluntary, e.g. nafl Hajj). The ruling differs based on these categories.
The source uses 'fara'id' generally for obligations, but inside it distinguishes fard, wajib, and nafl.
2
Apply the general rule of fard precedence
When bequests include both fard and non-fard, fard is always executed first, even if the testator mentioned it last. The rationale (talil) is that fard is more important than nafl, and the testator's apparent intent is to prioritize the important.
This rule is absolute; it overrides the testator's order.
3
Handle equal-strength bequests
If all bequests are of the same strength (all fard, all wajib, or all tatawwu'), the testator's own order of mention is followed, as it indicates his priority. This applies only when one-third is insufficient.
Equal strength means they belong to the same category, not that they are of equal importance.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on Zakat vs Hajj
Within the fard category, if both Zakat and Hajj are bequeathed, there are two narrations: one from Abu Yusuf (followed by al-Tahawi) gives Zakat precedence; another from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad gives Hajj precedence. The passage does not resolve the dispute.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: the executor must decide which view to follow.

Section: Whoever makes bequests (wasiyyat) from the rights of Allah, the fard (obligatory) among them are given precedence, whether the testator preceded them or delayed them, such as Hajj, Zakat, and Kaffarat (expiations). Because the fard is more important than the nafl (voluntary), and the apparent intent of the testator is to begin with what is most important. Translation: This is a section. And whoever makes a bequest of several rights of Allah, then among them the fara'id (obligations) are given precedence, whether the testator made them prior or delayed, like Hajj, Zakat, and Kaffarat. Because the fard is more important than the nafl, and the apparent intent of the testator is to begin with that which is important. Explanation: If a person dies and he owes a right of Allah, e.g., Salah, Sawm, Hajj, Kaffarah, Nadhr, or Sadaqat al-Fitr, then there are two scenarios: the deceased made a bequest about them or not. If not, the heirs are not obliged to pay; they have the option to pay or not. If he did make a bequest, then payment is obligatory from one-third of his estate. Then which bequest is given precedence? There is detail. The bequests are either rights of Allah or rights of people. Those that are rights of Allah are either all included in fard (like Zakat, Hajj, Sawm, Salah) or all in wajib (like Kaffarat, Nadhr, Sadaqat al-Fitr) or all in tatawwu' (voluntary, like bequest for nafl Hajj or charity to the poor). If the testator combined all these bequests, and if his one-third is sufficient for all, all are executed. If insufficient but the heirs permit, all are executed. If heirs do not permit, then it is checked: if all bequests are fard, start with what the testator presented first. If some are fard and others non-fard, start with fard even if the testator delayed them and presented wajib and tatawwu' first. Why give precedence to fard? Because fard is more important than nafl, and it is apparent that the testator's intent is to give precedence to what is important, because a debtor usually does not engage in charities. When all bequests are equal in strength, which is given precedence? The statements of the jurists: 'If they are equal in strength, start with what the testator presented, when the one-third is insufficient for them, because it is apparent that he starts with the more important.' And al-Tahawi mentioned that one starts with Zakat and gives it precedence over Hajj, and this is one of two narrations from Abu Yusuf, and in another narration from him that one gives precedence to Hajj, and that is the saying of Muhammad. Translation: So if all bequests are equal in strength, one will begin with the bequest which the testator presented first when the one-third is insufficient for all these bequests, because the apparent is that the testator will begin with the more important. And al-Tahawi mentioned that one will begin with Zakat and give it precedence over Hajj, and this is one of two narrations from Abu Yusuf, and in another narration from him that Hajj is given precedence, and that is the saying of Muhammad. Explanation: If all bequests are equal in strength, e.g., all are fard, or all are wajib, or all are tatawwu', then the bequest that the testator presented first is given precedence, provided that the one-third is insufficient. Because the testator's statement shows that he considered that bequest more important. Imam al-Tahawi mentioned that if Zakat and Hajj are combined, and both are within fard, still Zakat is given precedence over Hajj. This mentioned by al-Tahawi is one narration from Abu Yusuf: that Zakat is given precedence over Hajj.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Wasiyyat (bequests) discusses the order of execution when a testator makes multiple bequests involving rights of Allah (huquq Allah) and the one-third of the estate is insufficient. The commentary opens by stating the section. It explains that the testator may have made bequests for obligatory acts (fard, like Hajj, Zakat), necessary acts (wajib, like Kaffarat, Nadhr), or voluntary acts (tatawwu', like nafl Hajj or charity). The rule is: obligatory bequests are given precedence over voluntary ones regardless of the order in which the testator mentioned them. The proof given is 'because fard is more important than nafl' (l'an al-faridah ahammu min al-nafilah). The apparent intent of the testator is to start with the important. If all bequests are of the same strength (all fard, all wajib, or all tatawwu'), then the testator's own order is followed, as it indicates his priority. The passage then introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute among the Sahibayn regarding Zakat and Hajj when both are fard and one-third is insufficient: one narration from Abu Yusuf (followed by al-Tahawi) gives Zakat precedence; another narration from Abu Yusuf and the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani give Hajj precedence. The commentary follows the author's order, first presenting the Arabic ruling, then translation, then detailed explanation with scenarios.

Key Terms
فرائض (fara'id): Obligatory acts of worship commanded by Allah, such as Hajj, Zakat, Salah, Sawm.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a person during lifetime to take effect after death, from up to one-third of the estate.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum that can be bequeathed without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a testator makes bequests of both fard and nafl rights of Allah, and the one-third is insufficient, which is executed first?
A) The bequest mentioned first by the testator.
B) The nafl bequest because it is more common.
C) The fard bequest regardless of order.
D) They are executed proportionally.

Key Takeaway
Fard bequests in rights of Allah always take precedence over nafl, and when all are equal in strength, the testator's order decides; an intra-Hanafi dispute exists on the order of Zakat and Hajj.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
6 min
Categories of Bequests and Precedence Rules
Classifies bequests and sets priority rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify bequests into fara'id, wajibat, and tatawwu', and apply the precedence rule when the thulth is insufficient and heirs do not consent.

Core Idea
Obligatory bequests (fara'id) take precedence over non-obligatory ones, regardless of the testator's order.

When a testator leaves multiple bequests but the bequeathable third (thulth) is insufficient, a priority system is needed. The Hanafi school categorizes bequests by their legal weight: obligatory acts (fara'id), necessary duties (wajibat), and voluntary acts (tatawwu'). This lesson explains how to determine which bequest is executed first when resources are limited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Recognize that bequests are classified as fara'id (e.g., missed zakat, hajj, fasting, prayer), wajibat (e.g., expiations, vows, sadaqat al-fitr), or tatawwu' (e.g., voluntary hajj, charity).
The categories are based on the type of obligation in the shari'ah.
2
Check thulth sufficiency
If the testator's bequeathable third covers all bequests, all are executed. If not, proceed to check heirs' consent.
3
Consider heirs' consent
If heirs permit execution beyond thulth, all bequests are executed. If they object, apply priority rules.
Heirs' consent can override the thulth limit.
4
Apply precedence among categories
If bequests mix categories, fara'id are executed first, even if the testator mentioned them later. Then wajibat, then tatawwu'.
Fara'id are more important because they are obligatory duties owed to Allah.
5
Handle all-fara'id case
If all bequests are fara'id, begin with the one the testator mentioned first.
This respects the testator's intent within the same category.

كتاب الوصايا

هوگي پھر وصایا میں سے کون سی وصیت مقدم ہوگی تو اس میں تفصیل ہے۔ وہ وصایا اللہ کا حق ہوں گی یا بندوں کا اور جو اللہ کا حق ہیں وہ یا تو سب وصایا فرائض میں داخل ہوں گی جیسے زکوۃ اور حج اور روزہ اور نماز یا سب واجبات میں داخل ہوں گی جیسے کفارات اور نذر اور صدقہ فطر یا سب وصایا تطوع میں داخل ہوں گی جیسے حج نفلی کی وصیت اور فقراء پر صدقہ کی وصیت، پس اگر موصی نے ان تمام وصایا کو جمع کر دیا ہو تو اگر موصی کا ثلث مال تمام وصایا کے نفاذ کے لئے کافی ہو سکے تو ان تمام وصایا کو نافذ کر دیا جائے گا، اور اگر موصی کا ثلث مال ان تمام وصایا کے لئے کافی نہ ہو لیکن ورثہ نے اجازت دیدی ہو کہ ان تمام وصایا کو نافذ کر دیا جائے تو ان سب کو نافذ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر ورثہ نے اجازت نہ دی ہو تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ یہ تمام وصایا فرائض میں داخل ہیں یا نہیں اگر سب فرائض میں داخل ہوں تو جس وصیت کو موصی نے مقدم بیان کیا ہے اس سے ابتداء کی جائے گی، اور اگر بعض فرائض اور بعض غیر فرائض ہوں تو اولا فرائض سے ابتدا کی جائے گی اگر چہ موصی نے ذکر میں فرائض کو موخر کیا ہو، اور واجبات اور تطوعات کو مقدم کیا ہو۔

فرائض کو کیوں مقدم کیا جائے گا ؟ اس لئے کہ فرائض نفل سے اہم ہے اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ موصی کا مقصد بھی اہم ہی کو مقدم کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ جس شخص پر قرض ہوتا ہے وہ عموماً صدقات و خیرات میں مشغول نہیں ہوتا۔
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the order of execution when multiple bequests (wasaya) are made and the bequeathable third (thulth) is insufficient. The author first categorizes bequests into three types: those that are obligatory acts of worship (fara'id) like zakat, hajj, fasting, and prayer; those that are wajibat (obligatory duties) like expiations (kaffarat), vows (nadhur), and sadaqat al-fitr; and those that are voluntary (tatawwu') like supererogatory hajj and charity to the poor. If the testator's bequeathable third is sufficient, all are executed. If insufficient but heirs permit, all are executed. If heirs do not permit, we look: if all bequests are fara'id, we begin with the one the testator mentioned first; if some are fara'id and some are not, we give precedence to the fara'id even if the testator mentioned them later, because fara'id are more important than non-obligatory acts, and a person in debt (obligation) does not usually engage in voluntary charity.

Key Terms
وصیہ (wasiyya): A bequest made by a testator, valid from up to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent.
فرائض (fara'id): Obligatory acts of worship that are fard, such as missed prayers, zakat, hajj, etc.
واجبات (wajibat): Duties that are wajib, like expiations (kaffarat) and sadaqat al-fitr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A testator bequeaths: 1) a missed hajj (fard), 2) a kaffarah (wajib). The thulth is enough for only one. Heirs object. Which is executed?
A) The kaffarah, because it was mentioned second?
B) The missed hajj, because fara'id take precedence over wajibat.
C) Both are divided proportionally.
D) None, because the testator did not specify order.

Key Takeaway
Fara'id bequests always take precedence over wajibat and tatawwu' when the thulth is insufficient and heirs do not consent.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Equal Strength Bequests and the Zakat-Hajj Priority Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on priority of zakat and hajj bequests with legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for prioritizing bequests of equal legal strength and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether zakat or hajj is given precedence, along with the reasoning for each position.

Core Idea
When bequests are equal in strength, the testator's order governs; but for zakat and hajj, the school is divided based on human rights vs. comprehensiveness.

We have already seen that bequests are prioritized by legal strength: fara'id first, then wajibat, then tatawwu'. But what if multiple bequests fall into the same strength category and the third (one-third of the estate) is insufficient for all? The Hanafi school has a general rule, but a specific dispute arises when both zakat (a fard involving wealth) and hajj (a fard involving wealth and body) are bequeathed. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for equal-strength bequests
Identify the rule: when bequests are equal in legal strength (all fara'id, all wajibat, or all tatawwu'), and the third is insufficient, execution follows the testator's order of mention. The rationale is that the testator likely prioritized what he considered most important.
This rule applies only when the third is insufficient; otherwise, all are executed fully.
2
Recognize the specific dispute: zakat vs. hajj
Note that both zakat and hajj are fara'id (obligatory). According to Imam Tahawi, zakat is given precedence. This is one of two narrations from Abu Yusuf. The other narration from Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad's view give precedence to hajj. A tanbih (note) indicates that many Hanafi scholars report that Imam Muhammad actually gave precedence to zakat.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; both views are within the school.
3
Analyze the proofs for each view
First view (zakat first): Although both are fard, zakat involves the rights of the poor (haqq al-ibad), making it stronger. Second view (hajj first): Hajj is performed with both wealth and life, making it more comprehensive and thus stronger.
Both proofs are based on the nature of the acts, not on textual evidence.
4
Place zakat and hajj in the broader hierarchy
The passage extends the comparison: zakat and hajj are given precedence over expiations (kaffarat) because of the severe warnings about neglecting them. Then, among kaffarat, those whose obligation is established by the Quran (e.g., kaffarat for killing, zihar, oath) are given precedence over sadaqat al-fitr, which is based on hadith.
This hierarchy shows a general principle: stronger evidence (Quran vs. hadith) and higher importance yield priority.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The text does not clearly indicate which view is mufta bihi. The tanbih suggests that the author of Hidayah may have followed a particular narration, while many other scholars report that Muhammad gave precedence to zakat. This ambiguity means the mufti must be aware of both narrations and the context.
In practice, the mufti may choose based on the testator's intention or the specific circumstances.

تمام وصایا قوت، درجہ میں برابر ہوں تو کس کو مقدم کیا جائے گا، اقوال فقہاء

فان تساوت فى القوة بدئى بما قدم الموصى اذا ضاق عنها الثلث لان الظاهر انه يبتدى با لا هم وذكر الطحاوى انه يبتدئى بالزكوة ويقد مها على الحج وهو احدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف وفي رواية عنه انه يقدم الحج وهو قول محمد

ترجمہ: پس اگر تمام وصایا قوت میں مساوی ہوں تو ابتدا کی جائے گی اس وصیت سے جس کو موصی نے مقدم کیا ہے جب کہ ثلث ان تمام وصایا سے تنگ ہو جائے اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ موصی اہم سے ابتدا کرے گا اور طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ زکوۃ سے ابتدا کی جائے گی اور اس کو حج پر مقدم کیا جائے گا اور یہی ابو یوسف سے دو روایتوں میں سے ایک روایت ہے اور ابو یوسف سے دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ حج کو مقدم کیا جائے گا اور یہی محمد کا قول ہے۔

تشریح: اگر تمام وصایا قوت میں برابر ہیں مثلاً سب فرائض میں ہیں یا سب واجبات میں سے ہیں یا سب تطوعات میں سے ہیں تو اس وقت اس وصیت کو مقدم کیا جائے گا جس کو موصی نے مقدم بیان کیا ہے اور یہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جب کہ ثلث ان تمام وصایا کے لئے نا کافی ہو، اس لئے کہ موصی کے بیان سے یہی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ اس نے اس وصیت کو مقدم کیا ہے جو اس کے نزدیک اہم ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر زکوۃ اور حج دونوں جمع ہو جائیں اور یہ دونوں فرائض کے اندر داخل ہیں پھر بھی زکوۃ کو حج پر مقدم کیا جائے گا اور یہ جو امام طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے یہ امام ابو یوسف سے دو روایات میں سے ایک روایت ہے کہ زکوۃ کو حج پر مقدم کیا جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف کی دوسری روایت اور یہی امام محمد کا قول ہے کہ حج کو زکوۃ پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ تنبیہ: شاید صاحب ہدایہ کو کوئی ایسی روایت لی ہوگی کہ امام محمد حج کو زکوۃ پر مقدم فرماتے ہیں ورنہ امام قدوری نے شرح مختصر الکرخی میں اور شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے شرح کافی میں اور شمس الائمہ بیہقی نے کفایہ میں اور صاحب تحفہ نے اور شیخ ابو نصر نے شرح الاقطع میں امام محمد کا قول یہ بیان کیا ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک زکوۃ کو حج پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔

زکوۃ اور حج میں سے کس کو مقدم کیا جائے گا

وجه الأولى انهما وان استويا في الفريضه فالزكوة تعلق بها حق العباد فكان اولى وجه الاخرى ان الحج يقام بالمال والنفس والزكوة بالمال قصرا عليه فكان الحج اقوى ثم تقدم الزكوة والحج على الكفارات لمزيتهما عليها فى القوة اذ قد جاء فيهما من الوعيد ما لم يات فى الكفارة والكفارة فى القتل والظهار واليمين مقدمة على صدقة الفطر لانه عرف وجوبه القران دون صدقة الفطر

ترجمہ: پہلی روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں اگر چہ فرضیت میں برابر ہیں پس زکوۃ کے ساتھ بندوں کا حق متعلق ہے پس زکوۃ اولی ہوگی دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج مال اور جان سے ادا کیا جاتا ہے پس زکوۃ فقط مال سے ادا کی جاتی ہے (جو مال پر مقصود منحصر ہے) تو حج اقوی ہو گا پھر زکوۃ اور حج تمام کفارات پر مقدم ہوں گے ان دونوں کی فضیلت کی وجہ سے کفارات پر قوت کے اندر اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کے بارے میں ایسی وعیدیں ہیں جو کفارہ کے اندر نہیں ہیں اور کفارہ قتل اور کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین صدقہ فطر پر مقدم ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ان کفارات کا وجوب قرآن سے معلوم ہوا ہے نہ کہ صدقہ فطر کا۔

تشریح: زکوۃ اور حج میں کس کو مقدم کیا جائے گا اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں پہلی روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ اور حج اگر چہ دونوں فرض ہیں لیکن زکوۃ کے ساتھ حق اللہ ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ بندوں کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے اس لئے زکوۃ کو حج پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حج مال اور جان سے ادا ہوتا ہے اور زکوة فقط مال سے ادا ہوتی ہے اس لئے حج زکوۃ سے اقوی ہوا اسی لئے حج زکوۃ سے مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ پھر زکوۃ اور حج اور کفارات اگر چہ سب فرائض میں داخل ہیں لیکن کفارات پر زکوۃ اور حج کو مقدم کیا جائے گا، اس لئے کہ زکوۃ اور حج کے بارے میں جو وعیدات وارد ہوئی ہیں وہ کفارات میں نہیں۔

پھر کفارہ قتل اور کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین یہ سب صدقہ فطر پر مقدم ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ان کفارات کا وجوب قرآن سے معلوم ہوا ہے اور صدقہ فطر کا وجوب قرآن سے معلوم نہیں ہوا بلکہ حدیث سے معلوم ہوا ہے۔
When they are equal in strength, one begins with what the testator gave precedence, when the third is insufficient for all, because the apparent meaning is that he begins with the most important. Al-Tahawi mentioned that he begins with zakat and gives it precedence over hajj, and this is one of two narrations from Abu Yusuf. In another narration from him, he gives precedence to hajj, and that is the saying of Muhammad. Explanation: (first proof) Although they are equal in obligation, the right of humans (haqq al-ibad) is attached to zakat, so it is more deserving. (second proof) Hajj is performed with wealth and life, while zakat is performed with wealth only, so hajj is stronger. Then zakat and hajj are given precedence over expiations (kaffarat) due to their superiority in strength, because severe threats have come concerning them that have not come concerning kaffarat. And the expiation for killing, zihar, and an oath are given precedence over sadaqat al-fitr, because their obligation is known from the Quran, unlike sadaqat al-fitr.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and legal reasoning. It first establishes the general rule: when bequests are of equal legal strength (all fara'id, all wajibat, or all tatawwu'), and the third is insufficient, the testator's order of mention determines priority. The assumption is that the testator prioritized what he considered most important. Then it focuses on a specific case: if both zakat and hajj bequests exist (both are fara'id), which is executed first? Imam Tahawi reports that one should begin with zakat. This is one of two narrations from Imam Abu Yusuf. The other narration from Abu Yusuf and the view of Imam Muhammad give precedence to hajj. However, a note (tanbih) points out that many other Hanafi scholars (like Quduri, Sarakhsi, Bayhaqi, etc.) report that Imam Muhammad actually gave precedence to zakat, not hajj. The text then provides the reasoning for each view: the first view (zakat first) argues that although both are fard, zakat involves the right of the poor (haqq al-ibad), so it is stronger. The second view (hajj first) argues that hajj is performed with both wealth and body, making it more comprehensive and thus stronger. Then the passage extends the comparison: zakat and hajj are preferred over kaffarat (expiations) because of the severe warnings in the Quran and hadith about neglecting them. Next, among kaffarat, those that are directly from the Quran (e.g., killing, zihar, oath) are given precedence over sadaqat al-fitr, because sadaqat al-fitr is based on hadith, not explicitly in the Quran.

Key Terms
قوة (quwwa): Legal strength or category: fara'id, wajibat, or tatawwu'.
حق العباد (haqq al-ibad): Rights of human beings, as opposed to purely divine rights (haqq Allah). In this context, zakat involves the right of the poor to receive their due.
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act required for certain sins or violations, such as breaking an oath or invalidating a fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to one narration from Abu Yusuf, why is zakat preferred over hajj in bequests?
A) Because hajj is not obligatory.
B) Because zakat involves the rights of the poor (haqq al-ibad).
C) Because hajj can be performed later.
D) Because zakat is mentioned first in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
When bequests are equal in strength, follow the testator's order; but for zakat and hajj, the Hanafi school has a valid internal dispute based on the presence of human rights versus comprehensiveness of the act.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Precedence of Sadaqat al-Fitr over Udhiyyah
Establishes precedence of sadaqat al-fitr over udhiyyah and general rule for wajibat and voluntary bequests.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over udhiyyah in a will, explain the proof (ijma vs ikhtilaf), and apply the analogy to other wajibat and voluntary bequests.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-fitr takes precedence because its obligation is proven by ijma, while udhiyyah is disputed.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in estate execution: when a testator's bequests include both sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyyah but the estate cannot fulfill both. The ruling hinges on the strength of evidence for each wajib. The author also extends this principle to all wajibat and clarifies that voluntary bequests follow the testator's order of mention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific ruling
Locate the explicit statement: sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over udhiyyah in a will.
The text uses 'مقدمة على' (given precedence).
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
Note that the proof for sadaqat al-fitr's precedence is ijma (consensus) on its obligation, while udhiyyah's obligation is subject to ikhtilaf (disagreement).
Ijma is a qat'i (definitive) proof, making sadaqat al-fitr a stronger wajib.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
Identify that the text extends the same reasoning by qiyas to all wajibat: any wajib with stronger evidence takes precedence over one with weaker evidence.
The phrase 'وعلى هذا القياس' signals the analogical extension.
4
Understand the rule for voluntary bequests
For non-obligatory (voluntary) bequests, the testator's expressed order is followed as if explicitly stated.
This aligns with the earlier principle that the testator's intention governs.
5
Recognize the practical consequence
The ruling ensures that obligations with stronger proof are not overridden by weaker ones in estate distribution.
This prevents injustice to more firmly established duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صدقۃ الفطر کو قربانی سے مقدم کیا جائے گا

وصدقة الفطر مقدمة على الأضحية للاتفاق على وجوبها والاختلاف في الاضحية وعلى هذا القياس يقدم بعض الواجبات على البعض قال وما ليس بواجب قدم منه ما قدمه الموصى لما بينا وصار كما اذا صرح بذالک

ترجمہ: اور صدقہ فطر قربانی پر مقدم ہے اس لئے کہ صدقہ فطر کے وجوب پر اتفاق ہے اور قربانی میں اختلاف ہے اور اسی قیاس پر بعض واجبات بعض پر مقدم کئے جائیں گے۔ اور جس چیز کا واجب ہونا نہیں تو اس میں سے جس کو موصی نے مقدم کیا ہے اس کو مقدم کیا جائے گا جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا اور یہ حکم اس صورت کی طرح ہے جب کہ موصی نے اس کو صراحتاً بیان کیا ہو۔

تشریح: صدقہ فطر اور قربانی دونوں واجبات میں داخل ہیں لیکن صدقہ فطر کے وجوب پر اجماع ہے اور قربانی کے وجوب پر اختلاف ہے اس لئے صدقہ فطر کو قربانی پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ اور اسی قیاس پر بعض واجبات کو بعض پر مقدم کیا جائے گا۔ اور جو وصیت واجب نہیں ہے یعنی تطوع ہے تو اس میں اس کو مقدم کیا جائے گا جس کو موصی نے مقدم کیا ہے۔
Sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over udhiyyah (sacrificial animal) because of the consensus on its obligation and the difference of opinion regarding udhiyyah. And by analogy, some wajibat are given precedence over others. He said: And what is not wajib, among it, what the testator gave precedence is given precedence, as we have stated, and it becomes as if he explicitly stated that.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the order of precedence among wajibat and voluntary bequests. The specific ruling is that sadaqat al-fitr (the charity due at the end of Ramadan) is given precedence over udhiyyah (the sacrificial animal for Eid al-Adha) in wills, because there is consensus (ijma) that sadaqat al-fitr is wajib, while there is disagreement among scholars regarding the obligation of udhiyyah. By analogy (qiyas), other wajibat are prioritized over one another based on the strength of their evidence. The passage then returns to the general rule for non-obligatory (voluntary) bequests: the testator's order of mention is followed, as if he had explicitly stated his preference. This echoes the earlier rule for bequests of equal strength.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): A wajib charity given at the end of Ramadan before the Eid prayer.
الأضحية (al-udhiyyah): The sacrificial animal offered on Eid al-Adha.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of scholars; used here as the proof for sadaqat al-fitr's obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sadaqat al-fitr given precedence over udhiyyah in a will?
A) Because sadaqat al-fitr is more important in the Quran.
B) Because there is consensus (ijma) on its obligation, while udhiyyah is disputed.
C) Because sadaqat al-fitr involves charity to the poor.
D) Because udhiyyah is haram.

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-fitr is prioritized over udhiyyah in bequests due to ijma; this principle extends to all wajibat based on strength of evidence, while voluntary bequests follow the testator's order.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Priority Among Bequests and Division of the Thulth
Commentary on prioritizing bequests and dividing the one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi priority order among bequests and apply the method of dividing the thulth when multiple bequests exist, including both rights of Allah and rights of servants.

Core Idea
Bequests are prioritized by strength of obligation; the thulth is divided proportionally among all bequests.

When a testator makes multiple bequests, not all can be treated equally. Some are given precedence due to their stronger basis in obligation. This lesson, based on the commentary of Al-Hidayah, explains how to prioritize bequests and how to divide the one-third estate when both acts of devotion (qurbat) and personal bequests are involved. You will learn the reasoning behind the priority and the practical method of distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of priority
Determine which bequests are authoritative by consensus (ijma') vs. those with disagreement, and differentiate between obligations directly from Allah and those arising from the servant's actions.
Consensus on obligation gives precedence over disputed obligations; direct divine obligation precedes that caused by human action.
2
Apply the priority order to qurbat
Arrange the qurbat (acts of devotion) in the order: sadaqat al-fitr, then kaffarat and nadhr, then qurbani, then nawafil. Within kaffarat, precedence goes to qatl, then yamin, then zihar.
This order is established by analogy and the relative strength of each obligation.
3
Divide the thulth among multiple bequests
When bequests include both rights of Allah and rights of servants, the thulth is first divided by the total number of bequests, not by type. Each qurbat is counted separately, just as personal bequests are.
This ensures fairness: the share for rights of Allah is further distributed internally according to the priority order.
4
Handle a mixed case example
In the example of Zayd's bequests (zakat, hajj, kaffarat, and to a person), the thulth is divided into four equal shares: one for the person, then among the three qurbat, precedence is applied (zakat first, then hajj, then kaffarat).
This illustrates the full procedure: first allocate to huquq al-ibad, then prioritize among huquq Allah.

The Book of Wills. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume 19. Translation: And sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over qurbani because of consensus on its obligation and difference regarding qurbani, and by this analogy some obligations are given precedence over others. Quduri said: And among those that are not obligatory, precedence is given to what the testator gave precedence, for the same reason we mentioned, and it becomes as if the testator expressly stated it. Explanation: And sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over qurbani because there is consensus among jurists on its obligation, and there is no consensus on the obligation of qurbani. Similarly, some obligations are given precedence over others; thus sadaqat al-fitr is given precedence over nadhr (vows) because sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory by Allah's making it so, while nadhr are obligatory by the servant's making them so. And nadhr and kaffarat are given precedence over qurbani because there is difference on the obligation of qurbani but no difference on the obligation of kaffarat and nadhr. And qurbani is given precedence over nawafil. Then kaffarat al-qatl (expiation for killing) is given precedence over other kaffarat because it is stronger; that is why in kaffarat al-qatl the slave to be freed must be a believer. Then kaffarat al-yamin (expiation for an oath) is given precedence over kaffarat al-zihar because the obligation of kaffarat al-yamin arises from disrespecting Allah's name, while kaffarat al-zihar arises from making one's wife forbidden; thus kaffarat al-yamin is stronger. And if the bequests are not from the obligations but rather supererogatory, then what the testator mentioned first is given precedence, for the reason already mentioned, i.e., the testator prioritizes what he deems important. And if he explicitly stated that the one given precedence should be given precedence, then it is necessary to give it precedence; similarly here precedence is given even if he did not explicitly state it but mentioned it first. The question of what is given precedence between right of Allah and right of servant. They said: The third (thulth) is divided among all bequests, whether for Allah or for a servant; what falls to the share of acts of devotion (qurbat) is spent on them according to the order we mentioned, and it is divided by the number of acts of devotion, and all are not considered as one bequest because the purpose of all is the pleasure of Allah, yet each act of devotion is intended in itself, so each is independent just as bequests for different people are independent. Explanation: Here the author states a new issue. For example, Zayd made several bequests: for zakat, for hajj, for kaffarat, and for Zayd (a person). The first three are rights of Allah and the fourth is right of a servant. What should be done? He said: The thulth is made into four shares; one share is given to Zayd (the person). Then the remaining three shares follow the method already mentioned: from these three qurbat, zakat is given precedence; if after paying zakat some remains, then hajj is given precedence over kaffarat; if something remains for kaffarat, it is also paid. And not? They are counted as four bequests, and the thulth is made into four shares, not that the three are considered one because they are rights of Allah and only two shares are made. Now match this with the text: The thulth is divided over all bequests, i.e., the total of rights of Allah and rights of servants is added, and the thulth is divided by the number of that total. The portion that falls to the share of rights of Allah, within that portion precedence is given as mentioned before. And the thulth is divided by the number of acts of devotion; it is not that all acts of devotion are considered one and divided by two, even though the purpose of all acts of devotion is the pleasure of Allah, but each act of devotion is intended separately, so each is counted separately. For example, Zayd made bequests for the poor, the needy, and travelers: each is counted separately, and a share is taken for each group, even though the purpose of all is devotion. Similarly, all acts of devotion are counted separately.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's matn regarding the order of priority among bequests. The author explains that when multiple bequests are made, some are given precedence based on their strength of obligation. Sadaqat al-fitr is prioritized over qurbani because its obligation is agreed upon, while qurbani's obligation is disputed. This principle extends to other wajibat as well. The text then discusses the division of the thulth when bequests include both huquq Allah and huquq al-ibad. The thulth is divided proportionally by number of bequests, not by type. For acts of devotion (qurbat), each is considered separately because each is independently intended for Allah's pleasure. The example with Zayd's four bequests (zakat, hajj, kaffarat, and to a person) illustrates the method: first separate the portion for human right, then prioritize among the remaining qurbat according to the established order (zakat first, then hajj, then kaffarat).

Key Terms
قربات (qurbat): Acts of devotion or piety, such as zakat, hajj, kaffarat, and qurbani, which bring one closer to Allah.
وصايا (wasaya): Bequests made in a will, which are executed from the one-third of the estate after debts.
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum amount that can be bequeathed in a will without heirs' permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which of the following is given precedence over qurbani?
A) Nawafil (supererogatory acts)
B) Sadaqat al-fitr
C) Bequests for charity to the poor
D) Hajj al-Islam

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, bequests are prioritized based on the strength of their obligation, and the thulth is divided proportionally among all bequests, counting each act of devotion separately.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest for Hajj al-Islam: Method of Performance
Ruling on performing hajj from the testator's town and mode of travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the method of performing a bequest for Hajj al-Islam and explain the rationale behind requiring performance from the testator's town and riding.

Core Idea
A bequest for obligatory hajj must be performed riding from the testator’s own town, replicating the obligation exactly.

When someone makes a bequest for the obligatory hajj (Hajj al-Islam), the Hanafi school prescribes a specific method of performance. This lesson examines the ruling from the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, clarifying that the proxy must perform hajj from the testator's town and while riding, not walking. Understanding this ensures the bequest fulfills the testator's duty correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The subject is a bequest for Hajj al-Islam (the obligatory hajj). The ruling: the heirs must have a man from the testator's town perform hajj riding.
The text says 'احجواعنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا'
2
Understand the rationale (dalil)
The proof is that the obligation of hajj was upon the testator from his town. Therefore, the proxy must replicate the same condition.
The Arabic phrase: 'لان الواجب الله تعالى الحج من بلده'
3
Determine the mode of travel
The text specifies 'riding' because the testator was not obligated to walk. The proxy must perform hajj in the same manner that was obligatory on the testator.
Walking would be insufficient unless the testator had been a pedestrian.
4
Note the cross-madhhab consideration
Some schools may permit performing hajj from a different location or on foot to reduce expenses. The Hanafi position insists on exact replication of the obligation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Ummah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موصی حج کی وصیت کرے تو اس کی ادائیگی کا طریقہ کار قال ومن اوصى بحجة الاسلام احجواعنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا لان الواجب الله تعالى الحج من بلده ولهذا يعتبر فيه من المال ما يكفيه من بلده والوصية لاداء ما هوا لو اجب عليه وانما قال راكبا لانه لا يلزمه ان يحج ما شيا فانصرف اليه على الوجه الذى وجب عليه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے حج اسلام کی وصیت کی تو ورتا اس کی جانب سے کسی شخص کو حج کرائیں گے موصی کے شہر سے جو سوار ہو کر حج کریگا اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے اس کے شہر سے حج کرنا واجب ہے اس وجہ سے وجوب حج میں اتنا مال معتبر ہوگا جو موصی کے شہر سے کافی ہو اور وصیت اس چیز کی ادائیگی کے لئے ہے جو موصی پر واجب ہے اور قدوری نے را کیا فرمایا اس لئے کہ موصی پر پیدل حج کرنا لازم نہیں ہے تو حج اس غیر کی جانب اس طریقہ پر پھرے گا جس طریقہ پر موصی کے اوپر واجب ہے۔ تشریح زید کے اوپر حج فرض ہے اس نے مرض الموت میں وصیت کی کہ میری طرف سے حج کرا دینا ، تو ایسی صورت میں دور تا پر واجب ہوگا کہ اس کے مال سے حج کرائیں اور کسی شخص کو منتخب کریں کہ وہ موصی کے شہر سے حج کرے اور یہ حج پیدل چل کر نہیں بلکہ سوار ہو کر ہوگا۔
The method of performing a bequest for hajj. He said: And whoever makes a bequest for the hajj of Islam, they should perform hajj on his behalf from his town, riding, because what is obligatory on him from Allah is hajj from his town, and for this reason the amount sufficient from his town is considered. The bequest is for fulfilling what was obligatory on him. And he said 'riding' because he is not obliged to perform hajj walking, so it refers to the manner in which it was obligatory on him. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever makes a bequest for Hajj al-Islam, the heirs should have someone perform hajj on his behalf from his town, riding, because Allah has made hajj obligatory from his town; for this reason the amount sufficient from his town is considered in the obligation of hajj. The bequest is for fulfilling what was obligatory on him. And Quduri said 'riding' because he is not obliged to walk, so the hajj on his behalf is performed in the manner that was obligatory on him. Explanation: Zayd has hajj as obligatory; he makes a bequest in his terminal illness saying 'have hajj performed on my behalf'. In this case, it becomes wajib on the heirs to have hajj performed from his wealth, and they choose a person who performs hajj from the testator's town, and this hajj is not walking but riding.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on a bequest for Hajj al-Islam. The Hanafi school (via Quduri) holds that the hajj must be performed from the testator's own town, riding, not walking. This is because the obligation of hajj was on him in that manner - from his town and with the means of transport (riding). Since walking was not required of him, the proxy hajj must also be performed riding. The heirs must allocate sufficient funds for this purpose from the one-third of the estate.

Key Terms
حجة الإسلام (hijjat al-Islam): The obligatory hajj that every able Muslim must perform once in a lifetime.
راكبا (rakiban): Riding on a mount (e.g., camel, horse, or vehicle), as opposed to walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A relative, from the nearest city
B) Any Muslim, from anywhere
C) A person from the testator's town, riding
D) The eldest son, on foot

Key Takeaway
The substitute for the obligatory hajj must replicate the testator's obligation: from his town and riding.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Hajj Bequest: Performing from Hometown or Nearest Possible Point
Rulings on fulfilling a bequest for Hajj when funds are insufficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on executing a bequest for Hajj, distinguishing between the default obligation (hometown, riding) and the istihsan-based concession (nearest possible point).

Core Idea
A Hajj bequest must be fulfilled from the testator's hometown, but if funds are insufficient, istihsan allows performance from the nearest possible point rather than voiding the bequest.

This lesson examines two key rulings from Al-Quduri on the execution of a Hajj bequest. First, the heirs must arrange a proxy from the testator's hometown to perform Hajj riding, mirroring the testator's own obligation. Second, if the one-third of the estate is insufficient for the hometown rate, the bequest is not voided; rather, by istihsan, the proxy performs Hajj from the nearest location that the funds can reach. We will explore the legal reasoning behind these rules, including the interaction between qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is a bequest (wasiyyah) for the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam). The ruling is that the heirs are obligated (wajib) to execute this bequest from the testator's estate.
This obligation arises because Hajj is a debt owed to Allah that must be fulfilled after death if not performed in life.
2
Analyze the default method of performance
The proxy must be a man from the testator's hometown, performing Hajj riding (not walking). This is because the testator's own obligation was to perform Hajj from his hometown, and the method of travel (riding) was the required mode.
The testator's obligation is the standard; the proxy replicates it.
3
Examine the insufficiency scenario
If the one-third of the estate covers only a part of the cost from the hometown, by strict qiyas the bequest would be void (the specified quality is absent). However, by istihsan, the heirs are to have Hajj performed from the nearest location where the funds suffice.
Istihsan overrides qiyas because nullifying the bequest contradicts the testator's primary intention.
4
Understand the illa and istihsan rationale
The effective cause (illa) for qiyas is the necessity of the specified quality; istihsan recognizes that the testator's real intent is to fulfill the Hajj, not the specific location. Hence, partial fulfillment is better than complete voidance.
The commentary distinguishes this from a bequest of manumission where a specific slave is named, indicating that intention varies.
