موصی حج کی وصیت کرے تو اس کی ادائیگی کا طریقہ کار
قال ومن اوصى بحجة الاسلام احجواعنه رجلا من بلده يحج راكبا لان الواجب الله تعالى الحج من بلده ولهذا يعتبر فيه من المال ما يكفيه من بلده والوصية لاداء ما هوا لو اجب عليه وانما قال راكبا لانه لا يلزمه ان يحج ما شيا فانصرف اليه على الوجه الذى وجب عليه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے حج اسلام کی وصیت کی تو ورتا اس کی جانب سے کسی شخص کو حج کرائیں گے موصی کے شہر سے جو سوار ہو کر حج کریگا اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے لئے اس کے شہر سے حج کرنا واجب ہے اس وجہ سے وجوب حج میں اتنا مال معتبر ہوگا جو موصی کے شہر سے کافی ہو اور وصیت اس چیز کی ادائیگی کے لئے ہے جو موصی پر واجب ہے اور قدوری نے را کیا فرمایا اس لئے کہ موصی پر پیدل حج کرنا لازم نہیں ہے تو حج اس غیر کی جانب اس طریقہ پر پھرے گا جس طریقہ پر موصی کے اوپر واجب ہے۔
تشریح زید کے اوپر حج فرض ہے اس نے مرض الموت میں وصیت کی کہ میری طرف سے حج کرا دینا ، تو ایسی صورت میں دور تا پر واجب ہوگا کہ اس کے مال سے حج کرائیں اور کسی شخص کو منتخب کریں کہ وہ موصی کے شہر سے حج کرے اور یہ حج پیدل چل کر نہیں بلکہ سوار ہو کر ہوگا۔
اس لئے کہ زید کے اوپر بھی جو حج فرض تھا وہ اپنے شہر سے واجب تھا اور یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ زید پر اس وقت حج فرض ہوگا جب کہ اس کے پاس اتنا مال ہو جو اس کے شہر سے حج کرنے کے لئے کافی ہو ورنہ اگر زادو را حلہ نہ ہوتو زید پر عدم استطاعت کی وجہ سے حج فرض نہ ہوگا۔
بعد تو جب زید پر حج ادا کرنا اپنے شہر سے واجب ہے اور اس کے مرنے کے بعد جس آدمی سے حج کرایا جائے گا وہ اس حج کی ادائیگی ہے ادا جو زید پر واجب ہے اور زید پر اپنے شہر سے حج کرنا واجب تھا تو یہ بھی زید کے شہر سے حج کرے گا۔ اور یہ غیر جو حج کرے گا سوار ہو کر کرے گا کیونکہ زید کے اوپر پیدل چل کر حج کرنالازم نہیں تھا بلکہ سوار ہو کر واجب تھا تو غیر پر بھی حج کو اسی طریقہ پر ادا کرے گا جس طریقہ پر زید کے اوپر واجب تھا۔
ثلث مال سے وصیت حج پوری نہ ہو سکے تو کیا طریقہ اختیار کیا جائے
قال فان لم تبلغ الوصية النفقة احجو ا عنه من حيث تبلغ وفى القياس لا يحج عنه لا نه امر با لحجة على صفة عدمناها فيه غيرانا جوزناه لانا نعلم ان الموصى قصد تنفيذ الوصية فيجب تنفيذها ما امكن والممكن فيه ما ذكرناه وهو اولى من أبطالها راسا وقد فرقنا بين هذا و بين الوصية بالعتق من قبل
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر مقدار وصیت نفقہ حج کیلئے کافی نہ ہو تو ورثا اس کی جانب سے وہاں سے حج کرائیں جہاں سے پہنچ ہو سکے اور قیاس کے اندر موصی کی جانب سے حج نہیں کرایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ موسی نے حکم دیا حج کرانیکا ایسی صفت پر کہ اس مال میں ہم اس صفت کو معدوم پاتے ہیں علاوہ اس بات کے کہ ہم نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ ہم جانتے ہیں کہ موصی نے وصیت کو نافذ کرنے کا وعدہ کیا ہے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس کی تنفیذ واجب ہو گی اور اس میں وہی طریقہ ممکن ہے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ بالکل وصیت کے ابطال سے اولی ہے اور ہم نے اس کے درمیان اور معتق کی وصیت کے درمیان پہلے فرق بیان کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح ماقبل میں یہ بات متعدد مرتبہ گزر چکی ہے کہ وصیت میت کے ثث مال میں نافذ ہوتی ہے اس سے زیادہ میں نافذ نہیں ہوتی تو اگر مریض نے وصیت کی کہ میرے مال سے حج کرایا جائے گا لیکن اس کا مال اتنا نہیں ہے جس سے حج کرایا جا سکے تو ایسی صورت میں جس جگہ سے حج ہو سکے وہاں سے حج کرایا جائے، مثلاً استعمال ہے کہ جس سے دیو بند سے حج نہیں ہو سکتا البتہ بمبئی سے حج ہو سکتا ہے تو بمبئی سے حج کرایا جائے اور یہ حکم استحسانا ہے ورنہ قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اب موصی کی طرف سے حج ہی نہ کرایا جائے ، اس لئے کہ اس کی وصیت کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ دیوبند سے حج کرایا جائے کیونکہ موصی دیو بند کا باشندہ ہے اور دیو بند سے اتنے مال سے حج ہو نہیں سکتا تو وہ صفت ہی معدوم ہو گئی جو موصی نے بیان کی ہے۔ مگر ہم نے استحسانا اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ ہم کو یہ بات معلوم ہے کہ موصی کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ اس کی وصیت نافذ کی جائے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس کی وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور جو طریقہ بیان کیا گیا ہے یہ طریقہ ممکن ہے لہذا اسی کو اختیار کیا جائے گا۔
The method of performing the Hajj bequest: He said: 'Whoever bequeaths the Hajj of Islam, then he should be made to perform Hajj on his behalf by a man from his town, riding, because the obligation of Allah is Hajj from his town, and for this reason the amount sufficient from his town is considered, and the bequest is for the performance of what was obligatory upon him. And he said 'riding' because walking Hajj is not obligatory upon him, so it turns to the wajib method.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: 'Whoever bequeaths the Hajj of Islam, the heirs should make a person from the testator's town perform Hajj on his behalf, riding, because the obligation of Allah is Hajj from his town, so the amount that suffices from his town is considered, and the bequest is for the performance of what was obligatory upon him. And he said 'riding' because walking Hajj is not obligatory upon him, so the Hajj is performed on the wajib method.' Explanation: Zaid is obligated to perform Hajj; he bequeathed in terminal illness: 'Have Hajj performed on my behalf.' In such a case, it is wajib upon the heirs to have Hajj performed from his wealth and to select a person who performs Hajj from the testator's town, and this Hajj will be performed riding, not walking. Because the Hajj that was fard upon Zaid was wajib from his town, and this is why he became obligated when he had enough wealth from his town; otherwise, if he lacked provisions and mount, Hajj would not be fard due to lack of ability. Then, since it is wajib upon Zaid to perform Hajj from his town, the person who performs on his behalf is fulfilling the duty, so he will also perform from the testator's town. And the proxy will perform riding because Zaid was not required to walk but to ride, so the proxy performs in the same manner. What to do if the bequest from the third is insufficient for Hajj? He said: 'If the bequest does not cover the expenses, then make him perform Hajj from where it reaches. By qiyas, he should not be made to perform Hajj because he commanded a Hajj with a quality that we find absent in the wealth. But we permitted it because we know the testator intended to execute the bequest, so it must be executed as much as possible, and the possible is what we mentioned, and it is better than complete nullification. And we have already distinguished between this and the bequest of manumission.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: 'If the amount of the bequest is insufficient for the expenses of Hajj, then the heirs should have him perform Hajj from where it can reach. By qiyas, he should not be made to perform Hajj because he commanded a Hajj with a quality that we find absent in the wealth. But we permitted it because we know that the testator intended to execute the bequest, so it must be executed as much as possible, and the possible is what we mentioned, and it is better than its complete voidance, and we have already distinguished between this and the bequest of manumission.' Explanation: It has been mentioned multiple times that the bequest is executed from one-third. If the testator bequeathed that Hajj be performed from his wealth, but his wealth is insufficient, then in such a case Hajj is performed from the nearest place from which it can be done. For example, if it is not possible from Deoband but possible from Bombay, then it is performed from Bombay. This ruling is by istihsan. Otherwise, the requirement of qiyas is that Hajj should not be performed on his behalf at all, because his bequest intended Hajj from Deoband (his hometown), and since the wealth is insufficient for that, the specified quality is absent. However, by istihsan we have allowed it because we know that the testator's aim was to execute the bequest, so executing it as much as possible is wajib, and the method mentioned is possible, so it is adopted.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage deals with two sub-rulings regarding a bequest for the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam). First, if the testator bequeaths that Hajj be performed on his behalf, the heirs must arrange for a person from the testator's hometown to perform Hajj riding (not walking). This is because the testator's own obligation was to perform Hajj from his hometown, and the bequest is to fulfill that same obligation. The method of travel (riding) matches what was obligatory upon the testator. Second, if the available wealth from the one-third is insufficient to cover the cost of Hajj from the hometown, the heirs should have Hajj performed from the nearest possible location (e.g., Bombay instead of Deoband). By strict qiyas (analogy), this would not be allowed because the bequest specified a location, and that condition is absent. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), it is permitted because the testator's primary intention was to have Hajj performed, not to specify a location. The alternative would nullify the bequest entirely, which is less desirable. The commentary distinguishes this from a bequest of manumission (where a specific slave is named), where istihsan might not apply. The ruling is based on the principle of fulfilling the bequest as much as possible.

Key Terms
حج الاسلام (Hajjat al-Islam): The obligatory Hajj that every capable Muslim must perform once in a lifetime
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside a strict qiyas in favor of a more just or practical ruling
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning where the ruling of a known case is applied to a new case due to a shared effective cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths Hajj from his hometown, but the one-third is insufficient for that, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The bequest is void
B) Hajj is performed from the nearest possible place
C) The heirs must add their own money
D) Only the available amount is given to the poor

Key Takeaway
Istihsan allows partial fulfillment of a Hajj bequest from the nearest possible location when the specified hometown is unaffordable, prioritizing the testator's primary intent over strict specification.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Executing a Will for Hajj When Funds Are Insufficient
Ruling on executing a will for Hajj with insufficient funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to determine the ruling when a testator's estate cannot cover the prescribed conditions of a will for Hajj.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas to fulfill the testator's intent whenever possible.

A person wills from his one-third that Hajj be performed for him from his hometown, but the estate is insufficient. Strict analogy would void the will entirely. However, the Hanafi school employs istihsan to preserve the purpose of the will: the deceased's desire to have the worship performed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that preference and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and its condition
Recognize that the testator's obligation was to perform Hajj from his own city (his hometown), which sets the default condition for the proxy.
This condition stems from the fact that Hajj becomes obligatory only when one has istita'ah (capability) from one's residence.
2
Apply strict analogy (qiyas)
If the condition cannot be met, by qiyas the will should fail because the commanded attribute (performance from hometown) is absent.
Qiyas reasons: the testator commanded a specific method; that method is impossible, so the command is void.
3
Override with istihsan
Consider the testator's overriding intention: to have Hajj performed. Since it is better to fulfill the will partially than to nullify it entirely, the heirs should arrange Hajj from the nearest location the funds can reach.
The proof is: 'We know the testator intended execution of the will, so execution is obligatory to the extent possible.'
4
Note the distinction from freeing a slave
The text mentions that the ruling for a will to free a slave differs (discussed earlier); here the emphasis is on preserving the act of worship.
This highlights that istihsan may apply differently depending on the nature of the act (worship vs. manumission).

کے درمیان پہلے فرق بیان کر دیا ہے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں یہ بات متعدد مرتبہ گزر چکی ہے کہ وصیت میت کے ثث مال میں نافذ ہوتی ہے اس سے زیادہ میں نافذ نہیں ہوتی تو اگر مریض نے وصیت کی کہ میرے مال سے حج کرایا تو بمبئی سے حج کرایا جائے اور یہ حکم استحسانا ہے ورنہ قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ اب موصی کی طرف سے حج ہی نہ کرایا جائے ، اس لئے کہ اس کی وصیت کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ دیوبند سے حج کرایا جائے کیونکہ موصی دیو بند کا باشندہ ہے اور دیو بند سے اتنے مال سے حج ہو نہیں سکتا تو وہ صفت ہی معدوم ہو گئی جو موصی نے بیان کی ہے۔ مگر ہم نے استحسانا اس کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اس لئے کہ ہم کو یہ بات معلوم ہے کہ موصی کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ اس کی وصیت نافذ کی جائے تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو اس کی وصیت کو نافذ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور جو طریقہ بیان کیا گیا ہے یہ طریقہ ممکن ہے لہذا اسی کو اختیار کیا جائے گا۔ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ ۱۸۵ کتاب الوصايا اور اس امکانی طریقہ پر وصیت کو نافذ کر دینا مطلق وصیت کو باطل کر دینے سے افضل ہے۔ اور ماقبل میں یہ بحث گزر چکی ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک حج کی وصیت کرنے میں اور غلام آزاد کرنے کی وصیت میں کیا فرق ہے۔
From Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Bidaya, Volume 19: Because the Hajj that was obligatory upon Zayd was due from his own city, and this is the reason why Hajj becomes obligatory upon Zayd only when he possesses enough wealth to perform Hajj from his city; otherwise, if he lacks provisions and mount, Hajj is not obligatory due to lack of capability. Then, when performing Hajj from his city is obligatory upon Zayd, and after his death the person hired to perform Hajj for him is performing the same obligation that was upon Zayd, and since Hajj from his city was obligatory upon Zayd, this proxy will also perform Hajj from Zayd's city. And this proxy will perform Hajj riding, because it was not necessary for Zayd to walk but rather riding was obligatory; so the proxy will perform it in the same manner as it was obligatory upon Zayd. [Heading:] If the will's amount is insufficient for Hajj expenses, what method should be adopted? He said: If the will does not cover the expenses, have Hajj performed for him from wherever it reaches. By qiyas, Hajj should not be performed for him because the testator commanded Hajj with a specific attribute (from his city) which we find absent in this wealth. However, we permit it because we know that the testator intended to execute the will, so it must be executed as much as possible. What is possible is what we have mentioned, and this is better than completely invalidating it. We have previously distinguished between this and the will for freeing a slave. Translation: al-Quduri said: So if the amount of the will is insufficient for Hajj expenses, the heirs should have Hajj performed for him from wherever it is possible. According to qiyas, Hajj would not be performed for him because the testator commanded Hajj with a specific condition which we find lacking in this wealth. However, we have permitted it because we know that the testator intended to fulfill the will, so fulfilling it as much as possible is obligatory. What is possible is what we have mentioned, and this is better than total annulment. We have already explained the distinction between this and the will for freeing a slave. Commentary: It has passed multiple times that a will is executed from one-third of the deceased's estate, not more. So if the testator willed that Hajj be performed from his wealth, but his wealth is insufficient, then in such a case Hajj should be performed from wherever possible. For example, if it cannot be performed from Deoband but can from Bombay, then perform from Bombay. This ruling is by istihsan. Otherwise, qiyas would require not performing Hajj at all because the will specified Hajj from Deoband (the testator's hometown) and that condition is unfulfillable. But we permit it by istihsan because we know the testator's purpose was to have his will executed, so it is obligatory to execute it as much as possible. The method mentioned is possible, so it will be adopted. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 19, page 185, Kitab al-Wasaya: And executing the will in this possible manner is superior to completely nullifying the will. And we have already discussed the difference between the will for Hajj and the will for freeing a slave according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the execution of a will for Hajj when the testator's estate does not have sufficient funds to cover the journey from his hometown. The commentator first establishes the principle that the obligation of Hajj is tied to the capability (istita'ah) from one's own city; thus the proxy performing Hajj must depart from the same starting point. Then he addresses the scenario where the testator's wealth, limited to one-third, cannot cover Hajj expenses from his city. By strict analogy (qiyas), the condition specified in the will cannot be met, so the will would be void. However, by juristic preference (istihsan), the heirs are instructed to have Hajj performed for the deceased from whichever location the funds can reach, even if it is not his hometown. The proof is the intention of the testator: his primary aim was to have the worship performed, not to mandate a specific starting point. Therefore, fulfilling the will to the extent possible (attanfidh ma amkan) takes precedence over nullifying it entirely. The commentator further clarifies that there is a difference between a will for Hajj and a will for freeing slaves, a point previously discussed in the text.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will directing an act of worship or charity to be performed after death from one-third of the estate.
حج (hajj): The pilgrimage to Makkah, here being performed by a proxy (badal) on behalf of a deceased person as per his will.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on public good or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The will is void because the condition cannot be met.
B) Hajj should be performed from the nearest location where the funds suffice, by istihsan.
C) The heirs must add their own money to cover the full journey.
D) The Hajj should be performed from the deceased's hometown regardless of cost.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas to execute a will for Hajj from the nearest possible location, honoring the testator's primary intent.

Definition of Neighbors in a Will: Qiyas vs. Istihsan within the Hanafi School
Dispute on the scope of 'neighbors' in a will between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on the scope of 'neighbors' in a will, and identify the respective proofs (qiyas and istihsan) and their practical implications.

Core Idea
A will for 'neighbors' divides the Hanafi school: adjacent only (qiyas) or all in the mosque community (istihsan).

When a testator leaves a bequest to 'his neighbors,' who qualifies? This question sparked a classic intra-Hanafi debate. The passage from al-Hidayah presents both the qiyas-based view of Imam Abu Hanifa and the istihsan-based view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school weighs literal meaning against customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Clarify the type of neighbor in dispute
Both sides agree that 'neighbor' here means neighbor by house (jar al-dar), not by kinship or land. The disagreement is on the scope: only physically adjacent (mulasiq), or also those in the same locality sharing a mosque.
This consensus is important before examining the dispute.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's qiyas argument
Abu Hanifa restricts to adjacent neighbors. His qiyas: 'jar' derives from 'mujawara' (adjacency). The same principle applies in shuf'a (pre-emption), where only adjacent neighbors have the right. Since it is impossible to include all possible meanings, the most specific (adjacent) is taken.
The illa (effective cause) is physical contiguity (mulasaqa).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's istihsan argument
Sahibayn include both adjacent and non-adjacent residents of the same locality who attend the same mosque. Their istihsan is based on custom (urf) and a hadith: 'No prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque,' interpreted broadly to mean anyone hearing the adhan. The purpose of benevolence is better served with a broader inclusion.
Customary usage ('urf) overrides literal meaning here.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a testator leaves one-third of his estate to his 'neighbors,' under Abu Hanifa only the adjacent neighbor(s) receive the entire amount. Under Sahibayn, both adjacent and non-adjacent residents of the locality who share the mosque share proportionally.
Later Hanafi practice often adopts Sahibayn's view due to custom.

Chapter of will for relatives and others. Translation: This is a chapter about making a will for relatives and non-relatives. Explanation: In this chapter, mention is made of a will for a specific group, while previous chapters were general; this is specific, and the general takes precedence over the specific, so this chapter is mentioned later. The meaning of neighbor, statements of jurists. He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever makes a will for his neighbors, they are the adjacent ones according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Sahibayn) said: They are the adjacent ones and others who reside in the testator's locality and are gathered by the mosque of the locality, and this is istihsan, and his (Abu Hanifa's) statement is qiyas because neighbor (jar) is derived from adjacency (mujawara) and adjacency in reality is contiguity (mulasaqa), and for this reason the neighbor is entitled to pre-emption (shuf'a) due to this adjacency, and because when it is impossible to direct (the will) to all, it is directed to the most specific, which is the adjacent one. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever makes a will for his neighbors, so they are the adjacent ones according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Sahibayn) said: They are the adjacent ones and besides them those who reside in the testator's locality and whom the mosque of the locality gathers, and this is istihsan. And Abu Hanifa's statement is qiyas because 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara' and 'mujawara' in reality is contiguity, for this reason the neighbor is entitled to shuf'a due to this adjacency, and because when it is impossible to direct the will to all, it is directed to the most specific, which is the adjacent neighbor. Explanation: Zaid made a will that one-third of my wealth is for my neighbors. So which neighbor is intended? Because there are several types of neighbors: one is neighbor by kinship (jar qaraba), meaning neighbor with kinship; second is neighbor of land (jar ard), meaning neighbor by land; third is neighbor of house (jar dar), meaning neighbor by house. Here by consensus, 'neighbor' does not mean neighbor by kinship or neighbor by land, but rather neighbor by house is intended. Then there is a difference in its interpretation. So Imam Abu Hanifa said that by 'neighbors' is meant those whose house is attached and adjacent to the testator's house, whether their doors are near or far. And the two (Sahibayn) said that 'neighbors' includes the adjacent ones and also includes those who live in the testator's locality and are worshipers in the testator's mosque. The statement of Sahibayn is istihsan, and Imam Abu Hanifa's is qiyas. The proof of qiyas is that 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara', and true mujawara is called contiguity. Therefore, the will is for those whose house is attached to the testator's house, and the adjacent neighbor is also entitled to shuf'a due to adjacency; other people will not be entitled to shuf'a. And the second reason is that directing the will to all neighbors is not possible because neighbors by kinship and by land are not included in it; rather specification has been made, so it is directed to the most specific, and the most specific is the adjacent neighbor. The proof of istihsan: The aspect of istihsan is that all these people are called neighbors customarily, and it is supported by his (the Prophet's) saying: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque,' and it is interpreted by everyone who hears the call (adhan). And because the purpose of the will for neighbors and its recommendation includes the adjacent and others, but interaction (ikhtilat) is necessary, and that occurs when the mosque is common. Translation: The proof of istihsan is that all these people are customarily called neighbors, and it is supported by the command of the Messenger (peace be upon him) that the prayer of the neighbor of the mosque is not valid except in the mosque, and he (ʿAli?) interpreted it as everyone who hears the adhan. And because the purpose of the will for neighbors and its recommendation encompasses the adjacent and others, but interaction is necessary, and interaction will occur when the mosque is common. Explanation: This is the proof of istihsan that in custom, all these people who live in one locality and are worshipers of one mosque are called neighbors, and a hadith supports it: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque,' meaning the prayer of the neighbor of the mosque will only be in the mosque. Here the neighbor of the mosque does not mean the person whose house is attached to the mosque, but rather every person who hears the adhan of the mosque.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage addresses the interpretation of the word 'jiran' (neighbors) when a testator makes a will for his neighbors. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) regarding who qualifies as a beneficiary under such a will.

First, the text clarifies that 'neighbor' here refers to the neighbor of the house (jar al-dar), not a neighbor by kinship or land, as agreed upon. The disagreement is on the scope: does it include only those whose property is physically adjacent (mulasiq) to the testator's, or also those who live in the same locality (mahalla) and share the same mosque?

Imam Abu Hanifa holds that only the adjacent neighbor (mulasiq) is included. His reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy): the word 'jar' is derived from 'mujawara', which literally means contiguity. The same principle is applied in shuf'a (pre-emption), where only adjacent neighbors have the right of pre-emption. Additionally, since it is impossible to include all possible meanings of 'neighbor', the will is interpreted to refer to the most specific category, which is the adjacent one.

The Sahibayn, on the other hand, hold that 'neighbors' includes both the adjacent ones and those who live in the same locality and attend the same mosque. Their view is based on istihsan (juristic preference), supported by 'urf (custom) and a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the neighbor of the mosque. They argue that customarily, all residents of a locality are called neighbors, and the purpose of the will (doing good to neighbors) is better fulfilled by including a broader group. The Prophet's statement that a neighbor of the mosque should pray in the mosque is interpreted to refer to anyone who hears the adhan, not just those physically adjacent. The condition for inclusion is that there is regular interaction (ikhtilat), which is achieved by sharing the same mosque.

The passage does not give a preference between the two views, presenting both as valid positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جار (jar): Neighbor; in this context, specifically a neighbor by house (jar al-dar), not by kinship or land.
ملاصق (mulasiq): Physically adjacent or contiguous; a neighbor whose property touches the testator's property.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that allows departure from qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or other considerations.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a basis for Imam Abu Hanifa's view that 'neighbors' in a will means only adjacent residents?
A) The hadith about the neighbor of the mosque.
B) Customary usage in the society.
C) The literal meaning of the word 'jar' and the principle of shuf'a.
D) The consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
In a will for 'neighbors', the Hanafi school has two interpretations: Abu Hanifa restricts to adjacent neighbors (qiyas), while the Sahibayn expand to all locality residents sharing the mosque (istihsan), with the latter often preferred in practice.

Defining 'Jar' (Neighbor) for a Will: Hanafi Inclusivity
Defines 'jar' for wasiyyah with Shafi'i dispute and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'jar' (neighbor) in the context of a will (wasiyyah) and distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a resident slave.

Core Idea
The Hanafi 'jar' includes all neighbors; a resident slave is included by Abu Hanifa but excluded by the Sahibayn.

In this passage, we examine the legal definition of 'jar' (neighbor) as it relates to a bequest (wasiyyah). The Hanafi school adopts a broad interpretation based on linguistic generality, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to forty houses. Additionally, there is an internal difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether a resident slave qualifies as a neighbor. Understanding this definition is crucial for determining the valid beneficiaries of a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: how is 'jar' (neighbor) defined for the purpose of a will? The definition determines who can receive a bequest when the testator uses the word 'neighbor'.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that 'jar' extends to forty houses (ten in each direction) and cites a hadith as evidence. Identify this view and its basis.
The hadith is considered weak by Hanafi scholars.
3
Analyze the Hanafi critique
The Hanafi author rejects the Shafi'i view, calling the hadith weak and the restriction 'far-fetched' (ba'id). The Hanafi position relies on the linguistic generality of the word 'jar'.
Linguistic principle: 'al-asl fi al-alfaz al-haqiqah al-lughawiyyah'.
4
Enumerate the inclusive categories
Under the Hanafi definition, 'jar' includes: resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi. List these categories from the text.
The term covers all who live near the testator.
5
Pinpoint the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A resident slave whose house is adjacent to the testator: Imam Abu Hanifa includes him due to the generality of 'jar'; the Sahibayn exclude him because the bequest would effectively go to the absent master. Identify both views and the reasoning.
This is an example of the Sahibayn's methodological caution regarding ownership.

پڑوسی کے بارے میں امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وما قاله الشافعى الجوار الى اربعين دار ابعيد وما يروى فيه ضعيف قالو او يستوى فيه الساکن و المالك والذكر والانثى والمسلم والدمى لان اسم الجاريتنا ولهم ويدخل فيه العبد الساكن عنده لا طلاقه ولا يدخل ما لان لـ الوصية له وصية لمولاه وهو لاد وهو غير ماکن
ترجمہ اور جو بات کی شافعی نے فرمائی ہے کہ پڑوس چالیس ۴۰ گھروں تک ہے یہ بات بعید ہے اور اس میں جو حدیث روایت کی جاتی ہے وہ ضعیف ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے اور اس میں ساکن اور مالک اور مرد اور عورت اور مسلم اور ڈمی سب برابر ہیں اس لئے کہ لفظ جاران تمام کو شامل ہے اور اس میں ساکن غلام داخل ہے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جار کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک داخل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ غلام کے لئے وصیت ہو گی حالانکہ آقا سا کن نہیں ہے۔ تشریح امام شافعی نے فرماتے ہیں کہ پڑوس چالیس گھروں تک ہے یعنی ہر سمت سے دس دس گھر تک ، اور یہ حدیث بھی ہے جس سے امام شافعی نے استدلال کیا ہے ، تو اس کے بارے میں مصنف نے فرمایا کہ امام شافعی کی یہ بات بعید از قیاس ہے اور جو حد بیث انہوں نے پیش کی ہے یہ حدیث ضعیف ہے۔ پھر علی اختلاف القولین جار میں خواہ وہ ہو جو اس مکان یا محلہ میں مالکانہ حیثیت سے رہتا ہو یا وہ ہو جو عاریت وغیرہ کے طریقہ پر رہتا ہو اور خواہ مرد ہو یا عورت ہو اور خواہ مسلمان ہو یا ڈمی ہو اس لئے کہ لفظ جار میں یہ سب داخل ہیں۔ اور اگر کوئی غلام رہتا ہو اور اس کا گھر موصی کے گھر سے ملاصق ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ غلام بھی وصیت میں داخل ہوگا اس لئے کہ جار کے اطلاق میں غلام بھی داخل ہے، اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام ساکن جار کے اندر داخل ہوگا اور وہ وصیت کا حقدار نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ اگر غلام کے لئے وصیت کو جائز مان لیا جائے تو یہ وصیت اس کے آقا کیلئے ہو جائے گی حالانکہ یہاں نہیں رہتا اور نہ وہ موصی کا
پڑوی ہے۔
Imam Shafi'i's view on neighbor: He said neighbor extends to forty houses (ten on each side), and the hadith he relies on is weak. The Hanafi scholars say: the term 'jar' includes equally the resident and owner, male and female, Muslim and dhimmi, because the word 'jar' encompasses all. It also includes a resident slave according to Abu Hanifa due to the generality of 'jar', but according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the slave is not included because a bequest to a slave goes to his master (who is not a resident neighbor). Commentary: Imam Shafi'i's view is improbable, and his hadith is weak. The word 'jar' includes any person living in the house, whether as owner or tenant, male or female, Muslim or dhimmi. If a slave resides next door, Abu Hanifa includes him; the Sahibayn exclude him because the bequest would benefit the absent master, not the slave as a neighbor.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling on the term 'jar' (neighbor) in the context of a will (wasiyyah). The author first presents the view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who defines a neighbor as extending forty houses (ten in each direction), citing a hadith. The Hanafi scholars reject this, calling the hadith weak and the definition irrational. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the word 'jar' applies to all persons who live near the testator, whether owners or tenants, males or females, Muslims or dhimmis. An intra-Hanafi disagreement arises regarding a resident slave: Imam Abu Hanifa includes the slave because the word 'jar' linguistically covers him, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) exclude him on the basis that a bequest to a slave would actually go to his master, who is not a neighbor. The text does not specify which view is mufta bihi, but the broader Hanafi position on inclusivity is emphasized.

Key Terms
جار (jar): In this context, 'jar' means a neighbor who lives near the testator, including owner, tenant, and resident slave.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a person for others after death.
ملاصق (mulasiq): Adjacent or immediately next door.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, who is included in the term 'jar' for a will?
A) Only the immediate neighbor (mulasiq)
B) Only the owner of the house
C) All neighbors regardless of gender, religion, and whether owner or tenant
D) Only Muslims and male neighbors

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'jar' broadly to include all neighbors, rejecting the Shafi'i limitation and differing internally over a resident slave.

Definition of 'Ashar' (In-Laws) in Wasiyyah
Defines 'ashar' with hadith proof and extension

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mahram relatives included in a will for 'ashar' by applying the Hanafi definition based on the chosen interpretation of Imam Muhammad and Abu Ubaydah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi wasiyyah, 'ashar' includes all mahram relatives of the spouse and extends to similar in-law relationships.

This passage from al-Hidayah defines the term 'ashar' (in-laws) in the context of a will (wasiyyah). The definition determines who qualifies as a beneficiary when someone bequeaths to his 'ashar'. The authors clarify that the term includes all mahram relatives of the testator's wife, and then extend the definition to include mahram relatives of other in-laws. The preferred Hanafi interpretation is supported by a prophetic practice and is the choice of Imam Muhammad and Abu Ubaydah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and context
Focus on the term 'ashar' as used in a will (wasiyyah). The passage begins with a quotation from al-Quduri: 'If someone makes a will for his ashar...'
The term appears in the context of specifying beneficiaries.
2
State the core definition
According to the passage, the will is for every mahram relative (dhu rahm mahram) of the testator's wife. List examples: wife's father, brother, uncle, etc.
Mahram means permanently prohibited from marriage due to blood kinship.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is a hadith about the Prophet's marriage to Juwayriyyah (or Safiyyah), where he freed mahram relatives of his wife and called them his ashar. This indicates that such relatives are included.
The hadith is cited as evidence that the Prophet treated these relatives as his ashar.
4
Note the preferred interpretation
The passage states that this interpretation is the choice (ikhtiyar) of Imam Muhammad and Abu Ubaydah. It is the mufta bihi position.
This implies there may be alternative definitions, but this is the relied-upon one.
5
Apply the extension
The passage extends the definition: 'ashar' also includes mahram relatives of the testator's father's wife, his son's wife, and the mahram relatives of any of the testator's own mahram relatives.
This ensures comprehensive coverage of in-law relationships.

اصہار کا مصداق اول
قال ومن اوصى لا صهاره فالوصية لكل ذى رحم محرم من امراته لماروى ان النبي عليه السلام لما تزوج صفية اعتق كل من ملك من ذى رحم محرم منها اكراما لها وكانوا يسمون اصهار النبي عليه السلام وهذا التفسير اختيار محمد و ابي عبيدة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے اصہار کے لئے وصیت کی تو وصیت اس کی بیوی کے ہر ذی رحم محرم کے لئے ہوگی بوجہ اس کے کہ مروی ہے کہ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب صفیہ سے نکاح کیا تو ہر اس شخص نے آزاد کر دیا تھا جو ان کے ذی رحم محرم کا مالک تھا صفیہ کے اکرام میں اور یہ لوگ نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کے امہار کے ساتھ نام رکھے جاتے تھے اور یہ غیر محمد اور ابوعبید کا مختار ہے۔ تشریح ایک شخص نے اپنے اصہار کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس وصیت میں کون لوگ داخل ہوں گے تو فرمایا کہ بیوی کے تمام ذورحم محرم اس میں داخل ہوں گے ، یعنی اس کی بیوی کے اہل قرابت میں سے وہ مرد داخل ہوں گے جس کی قرابت اس کی زوجہ کے ساتھ از راہ نسب اس طرح ہو کہ شرعاوہ اس کا محرم ہو یعنی اس کی زوجہ کو اس کے ساتھ دائگی نکاح کرنا حرام ہو جیسے زوجہ کا باپ اور بھائی اور ماموں اور چیاو نمیرہ ، پیس عورت کے ایسے قرابتی اس کے شوہر کے اصہار ہیں اور یہ عرب کا عرف ہے اور ہمارے ملک میں صبر کا ترجمہ خسر سے کرتے ہیں۔ اب اس پر مصنف نے ایک روایت کا حوالہ دیا ہے کہ جب نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت صفیہ سے نکاح کیا تھا تو ان کے ذی رحم محرم جس صحابی کی ملکیت میں تھا اس نے صفیہ کے اکرام میں اس کو آزاد کر دیا اور یہ لوگ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اصہار کہلاتے تھے اور اصہار سے یہ لوگ مراد ہیں، اس تفسیر کو امام محمد نے اور ابو عبیدہ نے اختیار کیا ہے۔
یہاں مصنف نے حضرت صفیہ کا ذکر کیا ہے جو یہود خیبر کے شرفاء میں سے تھیں، جب خیبر فتح کیا گیا تو یہ گرفتار ہوکر آئیں رت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو اپنے لئے منتخب فرمالیا اور پھر آزاد کر کے اس آزادی پر ان سے نکاح فرمالیا، اور یہود خیبر کو رہا کر کے بطور کاشتکاروں کے بٹائی پر جب تک چاہیں چھوڑ دیا پس صفیہ کے اقارب کو بصفت مذکورہ آزاد نہیں کیا گیا لہذا صفیہ کا ذکر ہوا ہوا ہے، اور حقیقت میں یہ واقعہ جویریہ بنت الحارث کا ہے، جس کا واقعہ یہ ہے کہ جویریہ کا باپ بنو مصطلق کا سردار تھا جب نبی مصطلق سے جہاد کیا گیا اور ان کو قید کیا گیا تو جومیر یہ بھی قید ہو کر آئیں اور یہ ثابت بن قیس یا ان کے چیرے بھائی کے حصہ میں پڑیں اور انھوں نے اپنے آپ کو مکاتبہ کر لیا اور جو یہ یہ بہت خوبصورت تھیں ۔ یہ خلاصہ کلام جویریہ نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ یا رسول اللہ میں جویریہ بنت الحارث ہوں اور جو کچھ میرا واقعہ اور جو ہواوہ آپ سے پوشیدہ نہیں ہے اور میں ثابت بن قیس کے حصہ میں پڑی ہوں ، پس میں نے اپنی جان کو مکا تبہ کر لیا ہے پس میں آپ کے دربار میں اس لئے حاضر ہوئی ہوں کہ آپ سے اداء کتابت کے بارے میں سوال کروں ۔ تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تو اس سے بہتر چاہتی ہے اس نے کہا وہ کیا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ میں تیرا بدل کتابت ادا کر دوں اور تجھ سے نکاح کرلوں اس نے اس کو منظور کر لیا۔ اور آپ نے بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا اور آپ نے ان سے نکاح کر لیا جب لوگوں کو یہ معلوم ہوا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جویریہ سے نکاح کر لیا ہے تو جس کے قبضہ میں بنو مصطلق سے کوئی قیدی مملوک تھا اس نے اس کو رہا کر دیا اور کہنے لگے کہ یہ لوگ تو اب آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اظہار ہیں الخ ۔
مصداق خانی
و كذا يدخل فيه كل ذى رحم محرم من زوجة ابيه وزوجة ابنه وزوجة كل ذي رحم محرم منه لان الكل أصهار
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اس میں موصی کے باپ بیوی کا ہر ذی رحم محرم داخل ہے اور موصی کے بیٹے کی بیوی کا اور موصی کے ہر ذی رحم محرم
First definition of ashar (in-laws): Al-Quduri said: If someone makes a will for his ashar, the will is for every mahram relative of his wife, because it is narrated that when the Prophet married Safiyyah, he freed every mahram relative of hers who was owned by a person, as a honor to her, and those people were called the Prophet's ashar. This interpretation is the choice of Muhammad and Abu Ubaydah. Commentary: The will for ashar includes all mahram relatives of the wife, meaning male relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as father, brother, uncle, etc. This is the Arab custom. The author then mentions the narration of Safiyyah, but the correct narration is about Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith. The full story: Juwayriyyah fell into captivity, made a kitabah contract, the Prophet paid it and married her, upon which the Muslims freed all captives from Banu Mustaliq saying they are now the Prophet's ashar. Also included are mahram relatives of the testator's father's wife, son's wife, and of any mahram relative of the testator, because all are considered ashar.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling on the term 'ashar' (in-laws) in the context of a will. It begins with a quotation from al-Quduri stating that a will for 'ashar' applies to every mahram relative of the testator's wife. Mahram relatives are those with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood kinship, such as the wife's father, brother, maternal uncle, etc. The preferred interpretation is that of Imam Muhammad and Abu Ubaydah, who base this on the historical incident of the Prophet's marriage to Safiyyah (or more correctly Juwayriyyah), where the in-laws were freed as a mark of honor. The passage then extends the definition: 'ashar' also includes mahram relatives of the testator's father's wife, his son's wife, and the mahram relatives of any of the testator's own mahram relatives (e.g., the wife of his maternal uncle). This comprehensive definition ensures that all individuals connected by marriage in a prohibited degree are considered in-laws for the purpose of the will.

Key Terms
اصهار (ashar): In this context, 'ashar' refers to the mahram relatives of one's spouse, and also the mahram relatives of the spouse of one's father, son, or other mahram relatives.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahm mahram): A male relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood kinship (e.g., father, brother, uncle).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only the testator's in-laws by blood

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'ashar' in a will includes all mahram relatives of the spouse and extends to other in-law relationships, based on the prophetic practice.

Defining 'As-har' in Bequests: Scope and Custom
Defining the scope of 'as-har' in bequests with extension and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'as-har' in Hanafi law, identify all male mahram relatives included in a bequest to 'as-har', and apply the ruling to extended marital connections.

Core Idea
As-har in bequests includes all mahram relatives of the wife and extends to mahrams of other marital links.

When a testator bequeaths to his 'as-har', the scope of this term determines who receives. The Hanafi school adopts a broad definition based on custom and prophetic practice, covering not only the wife's mahrams but also those of the father's wife, son's wife, and every mahram relative's wife. This lesson unpacks the definition, its proof, and its application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic definition
Start with the core: 'as-har' refers to the male mahram relatives of one's wife, such as her father, brother, and uncle. These are in-laws through marriage.
Mahram means a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
2
Recognize the extension
The definition expands to include mahram relatives of the testator's father's wife, son's wife, and the wife of every mahram relative of the testator. All these are 'as-har' because of the marital connection.
This is based on the principle that sihr (marital relationship) creates affinity.
3
Examine the dalil
The Prophet's marriage to Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith is cited. When he married her, the companions freed their captives from Banu Mustaliq, calling them the Prophet's 'as-har'. This establishes that in-laws include the wife's entire tribe.
The narration shows practical application of the term.
4
Note the role of 'urf
The definition is rooted in Arab custom. In some localities, 'as-har' is limited to the wife's father (khusar). The Hanafi ruling follows the wider custom unless a narrower local custom is established.
Custom can restrict or expand the scope.
5
Apply to a bequest scenario
If a testator bequeaths 1/3 of his estate to his 'as-har', distribute to all male mahram relatives of his wife, plus those of his father's wife, son's wife, etc., proportionally.
The executor must identify all qualifying relatives.

یہاں مصنف نے حضرت صفیہ کا ذکر کیا ہے جو یہود خیبر کے شرفاء میں سے تھیں، جب خیبر فتح کیا گیا تو یہ گرفتار ہوکر آئیں رت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان کو اپنے لئے منتخب فرمالیا اور پھر آزاد کر کے اس آزادی پر ان سے نکاح فرمالیا، اور یہود خیبر کو رہا کر کے بطور کاشتکاروں کے بٹائی پر جب تک چاہیں چھوڑ دیا پس صفیہ کے اقارب کو بصفت مذکورہ آزاد نہیں کیا گیا لہذا صفیہ کا ذکر ہوا ہوا ہے، اور حقیقت میں یہ واقعہ جویریہ بنت الحارث کا ہے، جس کا واقعہ یہ ہے کہ جویریہ کا باپ بنو مصطلق کا سردار تھا جب نبی مصطلق سے جہاد کیا گیا اور ان کو قید کیا گیا تو جومیر یہ بھی قید ہو کر آئیں اور یہ ثابت بن قیس یا ان کے چیرے بھائی کے حصہ میں پڑیں اور انھوں نے اپنے آپ کو مکاتبہ کر لیا اور جو یہ یہ بہت خوبصورت تھیں ۔ یہ خلاصہ کلام جویریہ نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں آکر عرض کیا کہ یا رسول اللہ میں جویریہ بنت الحارث ہوں اور جو کچھ میرا واقعہ اور جو ہواوہ آپ سے پوشیدہ نہیں ہے اور میں ثابت بن قیس کے حصہ میں پڑی ہوں ، پس میں نے اپنی جان کو مکا تبہ کر لیا ہے پس میں آپ کے دربار میں اس لئے حاضر ہوئی ہوں کہ آپ سے اداء کتابت کے بارے میں سوال کروں ۔ تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تو اس سے بہتر چاہتی ہے اس نے کہا وہ کیا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ میں تیرا بدل کتابت ادا کر دوں اور تجھ سے نکاح کرلوں اس نے اس کو منظور کر لیا۔ اور آپ نے بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا اور آپ نے ان سے نکاح کر لیا جب لوگوں کو یہ معلوم ہوا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جویریہ سے نکاح کر لیا ہے تو جس کے قبضہ میں بنو مصطلق سے کوئی قیدی مملوک تھا اس نے اس کو رہا کر دیا اور کہنے لگے کہ یہ لوگ تو اب آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اظہار ہیں الخ ۔

The book of bequests: And these people were named with the in-laws of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and this is the choice of non-Muhammad and Abu Ubayd. Explanation: A person made a bequest for his in-laws, so who will be included in this bequest? He said: All blood relatives who are mahram from the wife will be included, meaning from the wife's kinfolk, those men whose relationship with the wife is such that, by blood, they are legally her mahram, i.e., perpetual marriage with the wife is forbidden for him, like the wife's father, brother, maternal uncle, etc. Such relatives of the woman are the husband's in-laws. And this is the custom of the Arabs. And in our country, the translation of 'sihr' is 'khusar'. Upon this, the author referred to a narration that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) married Safiyya, her blood relative who was mahram and a slave of a companion, was freed in honor of Safiyya, and these people were called the Prophet's in-laws. And this interpretation was adopted by Imam Muhammad and Abu Ubayda. Here the author mentioned Safiyya, who was from the nobles of Khaybar Jews. When Khaybar was conquered, she was taken captive. The Prophet selected her for himself, then freed her and married her upon that freedom. And he released the Jews of Khaybar as sharecroppers as long as they wished. So Safiyya's relatives were not freed as such. Therefore, Safiyya was mentioned, but in reality this incident is about Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith. Her story is that Juwayriyyah's father was the chief of Banu Mustaliq. When jihad was done against Banu Mustaliq and they were taken captive, Juwayriyyah also came captive and fell into the share of Thabit ibn Qays or his cousin. They made a kitabah for themselves. Juwayriyyah was very beautiful. Summary: Juwayriyyah came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, I am Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith, and what happened to me is not hidden from you. I am in the share of Thabit ibn Qays. I have made a kitabah for myself, so I have come to ask for help in paying the kitabah. The Prophet said: Do you wish for something better? She said: What is that? He said: I will pay your kitabah and marry you. She accepted. He paid the kitabah and married her. When people learned that the Prophet married Juwayriyyah, whoever had a captive from Banu Mustaliq freed him and said: These are now the Prophet's in-laws. Text: And likewise included is every blood mahram relative from the wife of his father, and the wife of his son, and the wife of every blood mahram relative from him, because all are in-laws. Translation: Similarly, in this bequest, every blood mahram relative of the testator's father's wife is included, and the testator's son's wife's, and the testator's every blood mahram relative's wife. Explanation: He says that 'sihr' has generality. Just as the blood mahram relatives of one's own wife are included in as-har, similarly the blood mahram relatives of the father's wife, the son's wife, and every blood mahram relative's wife are included. Because all these people are included in as-har. But this is the custom of the Arabs. In our custom, only 'khusar' is meant.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling explanation from Ashraf al-Hidayah. It clarifies the scope of the term 'as-har' (in-laws through wife) in the context of a bequest. The commentator first explains the basic rule: when a man makes a bequest to his as-har, it includes all male blood relatives who are mahram (unmarriageable kin) to his wife, such as her father, brother, uncle, etc. This is based on Arab custom ('urf). The author then provides a historical proof: when the Prophet Muhammad married Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith, the companions freed their captives from Banu Mustaliq because they became the Prophet's as-har. This demonstrates that the term includes all such relatives. The passage then expands the ruling: 'as-har' is not limited to one's own wife's mahrams; it also includes the mahrams of the testator's father's wife, son's wife, and the wife of any mahram relative of the testator. All these are considered as-har because they share a marital connection. However, the commentator notes that this is the Arab custom; in the local custom (likely Indian), 'as-har' is often limited to the wife's father (khusar). The ruling is declaratory: the bequest is valid and must be given to all those included by the wider definition, but fatwa may follow local custom if it is established.

Key Terms
اصہار (as-har): Plural of sihr; in-laws through the wife, including all male mahram relatives of the wife and similar connections through other mahram relatives.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A male blood relative who is so closely related that permanent marriage with the woman is forbidden (e.g., father, brother).
عرف (urf): Custom; the prevalent practice that is considered in legal rulings when no explicit text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is included in a bequest to 'as-har'?
A) The testator's own brother
B) The wife's father
C) The testator's cousin
D) The testator's son

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'as-har' in bequests encompasses all male mahram relatives of the wife and extends to those of the father's wife, son's wife, etc., based on custom and prophetic practice, but local custom may narrow the scope.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Condition for In-Laws' Entitlement to Bequest
Ruling on when in-laws are entitled to a bequest based on marriage status at testator's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for in-laws to be entitled to a bequest and distinguish between revocable and irrevocable divorce in Shariah.

Core Idea
In-laws are entitled to a bequest only if the wife is still married or in revocable divorce iddah at testator's death.

This lesson clarifies when in-laws (as-har) are legally entitled to a bequest (wasiyyah). The ruling hinges on the marital status at the moment of the testator's death. Understanding the distinction between revocable (raj'i) and irrevocable (ba'in) divorce is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is the bequest to in-laws. The condition for entitlement is the existence of the marriage bond at the time of the testator's death.
2
Recall the types of divorce in Hanafi fiqh
Revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) allows the husband to take back his wife during iddah without a new contract, so the marriage continues. Irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) ends the marriage immediately.
3
Apply the condition: marriage exists at death
If the wife is in marriage or iddah of raj'i at death, the in-law relationship persists, so entitlement holds. If in iddah of ba'in, the relationship is severed.
The rationale is that sihr (in-law relationship) depends on the marriage.
4
Conclude the ruling
Thus, in-laws are entitled only when the marriage is still legally intact at the testator's death.

اصہا ر وصیت کے کب تک مستحق ہوتے ہیں
ولومات الموصى والمراة فى نكاحه او فى عدته من طلاق رجعى فالصهر يستحق الوصية وان كانت في عدة من طلاق رجعى فالصهر النكاح وهو شرط عند الموت
ترجمہ اور اگر موضی مرجائے اور عورت اس کے نکاح میں ہو یا اس کی طلاق رجعی کی عدت میں ہو تو صہر وصیت کا مستحق ہوگا اور اگر وہ عمر طلاق بائن کی عدت میں ہو تو صبر وصیت کے مستحق نہ ہوں گے اس لئے کہ صہریت کا بقاء نکاح کے بقاء کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور نکاح موت کے وقت شرط ہے۔ تشریح جب موصی کا انتقال ہو اس وقت عورت اس کے نکاح میں ہو یا اس وقت وہ طلاق رجعی کی عدت میں ہو تو اصہار وصیت کے مستحق ہوں گے کیونکہ نکاح باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے رشتہ صہبریت باقی ہے، اور اگر وہ طلاق بائن کی عدت میں ہو تو اصبار وصیت کے مستحق نہ ہوں گے اس لئے کہ نکاح باقی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے رشتہ صہریت ختم ہو چکا ہے اور استحقاق کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ موت کے وقت نکاح باقی ہو۔
When are in-laws entitled to the bequest? And if the testator dies and the woman is in his marriage or in the iddah of a revocable divorce, then the in-law is entitled to the bequest. And if she is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce, then the in-law is not entitled to the bequest because the in-law relationship continues due to the continuation of marriage, and marriage is a condition at the time of death. Translation: And if the testator dies and the woman is in his marriage or in the iddah of a revocable divorce, then the in-law will be entitled to the bequest. And if she is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce, then the in-laws will not be entitled to the bequest because the existence of the in-law relationship is due to the existence of marriage, and marriage is a condition at the time of death. Explanation: When the testator passes away, at that time if the woman is in his marriage or at that time she is in the iddah of a revocable divorce, then the in-laws will be entitled to the bequest because due to the continuation of marriage, the in-law relationship remains. And if she is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce, then the in-laws will not be entitled to the bequest because due to the non-existence of marriage, the in-law relationship has ended. And for entitlement, it is necessary that at the time of death, marriage exists.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the condition for in-laws to be entitled to a bequest. The key factor is the status of the marriage at the moment of the testator's death. If the wife is still married to the testator (even after his death, this is at the moment of death) or is in the iddah of a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i), then the marriage is considered ongoing, and the in-laws (as-har) are entitled. However, if the wife is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), the marriage is effectively dissolved, so the in-law relationship ceases to exist, and they are not entitled to the bequest. The rationale is that the in-law relationship is contingent upon the existence of the marriage bond. The ruling is straightforward and is based on the principle that the legal relationship (sihr) requires a valid marriage.

Key Terms
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce; the husband can take the wife back during the iddah without a new marriage contract.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage is completely dissolved, and the wife becomes a non-mahram after iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When are in-laws entitled to a bequest from the testator?
A) If the wife is in iddah of any divorce
B) If the wife is in iddah of a revocable divorce or still married
C) If the wife is divorced and iddah is complete
D) If the wife remarries after divorce

Key Takeaway
In-laws are entitled to a bequest only if the testator dies while the wife is still married to him or in the iddah of a revocable divorce.

Definition and Scope of 'Akhtan' in Bequests
Defining who is included in a bequest to 'akhtan' with ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'akhtan' in bequests and identify all individuals included for both male and female testators.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'akhtan' includes all husbands of the testator's female blood mahram relatives.

When a testator uses the term 'akhtan' in a bequest, it is essential to know exactly who is entitled. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition based on Al-Quduri's matn and its commentary, clarifying the scope for both male and female testators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Defined Term
Recognize that 'akhtan' is the plural of 'khatan', referring to male in-laws through marriage.
2
Determine Testator's Gender
The inclusion varies based on whether the testator is male or female. For a male, the bequest goes to husbands of his female mahram relatives and his wife's mahrams. For a female, it goes to the mahram relatives of her husband.
3
List Included Persons for Male Testator
For a male testator, 'akhtan' includes the husband of every woman who is a blood mahram relative of his—e.g., sister, aunt, daughter—and also the mahram relatives of his wife (e.g., father-in-law, brother-in-law).
4
List Included Persons for Female Testator
For a female testator, 'akhtan' includes the blood mahram relatives of her husband (e.g., his father, brothers) because they are also called 'khatan'.
5
Note Custom Consideration
The commentary mentions that in Arab custom the term covered all these, but in the commentator's local custom it was restricted. Nonetheless, the Hanafi ruling follows the inclusive definition based on the literal meaning of the word.
The ruling does not rely on local custom.

اخستان کیلئے وصیت کا حکم و مصداق اختان
ختنا
قال ومن اوصى لاختانه فالو صية لزوج كل ذات رحم محرم منه وكذا محارم الازواج لان الكل يسمى قيل هذا في عرفهم وفى عرفنا لا يتناول الازواج المحارم ويستوى فيه الحر والعبد والاقرب والابعد لان اللفظ يتناول الكل
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے اپنے اختان کے لئے وصیت کی تو اسکے ہر ذی رحم محرم کے شوہر کے لئے وصیت ہوگی اور اسی طرح ازواج کی ذور تم محرم ( بھی داخل ہیں ) کیونکہ سب کو ختن کہتے ہیں کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ اہل عرب کے عرف میں ہے اور ہمارے عرف میں شامل نہ ہو گا۔ مگر محارم کے شوہروں کو اور اس میں آزاد اور غلام اور اقرب اور ابعد سب برابر ہیں اس لئے کہ یہ لفظ سب کو شامل ہے۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے یہ وصیت کی کہ میرے اختان کو اتنا مال دے دینا تو اختان میں ہر اس عورت کا شوہر داخل ہوگا جو موصی کی ڈی رقم محرم ہے جیسے ، بہن ، پھوپھی وغیرہ۔ اور اگر عورت وصیت کرے تو اس کے شوہر کے ذور تم محرم اس میں داخل ہونگے اس لئے کہ ان سب کو خفتن کہتے ہیں ، اس پر
Ruling and meaning of bequest for akhtan (in-laws through husband). Text: He said: And whoever makes a bequest for his akhtan, then the bequest is for the husband of every female blood mahram relative from him, and likewise the mahram relatives of the wives (are included) because all are called khatan. It is said that this is in their custom (Arabs), and in our custom it does not include the husbands of mahram relatives. And the free and slave, the near and far, are all equal because the word includes all. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever makes a bequest for his akhtan, then the bequest is for the husband of every female blood mahram relative from him, and similarly the mahram relatives of the wives (are included) because all are called khatan. It has been said that this is in the custom of the Arabs, and in our custom it will not include the husbands of mahram relatives. But the free and slave, the near and far, are all equal because the word includes all. Explanation: If someone makes a bequest saying 'give such wealth to my akhtan,' then into akhtan will enter the husband of every woman who is a blood mahram relative of the testator, such as sister, aunt, etc. And if a woman makes a bequest, then the blood mahram relatives of her husband will enter into it because all these are called khatan. Upon this...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'akhtan' which refers to in-laws through the husband (the counterpart of as-har). According to Quduri's matn, when a testator (male or female) makes a bequest to his or her akhtan, it includes the husbands of all female mahram relatives of the testator. For example, if a man bequeaths to his akhtan, it goes to the husbands of his sisters, aunts, etc. If a woman bequeaths, it goes to the mahram relatives of her husband (her in-laws). The ruling is based on Arab custom where both sets are called khatan. However, the commentator notes that in their local custom (likely Indian), the term is more restricted and does not include all those husbands. Nevertheless, the legal ruling includes all, and all such individuals are equal in entitlement regardless of being free or slave, near or distant relative. The passage emphasizes the literal meaning of the word and its application in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اختان (akhtan): Plural of khatan; in-laws through the husband, i.e., the husbands of female mahram relatives of the testator, and the mahram relatives of the testator's spouse.
ختن (khatan): A male in-law through marriage, especially the husband of a daughter or sister.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a bequest to 'akhtan' includes all of the following EXCEPT:
A) The husband of the testator's sister
B) The husband of the testator's maternal aunt
C) The testator's own wife
D) The mahram relatives of the testator's wife (if testator is male)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'akhtan' broadly to include all husbands of the testator's female blood mahram relatives and the mahram relatives of the testator's spouse, ensuring comprehensive coverage in bequests.

Condition for In-Laws to Receive a Bequest
States ruling and condition for as-har to inherit will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for an in-law (as-har) to be entitled to a bequest under Hanafi law and apply it to scenarios involving revocable and irrevocable divorce.

Core Idea
An in-law's entitlement to a will depends on the marriage being intact at the testator's death.

This lesson examines a specific condition for the validity of a bequest to in-laws (as-har) in Hanafi law. The ruling hinges on the status of the marriage at the moment of the testator's death. Understanding this condition not only clarifies the law of wills but also illustrates how the continuity of a legal relationship affects inheritance rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The subject is the as-har (in-law) and the ruling is whether they are entitled to the will. The passage states that they are entitled if a certain condition is met.
The passage is from al-Quduri's matn with commentary.
2
Determine the condition
The condition is that the testator's wife must be in a current marriage or in the iddah of a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) at the time of death. This preserves the in-law relationship.
Revocable divorce iddah is considered continuing marriage in Hanafi law.
3
Distinguish the excluded scenario
If the wife is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in), the in-law is not entitled because the marriage is completely dissolved at that point.
Irrevocable divorce severs the marriage relationship entirely.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that the in-law relationship (sihriyyah) remains only as long as the marriage continues, and marriage is a condition at the moment of death.
This shows that legal relationships are evaluated at the critical moment of death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولومات الموصى والمراة فى نكاحه او فى عدته من طلاق رجعى فالصهر يستحق الوصية وان كانت في عدة من طلاق بائن فلا يستحق لان الصهرية تبقى ببقاء النكاح والنكاح شرط عند الموت
And if the testator dies and the woman is in his marriage or in the iddah of a revocable divorce, then the in-law is entitled to the will. And if she is in the iddah of an irrevocable divorce, then he is not entitled, because the in-law relationship remains with the continuation of marriage, and marriage is a condition at the time of death.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn, elaborated by the commentator. It specifies the condition for a person designated as 'as-har' (in-law) to be eligible for a bequest (wasiyyah). The testator's death is the moment of vesting. If at that moment the connecting marriage is still intact (either current marriage or revocable divorce iddah where the marriage is considered continuing), the in-law qualifies. However, if the iddah is irrevocable (bain), the marriage is dissolved retroactively, and the in-law relationship ceases, so they do not qualify. The rationale is that the in-law relationship depends on the existence of the marriage, and the marriage must be present at death. The commentator explains that the condition is the continuation of the marriage at the time of death.

Key Terms
صهر (sihr (pl. as-har)): In this passage, sihr means any in-law relative by marriage to the testator, specifically through the wife.
طلاق رجعي (talaq raj'i): Revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife during the waiting period without a new contract; marriage is considered continuing.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that severs the marriage immediately; the wife is no longer lawful for the husband until a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The in-laws are still entitled to the will because the iddah period is ongoing.
B) The in-laws are not entitled because the marriage was already dissolved at death.
C) The in-laws are entitled only if the testator's wife was pregnant.
D) The in-laws are entitled regardless because the will was made before the divorce.

Key Takeaway
The entitlement of an in-law to a bequest depends on the marriage being intact at the testator's death; revocable divorce iddah preserves the relationship, irrevocable divorce does not.

Defining Akhtan in Wills: Scope and Custom Shift
Definition of akhtan in a will with custom shift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of akhtan in a will and distinguish the earlier custom from the later restricted custom.

Core Idea
Akhtan in a will includes husbands of all mahram women, but later custom restricts it to husbands of the testator's own mahram women.

When someone makes a will for their 'akhtan,' who actually receives the bequest? The answer depends on how the term is defined by custom. This passage from Al-Quduri gives the broad definition based on early Arab custom, then notes a shift in later Hanafi practice. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly executing wills and avoiding invalid bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text
Locate the passage from Al-Quduri: 'And whoever makes a will for his akhtan, then the will is for the husband of every woman who is a mahram relative of him.' This is our legal unit.
2
Analyze the term 'akhtan'
Break down the definition: 'khatan' (plural akhtan) means a male relative by marriage. The text defines it specifically as the husband of a mahram woman (blood relative whom marriage is permanently prohibited).
Mahram here means blood mahram, e.g., sister, daughter, aunt.
3
Note the earlier custom
The phrase 'because all are called akhtan' indicates that in the earlier Arab custom (or Kufan custom), the term also included the mahram of the husband (i.e., when a woman wills, her akhtan includes her husband's mahram relatives).
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
4
Understand the later custom shift
The text says 'in our custom it does not include the husbands of mahram' – meaning later Hanafi scholars restricted the term to only the husbands of the testator's own mahram women, excluding the mahram of the husband.
This becomes the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the ruling equally
The ruling applies equally to free and slave, near and distant relatives, because the word 'akhtan' includes all such husbands regardless of status or distance.
No differentiation based on social status or degree of relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اوصى لاختهانه فالوصية لزوج كل ذات رحم محرم منه وكذا محارم الازواج لان الكل يسمى قيل هذا في عرفهم وفى عرفنا لا يتناول الازواج المحارم ويستوى فيه الحر والعبد والاقرب والابعد لان اللفظ يتناول الكل
He said: And whoever makes a will for his akhtan, then the will is for the husband of every woman who is a mahram relative of him, and likewise the mahram of the husbands. Because all are called akhtan. It was said: This is in their custom, and in our custom it does not include the husbands of mahram. And in this, the free and the slave, the near and the far are equal because the word includes all.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'akhtan' (plural of khatan). According to al-Quduri, whoever makes a will for his akhtan means he bequeaths to the husbands of every woman who is a mahram relative to him (like sister, aunt, etc.). Similarly, if a woman bequeaths to her akhtan, it includes the mahram relatives of her husband. The commentator notes that this definition is based on the custom of the Arabs (or Kufans). In the common custom (urf) of later Hanafi scholars, 'akhtan' refers specifically to the husbands of mahram women, not the wider circle. The ruling applies equally to free and slave, near and distant relatives, because the word includes all such husbands.

Key Terms
ختن (khatan (pl. akhtan)): In the text, khatan means a male relative by marriage, specifically the husband of a woman who is a mahram to the testator. In common usage, it often means son-in-law or brother-in-law.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muharram): A blood relative whom one is permanently prohibited to marry, e.g., mother, sister, daughter, aunt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband of his sister
B) The brother of his wife (his wife's brother)
C) The father of his wife (his father-in-law)
D) The son of his brother (his nephew)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wills, the term 'akhtan' is defined by custom; the later mufta bihi restricts it to husbands of the testator's own mahram women, excluding the husband's mahram relatives.
